einer 2/4

|


narrative, perhaps by some action or as an image scooped
out of the sand but slowly filled by the lapping waters. The
important thing here is to make the characters realize they
have a role to play in the upcoming drama.

Rejoining the Pack: A Galliard character may hear the
voice of her tribe's totem calling out in song in the woods.
(an indication that she should speak of what she has seen
here). Gaia has granted the pack access to information
which grows greatly more valuable when disseminated to
other Garou, even though it may also have personal rel-
evance to the members of the pack.

The Lesson of the Trickster
(Ragabash)

The trickster is the questioner of stasis, the impolitic
observer who brings change into the world. She is the
antihero, far more capricious than the hero. The hero
almost always works for the good of his group, or at least
does not actively work to undermine it. Although the
trickster also usually works for the good of the group, her
intentions and concerns are far different.

In tales of the trickster, any hypocrisy or pretense is
revealed to the world. Establishment and order are often
thrown on their heads, although in the end the trickster
almost invariably aids those she has so discomfited. It is the
trickster's role to force issues when adam of convention and
tradition blocks the necessary flow of ideas and energy that
make up the rhythmic cycles of the universe. In this role as
connector, the trickster straddles the divide between worlds
better than any other type of character. Prometheus was the
trickster who stole fire from the gods and gave it to man.
Tricksters are masters of transformation.

Storytellers can create trickster tales in which the play-
ers' Garou perform the role of the trickster, or in which they
are confronted by the trickster in the form of another
Garou, the Coyote-spirit, a Bastet or any of a host of
creatures. However, the following example places the play-
ers' Garou in the roles of both the trickster and the tricked.

Call of the Wyld: A pack of Garou discover an unusual
fetish (possibly towards the end of another story). The
fetish is a Coyote mask, which when placed over the head
allows the wearer to sense the age-old tracks of Coyote
which crisscross Gaia's surface. Even after the mask is
removed, the werewolf can still see the slightly glowing
tracks of Coyote leading off into the distance. The Garou
has an increasingly difficult time concentrating until he
follows the path left by Coyote. Finally, the Garou and his
pack set off to follow Coyote's tracks.

Into the Dark: The tangled path of Coyote leads the
Garou to the edge of a large city. In this instance, it is the
border between the wilderness and the city that represents
the divide between the known and the unknown world. By
stepping into the mechanized world of the humans, the
Garou are stepping into an alien reality.

Guardian at the Gate: Following the erratic path into
the heart of the city, the Garou find themselves on an
elevator in a skyscraper. The elevator jams between floors
on the way up, and the Garou can hear a disquieting
creaking as some techno-spirits chew away at the cables.

After a quick scramble, the Garou are able to free
themselves from the elevator before it plunges down the
shaft. After all, they are following the path of the trickster,
and the trickster is known for her natural luck. The
werewolves find themselves high within the skyscraper,
looking out on a panorama of the city below. Beside them
isadoor with the words "Glass Walker Computers." Coyote's
tracks lead behind the door.

The Transfiguration: In the case of the trickster's myth,
the transfiguration is actually the point at which the
trickster figure pulls off his trick; that is, he manages to
successfully steal something of true importance from a
powerful group (then gives it into the hands of a less
powerful group), or exposes some hypocrisy or pretense.

Managing to spring the lock, the curious Garou slip
inside the offices of their fellow Garou. Quickly searching
the premises, the Garou find several reports regarding the
recent successes of the Glass Walkers in developing de-
structive techno-spirits that they could send to sabotage
their competitors' electronic systems. Incidentally, these
spirits would also give the Glass Walkers an insurmount-
able advantage over all the other tribes — proving the
Glass Walker's innate superiority. Grinning, the werewolves
lure the destructive techno-spirits from the elevator shaft
into the computer room, where there is ever so much more
to destroy...

The return journey can be easy or difficult depending on
the desires of the Storyteller and the actions of the players.
What is important in the tale of the trickster is that the
flaws of some stale hierarchy or other representative of
authority are exposed, or that the trickster steals and
disseminates some hoarded kernel of knowledge. This sort
of behavior at first seems merely cruel, but in actuality the
trickster serves as a catalyst for needed change.

The Moon Queen and the Sacrificial
King (Philodox)

The myth of the ever-living goddess figure and the
sacrificial king is one of the oldest myths representing the
turning of the seasons and the cycle of life, death and
rebirth. Unlike the tale of the trickster, in which authority
is constantly questioned or mocked, the story of the sacri-
ficial king is one of duty to a higher cause. In some senses
it is very similar to the Hero's Journey, save that the effect
of the Sacrificial King's transformation does not occur
within the king, the hero figure, but without in the world
around him.

The story of the Moon Queen and the Sacrificial King is
a story of the necessity for both stasis and change. The
Moon Queen is ever-present, traveling down through the

Chapter One: Storytelling 25

_— ——

nie iocinaay /


|

ages. The Sacrificial King burns brightly, his energy warming her
face for a brief instant before he sacrifices his life-energy for the
Queen, and thus the world, to continue. She is ever-living and he
is ever-dying, and in them is the dance of eternity, the cycle of life-
death-rebirth.

Storytellers can create these tales of duty and balance in a
variety of ways. In these tales the players' Garou will sometimes
take the role of facilitators, aiding another in a dangerous but
necessary task that will aid a large group of Garou. More often,
however, the players' Garou take the sacrificial role. [tisimportant
forStorytellerstounderstand, thatthe Garoudonot, byanymeans,
need to die in this journey, but they must be willing to die should
it prove necessary for the greater good. First though, the Garou
must prove themselves worthy of this type of sacrifice. This can
only be done by facing a variety of challenges and choosing the
wisest course of action.

The following example places the players' Garou in the role of
the Sacrificial King.

Call of the Wyld: The sept's caem is dying. Over the course of
‘one season the once-vital source of Gaia's energies has faded
alarmingly. The Theurges estimate that within another season the
caern willbenomore. After much searching, the elders determine
thatthecaemn'senergiesare somehow being diverted into the Dark
Umbra of the Underworld. It is rare for any Garou to attempt a
joumey into the realms of the dead, and once there the chance of
retuming is slim. However, this unjust assault on Gaia must be
halted. The characters volunteer to go on the mission.

Into the Dark: The elders give the Garou talismans that will
enable them to follow the caemn's dwindling energies through the
Umbra and into the Dark Umbra. Grimly stepping sideways, the
pack follows the gleaming trail revealed by the talismans.

Guardian at the Gate: The Garou reach a piece of dark, rusted
grating in the forest floor of the Umbra. Opening it, they slip
downwards. Once below, the Garou are surrounded in a dense,
greasy fog. Voices call out to the pack for help, and the werewolves
feel occasional tugs on their sodden fur. Soon they are lost. The
voices ask questions, and if the Garou answer honestly about why
they have entered the realm of the dead, the tuggings will become
stronger, and lead the pack out of the fog. If the Garou are vicious
or rude, they will have to fight the spirits at the gate.

The Transfiguration: After several more challenges, the
Garou finally discover to where the caem's energies are being
drained. It isa terrible, black hole that seems to bleed directly into
nothingness. The caem's energies have been diverted into this
awful void. A lone, mournful figure bearing a sword stands guard
beside the hole. The figure asks the living Garou what their
businessisin the world of thedead. Ifthe characters tell him, he will
laugh hollowly and remark upon their unfortunate bravery —
saying they will undoubtedly come to accept life among the dead
in time, unless one of them enters the void to replace the energies
from the cae. However, whatever creature steps into the void
becomesone with Oblivion—their soul destroyed forall eternity.
Ifa Garou volunteers to do this, the figure will stop her at the last
second and grant the release of the energies, remarking on the
strength ofher convictions. If the Garou fight, it will bea horrible,

ia maim i)

evenly matched battle. Ifthe Garou gain the caern'senergies, then
they may head back, bringing the caem's vitality with them.

Rejoining the Pack: The Garou may well face other challenges
on the long way back to the living lands. At least one of the Garou
must retum the caem's energies to the sept, else any successes they
have had in the realm of the dead are meaningless. It is the
continuation of Gaia's energies embodied in the caern and their
importance to the Garou that is truly important.

The World Eater (Theurge)

Everybody's got a hunger

No matter where they are

Everybody clings to their own fear

Everybody hides some scar

— Melissa Etheridge, "Precious Pain"

The World Eater is the myth of the destroyer, in particular
the destroyer who swallows her young. It is the myth of the
destruction that must precede all creation and is reflected in
stories of Kali, Cronus or Kalma. The World Eater is that
aspect of creation associated with death in the triat of life-
death-rebirth. In the World of Darkness this part of the
creation cycle is represented by the Wyrm and its increasing
onslaught upon Gaia, the Earth Mother.

It is imperative in the world of myth to look into the face of
the World Destroyer, the face of death, lest the terror of this
great force overcome you and leave you passive when action
is required. It is the constant fear of the Garou that the Wyrm.
will win and swallow up the world at the time of the Apoca-
lypse.

In the part of the life cycle controlled by the World Eater,
people may become trapped within the power of the De-
stroyer, find themselves unable to pass through to the next
portion of the cycle. This greediness and the corresponding
fear are echoed in the Wyrm, the force that is no longer
content to remain in balance with the other members of the
Triat, the Weaver and the Wyld.

The Storyteller can use fear of the devourer Wyrm, the
Destroyer aspect of Gaia (who is actually formed from all
aspects of the Triat), to create stories based on the coming
Apocalypse. When creating such stories, Storytellers may
wish to emphasize the womb/tomb symbolism that is particu-
larly prevalent in the vast majority of World Devourer myths.
The World Eater is powerful, and what is more powerful than
the birthplace of creation, which may also be the arbiter of
death?

The following is an example of how the symbolic World
Eater images can be brought into one of the many Apocalyptic
stories so common in Werewolf. It is actually a variation on
the Hero's Journey (as are so many tales), but it is one that
emphasizes the dark world myths.

Call of the Wyld: In tales of the World Eater, the protago-
nists rarely choose to walk the path of the adventurer. Instead,
the path is almost always initially forced upon them by some
minions of the powerful defiler Wyrm-as-mother.


Traveling in unfamiliar territory, the pack of Garou are
overwhelmed by a pack of female Black Spiral Dancers.
During the fight, the Garou are pushed slowly backwards until
the wet, sandy ground they are standing upon gives way and
they go plunging and tumbling helplessly down a steep slope.

Into the Dark: As with the initial summons to the adven-
ture, the protagonists are often forced into the magical world
where the World Eater holds greater sway. It is the realm of
death, a dark place almost always represented by a journey
through a small, dark opening. It is the dark forest or en-
chanted pool of fairy tales, the vagina dentata, or "toothed
vagina" that Freud, the Yanamamo, and others brought up in
patriarchal societies dread so much. It is a dark, powerful,
primal arena of both life and death.

Atthe bottom of their rough descent the Garou fall through
a jagged, narrow opening in the earth. The opening is lined
with rough rocks, which cut several of the Garou as the
tumble. For seconds they watch as the opening seems to close
in above them, and then there is pain and unconsciousness.

Guardian at the Gate: The Guardian in World Eaterstories
functions much the same as it does in other mythic cycle
stories. However, if possible, the Guardian should be one
which truly evokes primal fears in the Garou and through
them, their players.

Picking themselves up from the soft sand, the Garou begin
toslowly make their way through the echoing darkness. Lifting
their noses to scent for any sign of an enemy, they note the
pungent aroma of gas just as sparks flicker in the darknes
Li
verely burned by the gouts of flame that suddenly leap upwards

ping backwards, the werewolves barely avoid being se-

from fissures in the ground. After watching the shifting,
sputtering licks of flame for some time, the Garou begin to
discern an odd pattern to the dance of the flames. After much
concentration, they leap at just the appointed second, sailing
through the darkness of the chamber to the even greater
darkness beyond

The Transfiguration: In World Eater myths the transfigu-
ration is always one in which true world-death is faced,
acknowledged and
ing firm in the face of such horror can the protagonists prove
once again that the world is not yet ready to be consumed and

asted by the protagonists. Only by stand-

destroyed. Whether they personally succeed or fail is immate-
rial. What does matter is that they do not run from the face of
the Destroyer, which is really the dark aspect of their mother
Gaia.

After picking their way along a damp, spiraling path that
seemed to wind down into the very center of the earth, the
Garou finally emerge into a dully lit chamber. The chamber
smells strongly of a rich, fetid loam, a combination both
nauseating and sickening to the Garou. Whining softly, the
werewolves approach the far side of the chamber. As they
reach the center, the sandy floor once more begins to give way,
but this time long, tooth-encrusted tendrils crowned with the
snarling heads of Black Spirals burst out from all around them.
Fighting despite the almost overwhelming urge to run or to

ne A Ae ee

curl up in a ball and just let it finish, the Garou somehow
triumph over their writhing, gnashing enemies.

The Journey Home: This part of the World Eater myth is
also much like the other stories. Once again, however, the
emphasis is usually placed on climbing, especially in a clock-
wise spiral, out of the darkness and back to the surface world.
This journey is the journey back towards light from out of the
realms of death itself. It is the journey of Orpheus, and it is
never wise to pause for long or look back, lest the protagonists
be yet overcome by the forces of the Destroyer.

Hurrying up and over the endless rocks and sand, the Garou

finally spot the tiniest flicker of light. Digging furiously, they
finally enlarge the light hole enough for even the largest of the
pack to make his

y out of the dead realm.

Rejoining the Pack: At this point the Garou are resur-
rected through their own efforts and brought back to the world
of the living. They have faced the death-in-life Wyrm and
have returned to the bright surface world, with its relatively

an be made
adding trials, tests and

familiar terrors. This in itself is a great success. It
even more profound, however, by

helpers that have personal meaning to the players' Garou.
Every character has personal fears and doubts, and at least
some aspect of their journey to the Destroyer's underworld
should reflect one or two such weaknesses. This gives the
opportunity for the Garou to face their unconscious, their

Jungian Shadow, and to overcome it, a truly heroic task.

(Daring to Improvise
By Andrew Greenberg

Well, the story is finally ready to go. You've statted out
Gorlansen, the thousai nf itor of the Wyrm, to
the last Background. nappe he blasted Antartic
mountains whe i le Mwill take place.
You've come upl With : ings for Makrie, the
kidnapped Sha Ht as the Wyrm
tries to sacrifi Storyteller's most
important skill
The ability
preparations.

gness to chuck all these careful

to improvise as the pl#

she never could have expectedehat do you do when the
characters hire a mage to teleport Gorlansen into orbit?
How about if they try to cut a deal with the thousand-
tongued beastie instead of fighting it? For all we know, they
might manage to force all the Garou and spirits in the world
to do their work for them.

Thus, no matter how much preparation you do, there is
no way youcan be ready for the infinite number of wrenches
players can throw into the works. Now you're shaking.
You've witnessed both the biggest advantage and biggest
disadvantage to the Storyteller System — it's so wide open
that literally anything can happen. There are some things
humanity was not meant to see.

Afraid of improvising? There are some basic tools which
can make this terrifying process immensely easier.

First of all, keep these basic rules of Storytelling in mind:

1. A game is useless unless both the players and Story-
teller enjoy it.

2. The players' characters are the center of the story.

3. No matter how interesting a Storyteller makes her
characters, they should not overshadow the players' char-
acters.

4. Anything the players do will backfire on them.
(Whoops! Thar's the rule for Vampire. How'd that sneak in
here?).

Real Rule 4. Anything you do in a game can be ex-
plained later (when you've had time to come up with the
explanation).

(By the way, like all rules, the Rules for Storytelling were
made to be broken.)

Whenever things start to go askew, and the Storyteller
has no idea where to turn next, she can think of these and
center the next scenes on them. So how do you keep the
players the center of things when they seem intent on
relegating their characters to a game-life of mediocrity?
The easiest way is to say that a character or the pack is
destined for greatness, that people know that and push
them on. As in real life, however, this strategy is destined
to backfire. The harder the characters are pushed, the more


the players will rebel, until all your hard earned plans are
ruined.

On the other hand, having the player characters become
heroes by accident always seems to work so much better.
When the characters go on their Rite of Passage and find
some tangent path you never thought of, run with it and
beef up the difficulty. Later the elders can apologize and say,
"We have no idea why those 10 mauve fomori were so
interested in you." Now the characters have their second
story (finding out why the Order of Mauve Fomori are
hunting them) and the Storyteller has several more sessions
before she has to commit to a reason for the situation.

Now, the problem is coming up with ideas on the spur of
the moment. Here are some more tools — hope you have a
good place to store them.

1. Make up a new character for the players' characters to
meet or bring back an old one. These characters can be used
to get the story back on track, feed the players interesting
information, start a new story line or just entertain the
players while you think of a more substantial direction in
which to send the story.

2. Think in terms of conspiracies. If things are going off
track, maybe there is a reason beyond the characters' own
actions, Maybe a vampire has secretly Dominated one of
the characters into trying to lead the pack away from the
story you have prepared. Maybe a Theurge is using her
powerful spirits to send the characters on a more important
task. No matter what the characters do, somebody will
benefit from it, and maybe that somebody had a role in the

change. Thinking along these lines can give you all sorts of
ideas as to what may be at the end of the characters'
sidetrack.

3. Use humor to relax things while you come up with a
plan. I know one Storyteller (with whom I no longer play)
who whines like mad when players make light of any aspect
of the game — especially when they're forcing him to put
aside his carefully crafted scenario with their own plans and
schemes. On the other side of the coin, some Storytellers
use humor, both in and outside of the game, to relax things
while they try and figure out what to do next.

4. Listen to your players. This one tool cannot be used
too often. It's not that difficult to determine what your
players want. If they seem to seek out certain characters you
had not planned to use in that story, then they must like
them, and you might want to find a way to use them. On the
other hand, one of the most important things to listen for
is silence from one or more players. If you've been running
stories of political intrigue as the Shadow Lords and Silver
Fang battle for control of the sept, give the Get of Fenris a
toxic critter to sink his Klaive into. If the characters have
been fighting Pentex First Teams in the Amazon, let the
Theurge spend some time in the Umbra communing with
the spirits.

5. Up the Drama! When in doubt, make things more
exciting. Especially with Werewolf, if you have your choice
of two paths, opt for the one that is the more active.
Werewolves are not passive beings, and you can use this to
your benefit when you start flying by the seat of your pants

Chapter One: Storytelling 29

The Garou Yation

Greetings, my cubs. Don't be surprised, I sniffed your
coming long before you arrived. Welcome to my little hole in the
Umbra. Allow your Auntie Smollet to bind ‘your wounds in
partial reward for deciphering my riddles. In your very first
Concolation you, of all packs, chewed through the bony gristle
of my clues to discover the sweet marrow at the center of my
confounding tale. And you shall receive your desserts. I shall
keep the promise laid out in the skin of my riddle. I shall tell you
the true nature of the Garou Nation

You have heard the great speeches, sung the great songs and
danced the tributes to the might of the Garou Nation. The Litany
calls Garou Nation a mighty, unified pack. The Litany tells you
that we are a single, being — the mighty Wolf of Wolves. But
the dog has worms.

There was a time —so long ago — there was a time now lost
to dust, there was a time in ages past when all our hearts struck
with one beat. There was a time there was a nation of Garou,
and we were strong, our will was one, our souls called to others
and the others answered. There was a time, but the time is
passed. Let the others boast of the strength of the pack, the power
of the sept, the might of our leaders. I will not. Lam Ragabash,
packless, youngest of the Old Ones, and I will tell you what
others will not.

Chapter Two: Culture

f/POEL  T  Y imeem ae //

We are not one people. We are a pack of tired, frightened
mongrels. Our mighty nation struggles to lift its wounded head
from its sickbed and offer up a threatening howl to the serpent
that coils tighter and tighter around our nest. And yet our
wounds come not from the snake. The very finest and most
glorious battles the mighty Garou fight are against each other.

We mock the humans for carrying old hatreds from old wars
into new generations. We laugh that in the United States they
cannot forget their Civil War one hundred years after the final
shots. We scorn their Balkan conflicts that spill over from the
Middle Ages. But laughter chokes in Garou throats when I
mention the divided heart of the Garou Nation — rent thou-
sands of years ago after the end of the Impergium. On that day
a barrier arose in the heart of the Garou Nation, and we have
never acted fully in concert again

To this day great Garou grumble that we should never have
stopped the Impergium, never have let the humans breed out of
control. These Garou join the fight only halfheartedly , and they
argue when they need to act. It would be impolitic to tell you their
names, cubs. Ando I gleefully name them: Red Talons and Get
of Fenris.

|


|

The Garou Nation divided again with the coming of the
European Garou to the New World. The native tribes did not
accept the help of the Old-World tribes, deemed them as
tainted and as Wyrm-corrupt as the invading humans who
blighted the Pure Land. Many still feel thus, and I name
them: Uktena and Wendigo. The Uktena still seethe at the
patronage of the stronger, Old-World tribes, and they now
traffic in Wyrm lore to gain the power to shake the Garou
Nation to the core. And the Wendigo have all but withdrawn
from us. As they watch the native humans fade away, they
fear they are fated to die as were the Croatan.

Other tribes seethe with barely concealed secret anger over
past slights, and eagerly await a chance to avenge themselves
The Black Furies and the Bone Gnawers bristle over old
wounds, sometimes with good cause. And this too divides our
nation.

Other tribes have withdrawn from our fractured nation,
paying obeisance as required by the laws, and nothing more.
The Stargazers turn inward and keep their own counsel. The
Silent Striders look outward, away from the messy squabbles
of their snarling, extended family. The Fianna are torn from
within, rent along human political lines, distracted by mortal
concerns.

The Glass Walkers and the Shadow Lords see a leadership
vacuum and close for the kill, seeking to usurp leadership in
a thousand less-than-covert maneuvers. One seeks to move
the Garou Nation forward, the other seeks to return us to
earlier glories.

And where is the head of our nation in the midst of the
greatest Wyrm crisis? In our rehearsal for retirement, my
people, the Silver Fangs, cling to every finger of power and
hoard every resource rather than leading the body against the
Wyrm.

We of Garou Nation are no longer characterized by our
unity, but by our divisions. I tell you cubs of this not to push
you into the warm, welcoming jaws of Harano, but to enliven
you. In deciphering my riddle you have shown yourself to be
gifted with great insight by the great spirits. I offer you a
challenge: What can you do every day to forge a nation out
of squabbling cubs in the bodies of great grays? This concolation
is to induct you into the nation, but I tell you, O favored of
the Phoenix, that you ARE the nation. What becomes of you
is what will become of us. It is time you looked beyond the
petty plans of your pack, the schemes of sept and the demands
of tribe. You have a greater home now. And that is all your
kin. You are your brothers' keepers. Aye, and your sisters'
too. It is time that you and your family learned to act your
spiritual age.

— Auntie Smollet, Silver Fang Ragabash

Werewolf Storytellers Handbook

Garou Yation Jn Crisis

We have differed and quarreled in the past;
but now one bond unites us all —
to wage war until victory is won,
and never surrender ourselves to servitude and shame,
whatever the cost and agony may be..
Upon all of whom a long night of barbarism will descend
unbroken even by a star of hope,
unless we conquer, as conquer we must;
as conquer we shall.
— Winston Churchill, BBC radio, 1940

The mighty Garou Nation has stood the test of time, Triat
and technology, and it still stands tall. Though two tribes have
died and another has been corrupted, thirteen live on, and
have forged hard-won bonds of loyalty and honor. Despite
deep divisions and outright hostility within and among tribes,
the Garou have kept their community togetherand continued
to coordinate their actions. They try to maintain a veneer of
civility on the surface that masks the bitter enmity that roils in
their bellies. But at the very depths of the Garou community,
below the feigned politeness, below the brooding animosity,
there lies a very real respect. When all masks are peeled away,
the Garou have a unique admiration for one another. The
Garou all spring from a tradition of reverence for life, and at
their heart they stand with others who strive to defend Gaia.
This sets them apart from supernatural creatures such as the
undead vampires, who come from a tradition of death and
damnation. At the core of the vampire community, there is
precious little reverence for other vampires — just for survival.

Much of the internal strife among Garou is based on their
pack mentality, in which the greater intimidate the lesser and
the lesser threaten to topple the greater. Nonetheless, the
greater and the lesser are required to maintain an inborn
respect for the other.

In order to function, the Garou Nation must resolve
differences, work out policy, punish lawbreakers and conduct
a war against an implacable foe. In order to survive in the
dangerous new world, they often must compromise, and
Garou are terrible at compromise. Because many of them want
their own all or nothing solutions, they are often torn in many
directions.

The Challenge of a Common
Solution

Some Garou believe that the greatest challenge facing
them is finding and harnessing enough spiritual and physical
resources to triumph in the war against the Wyrm, the battle
against the Weaver and the struggle with humankind.

But they are wrong. The greatest challenge comes not from
without, but from within the nation of werewolves.

The Garou arguably have sufficient physical resources and
connections to higher spiritual powers to complete their


difficult mission against the Wyrm. But their energy and
power is constantly diffused by the crushing internecine
strife that has torn the werewolf community apart for
thousands of years. The greatest challenge now before the
tribes is the same one they faced at the end of the Impergium.
It is the vital, pressing need to resolve differences within
the Garou Nation and to put those differences aside in
order for the tribes to focus their energy and resources on
their highest purpose: championing Gaia. A\ll tribes agree
on this, but they disagree profoundly on how to get there.
This has created political chasms in Garou society along
many fault lines.

An Infusion of Politics:
Sources of Dissension

There are many ways to fit Garou politics into your
game, especially in an ongoing campaign when each player
hasa chance for some one-on-one time with the Storyteller
to further the personal aspirations and explore the private
fears of each character. Private time, even if it's no more
than fifteen minutes in every other game session, will go a
long way toward redirecting the focus of the game. If you
have the enviable luxury of entire gaming sessions with
each player singly, you can doa lot to establish ties to tribe,
Totem and Garou Nation.

Chapter Two: Culture 33

One-on-one gaming time can change the pack from
acting as a single-minded entity to behaving as a more
realistic set of individuals with competing and some-
times clashing interests. This is not an open invitation
for the Storyteller to spike all attempts at pack cohesion
with contrived divisions at every turn, but rather an
opportunity to spice up the game with some friction and
natural divisions. It's a chance for the players to get a
sense of their characters as really inhabiting a world with
a rich history: a world where the Garou are born into
conflicts they did not create, and in which they are
expected to carry on the hopes, fears and prejudices of
their ancestors. This will give the pack a chance to

explore some hot issues within the Garou nation and
experience the thrill of not just overcoming evil Wyrm
creatures, but overcoming their own fears and precon-
ceived notions. Garou character get to feel the greater
triumph over the inner being instead of the lesser tri-
umph over the outer world. The pack will have an
opportunity to face the unique challenge of overcoming
differences to find a common solution, which is the true
essence of politics.

Many Storytellers are hesitant to run games which
feature high-level politics, but incorporating these is-
sues is easier than it seems. This section describes a series
of political tensions in the Garou Nation, and gives you
several ways to entangle players in them.

Tribal Politics

The simplest and clearest way to generate political
friction is at the tribal level. All Garou must attend some
tribal moots where their loyalty and zeal for tribal goals
may be tested. These moots are a chance for each pack
member to experience himself as a part of a greater
spiritual group. If your players have been thinking of
their characters as being strongly identified with their
pack alone, this is a chance to give them another point

of view. The character could be caught in a conflict
between two feuding camps in his own tribe. Not taking
sides could be seen as cowardice and could be worse than
taking the losing side.

Generational Warfare

The politics of age weigh heavily on the Garou Nation
and always have. Older wolves have hurt the cause by

trying to impose solutions from an earlier time onto
newer problems. They sometimes try to preserve hard-
won victories long after the mourning has stopped, even
to the point of avoiding new challenges in order to fight
old battles. They sometimes resist necessary changes
even when the need for a new approach is clear. For
example, an Uktena elder who spent a great deal of time
resisting the incursions of the U.S. government into
native lands may carry his vendetta into the modern era,
and resist Uktena Kinfolk's opportunities to attain high
positions in local and state governments. During the


seige at Wounded Knee, the government was an impla-
cable foe, and all cooperation was capitulation. Now the
tide has turned, and the government is more receptive to
native grievances. When elders can't see this, they lose the
ability to form crucial alliances with the human world.
Uktena player characters could be caught in the middle of
this struggle and forced to take sides. The old bull may
count on them to help block the move, and the young
Kinfolk may seek their cooperation in breaching the halls
of government from within. The pack may vote their
conscience, or they may be compelled to side with one
group based on old favors.

Young, aggressive Garou also cause problems for the
tribe. They often carry their exuberance and new-found
hatred of the Wyrm to dangerous and suicidal extremes.
They need to be tempered by the elders to keep them from
jeopardizing missions or putting caerns at risk. If the players
are running young Garou, they may be likely to sympathize
with their younger, more aggressive cousins, and face seri-
ous conflicts when they realize that the youths are making
a ruinous mistake.

Generational conflicts are not alwaysas simple as age. As
aging leaders decline, they try to recruit young followers
who are in alignment with their way of thinking. These
youths may be more fanatical than the elders, since they
hold the position without an understanding of the forces
that shaped it.

The Battle of the Sexes

The Garou have faced gender conflicts at least as long as
have humans. Women have often been blocked from
positions of power, and the birth of a metis is far more likely
to damage the reputation and reduce the power of the
female who bears the child than the male who sows it.
These inequities have generated a great deal of animosity in
the Garou Nation and resulted in the creation of the Black

Furies tribe. The males who resist the accession of female

leaders are not organized and do not overtly stress their
beliefs. Their attitude is difficult to support, since they have
direct evidence that God is a woman. Still, they have
created elaborate rationalizations, such as the theory that
aia prefers that males lead as Her human consorts on
earth, and females who become leaders are usurpers trying
to compete with Her. These males tend to favor packs run
by males, and are uncooperative with packs run by females.

Some females, in large part Black Furies, favor packs led by
females, and do not trust male-led groups.

Old Ways and the Modern

Many Garou hate the ascension of Weaver forces in the
Garou Nation. They see the rise of the Glass Walker tribe
as either an aberration or an abomination. Garou with this
philosophy have tried to organize an antitech group several
times over the last few centuries, but they have never been


able to agree on a charter. Nevertheless, the antitechnol-
ogy faction resists attempts to synthesize magic and
technology and to bring modern ideas into the Garou
Nation. Individual followers of the Old Ways could cause
trouble with Glass Walker characters, or try to sow dissent
in a pack by trying to sway members to the Old Ways.

Warmongers and Peacemakers

The Children of Gaia have found kindred spirits in many
tribes, even in the unlikeliest places. Even some Get of
Fenris and Wendigo have acknowledged during moots that
the Unicorn tribe makes sense when they call for intertribal
unity. Others have been swayed by the words of the Chil-
dren of Gaia but don't wish to admit it. But many are
passionately against what they see as entangling alliances
and stifling cooperation with the entire body of the Garou.
Many Garou, especially high-ranking Shadow Lords, see
this cooperation as a direct threat to their plans for su-
premacy. Tribes such as the Black Furies and the Stargazers
see alliance as potentially jeopardizing their independence.
Still others adopt a pose of following peacemaker ideals in
order to gain support from peacemaker Garou. They will
ask the peacemakers to carry out their will, but they will
reject cooperation when the peacemakers ask them to
return the favor

Garou and Other Shape Changers

The Garou have always been on shaky relations with the
werebears and werecoyotes and the mysterious werecats.
The war in the Amazon has heated up conflicts with the
Bastet and Mokolé, though many point hopefully to the
victories won there. Some Garou take a hard line with their
distant cousins, preferring to strike rather than negotiate
with the alien shapeshifters. Other werewolves insist that
the Garou need to overcome ancient enmities and bring
together the entire community of werecreatures. This argu-
ment usually falls along the lines of the peacemakers and
warmongers. Those who resist unity within the Garou
community usually resist union without. Even some peace-
makers feel that bringing together their extraspecial cousins
isa chore that cannot be contemplated until Garou society
is unified. But many see South America asa very likely spot
for the Apocalypse and think that the hard work of gaining
the trust of the werejaguars and werecrocodiles will be
immensely recompensed. The warmongers find this think-
ing utter folly and believe that the costs of a peace effort will
be far too high to ever be repaid.

Political Encounters

There are many ways to get low-ranking characters
drawn up in Garou politics. This usually happens when a
high-ranking Garou decides to use them for pawns, but it
could also happen after the characters learn secret informa-
tion oraccomplish a great task that has political implications.
Young Garou are almost always out of their league when

a Ae

confronted by political turmoil, but if they meet the chal-
lenge, they can gain not only Renown, but invaluable
political links that they can call on later.

The Garou do not have a formal system of accounting for
favors owed and owing (as vampires do), but they do have
a system of honor that demands that favors and attacks be
repaid in kind. This makes feuds and grudges all too com-
mon within the Garou Nation.

The Renown Awards Chart in the Werewolf Second
Edition rulebook (pp. 190-193) can provide many ideas for
political and social conflicts, in addition to those listed
below.

Something is Rotten in the State of
the Tribe

A very patriotic, protribal Garou gets an unexpected
glimpse of corruption within his own tribe (Wyrm, Weaver,
vampire, mage, evil being, etc.). He has no proof other than
the evidence of his own senses and must decide whether to
ignore the evidence or to take the moral high ground and
tisk scorn, isolation and threats to bring the matter to light.
Any help from his packmates in exposing the matter will
cause the corrupt members to scream "conspiracy" and seek
to undermine the credibility of the pack members or chal-
lenge them outright. (Remember, falsely accusing a Garou
of being "of the Wyrm" is a grave offense and can cost the
accuser a lot of Honor Renown; see the Renown Awards
Chart in the Werewolf Second Edition rulebook, pp. 190-
193.)

Resolving this subplot is a tricky business, because it is
very hard to get proof of the problem. The character may
decide to keep quiet but continue to gather evidence to
build his case. This approach could fail if the character
waits too long, and the corrupt Garou launches his plan and
brings disaster on the area or tribe.

A Gest of Loyalties

A Garou or faction within the tribe approaches the
character and offers him a place within a growing tribal
faction that is out to depose a leader. The challenge may or
may not be legitimate, but the player will have to wrestle
with his character's highest goals and ambitions to make a
choice. The rewards of a successful challenge will be great.
The risks for failure are equally great. The rewards for
joining could be very high. The risk for snubbing the offer
could be worse than accepting and failing.

Alliance with Power

After the pack achieves a great victory and increases in
Renown, the pack members become heroes within their
tribes. This increases their status and makes them hot
properties. Clashing factions within the tribe appeal to
each character to join their group. The pack members have
very little time to determine which camp is truly worthy.

Chapter Two: Culture 35

Seer eee nen care arent are re a rem mrrrenemneren se)

Some camps believe that the character should join for
ideological reasons. Other camps sweeten the deal by
offering special favors and rewards. Each character will
have to decide to joina partisan faction, which will earn the
enmity of another faction, or to join no faction and risk
alienating them all. If the character tries to align with
multiple groups competing for his support, he may find
himself in a very uncomfortable wringer when competing
factions make conflicting demands on him.

J Spy

Once the character is solidly aligned with a faction his
mentors ask him to undertake a dangerous mission. They
ask him to publicly drop his allegiance with the camp and
join a rival camp to spy on them. The character will have
to face the scorn of his current camp, since the rank and file
members will not know he is a spy. Even his own pack may
distrust him, since he appears to be an oath breaker. If the
character accepts, he must work to gain the trust of the
other faction, and learn their secrets. He must make secret
reports without being discovered. If the arrangement goes
sour and the character is discovered, his original faction
may betray him and deny that he was a spy. They'll say
something like, "After he failed in our camp he joined
yours. After he failed in your camp he tried to learn your
secrets to get back in our good graces!"

To put a twist on the deal, the character may become
convinced that his old faction is actually working against
the interests of the tribe, Garou Nation, or Gaia asa whole.
He must decide whether to stick with his original mission
out of loyalty or to switch sides for real. If he switches sides
for real, he must decide whether to become a counterspy
and feed false information to his original camp. He also
must decide whether to disclose his spy activities to hisnew
camp and risk incurring their wrath. He must also decide
how much he wants to exploit his ties to his old group in
undermining them.

Ambitions of Youth

After a particularly stunning victory, the leadership
potential of pack members has been noticed by local
leaders. The Garou have the option to gain mentors, who
shepherd them around the rocky pitfalls of Garou politics.
The pack is invited to speak at moots to explain their
conquests, share the knowledge they have gained about the
Wyrm and call on the assembled Garou to take action in
whatever cause the characters are championing.

If the characters make a credible effort in swaying the
moot, they may be able to organize a large-scale invasion of
a Wyrm pit or Pentex branch. If the raid is successful, one
of the characters may be offered a high-ranking position, for
example as a Sept Leader or Caern Warder. She may have
to battle rivals for the position, but if she wins, she's on her
way to prominence in the Garou Nation.

36
———

But the higher the Garou climbs, the more she finds
competitors out to challenge her and rigid followers who
won't cooperate with certain directions. The player will
have to decide how much force to apply and how much she
should moderate her own actions. Leaders also cannot
come and go as they please, the way they did when they
were young and relatively powerless.

Sometimes succession opportunities come whena leader
dies a violent death or vanishes in the Umbra. If the players
are ambitious, their characters can fill the void by assuming
the leader's tasks uninvited. This is risky, since it can
backfire and earn the animosity of other Garou, but the
rewards are great.

The tribes often appoint representatives to carry their
words to other groups. These roving "ambassadors" move
from tribe to tribe, tribe to sept, tribe to caern and tribe to
council. Ambitious characters may seek and attain this
function. Even characters with no ambitions may be tapped
for this function. They must carry out their tasks out of a
sense of duty or lose Honor. Representing a tribe or sept is
agreat way to geta look into the politics of another tribe or
sept.

When special councils are called, as was the case for the
war in the Amazon, all tribes must send representatives.
This is another chance for the characters to seek offices of
power and importance. As a twist, the leaders may believe
a particular council is a waste of time and deliberately send
an underpowered, low-ranking youth as a subtle insult. Or,
if a council involves an especially deadly mission, a leader
mightsend a character he greatly dislikes. This will backfire
if the character survives, as the character may grow in
stature.

Leadership Dacuurm: The
Silver Fangs

The problems with the Garou Nation begin at the top,
with the Silver Fangs. This autocratic tribe has held su-
preme power over all Garou for millennia. In their early
days their ancestors oversaw the proudest victories of a
proud race. At present, their descendants preside over the
needless and tragic decline of the Garou Nation. Insulated
from the rest of Garou society by their own rituals and
aristocratic culture, they have lost touch with those they
command and issue orders that are confusing, contradic-
tory and often ignored. The rank and file Garou have lost
a tremendous amount of respect for the white-hued wolves
who preside over their community. Many Garou work hard
to circumvent the capricious dictates of the Silver Fangs
without appearing to contradict their rulers. Some take
their dictates only grudgingly. Others ignore them com-
pletely. And some take every opportunity to make their
masters look bad. This weakens the entire Garou Nation,
but the Silver Fangs refuse to acknowledge that a problem
exists and have closed off most channels that the rest of the
nation once used to air their grievances with the Fangs.

Werewolf Storytellers Handbook

a 7 ee

The Silver Fangs are prisoners of their own past success

Though they make a great outward show of proclaiming
past victories and ancient glories, many of the imperial
leaders secretly feel that they are pretenders who are always
one step away from being exposed. In their refined form of
Harano they covertly feel that their deeds fall far short of
the past accomplishments of the Garou Nation. Because
they feel personally inadequate to live up to the glories of
the past, each additional goal and new project fills them
with dread. They surround themselves with insulating
layers of sycophants and use their influence to try to
suppress or break the younger Garou who bring fresh vision
to the moldering halls of the Silver Fangs.

Many of the more powerful Garou of other tribes know
of the decay in the highest level of the whitest wolves, but
they fear to reveal it for fear of weakening and dividing the
Garou at a time when the Garou Nation needs to come
together. The Silver Fangs may be corrupt, but no one
(except the Shadow Lords) wants the Shadow Lords to take
over. This leaves the Silver Fangsas the main game in town.
So the other Garou stifle their outrage and continue to
bend the knee. For now.

Rivals

Though many Garou see the leadership void as the worst
form of crisis, some see it as a juicy opportunity. Several
camps conspire to take power, overtly or covertly.

Shadow Lord Revolutionary Guard

This Secret Shadow Lord camp consists mostly of high
powered Philodox and their Ahroun allies from around the
world. They are the most subtle of the Shadow Lords, and
most of them are homid. They meet in secret at each
Shadow Lord Grand Moot, and plot the complete over-
throw of the Silver Fangs. Militarily, the Guard are the
most powerful of the rival factions, and they have strong
internal coordination. Though they hatch their plots in
secret and carry out their actions without any coordination
with the Shadow Lord hierarchy, they operate with the
tacit blessing of the very highest levels of tribal authority.

Many high-ranking Shadow Lords aspire to join the
Revolutionary Guard, and being tapped for membership is
considered a tremendous honor. They have thoroughly
infiltrated the Shadow Lord Judges of Doom and have
corrupted the purpose of the Judges to further their assault
on the Silver Fangs. Some of the Judges, who are aware of
the growing politically motivated perversion of their sacred
purpose, are working to foil the Revolutionary Guard.
Some powerful lupus Shadow Lords hate the homid Guard
with a passion and seek to flush out and destroy the Guard.
They consider the Guard's covert operations to be tricks
worthy only of the Weaver and benefiting only the Wyrm.
This has led to some explosive confrontations that have
rocked Shadow Lord society to the core.

2 eer merce wee Mee ear cm PE Tr rR


Seer ere een renee caren are Ar Sa re smarrrennerenew

The Revolutionary Guard has tested the Silver Fang's
strength in some key conflicts, and has forced the white wolves
to back down in several important showdowns. The Guards
key advantage is that they are well organized, and they enjoy
the support of many Shadow Lords who know of their plans.
Their key disadvantage is the way they have made gains, often
by exploiting dangerous situations. On several occasions they
held back crucial resources that ensured that important Silver
Fang missions would fail. By exploiting these wins, Revolu-
tionary Guard leaders have managed to humiliate and further
weaken the Silver Fangs, but the Guard also earned the enmity
of the Garou whose lives they put in jeopardy.

The Guard has greatly increased in power recently and is
rumored to be planning a major coup very soon.

Loki's Smile

This Get of Fenris camp is limited to European Garou and
operates entirely behind the scenes of Garou politics. They do
not have the blessing of the Fenris leadership, who openly
challenge Silver Fang policy but have forbidden conspiracies
against the leaders of the Garou Nation. The Get's rugged,
almost fanatical sense of duty and loyalty, even to weak
leaders, is legendary. Loki's Smile is not out to topple the Silver
Fangs in order to exalt the current Get of Fenris leadership.
Though the members seldom discuss their goals after the
toppling of the Fangs, they all know that they seek to claim
tulership of the Get of Fenris and depose their current leaders.
They are named for the Norse trickster god and chose their
name toreflect the high degree of secrecy of their methods and
goals.

Loki's Smile is led by Half-Moons, and staffed by Full-
Moons, and only admits as members those who have somehow
crossed the Get leaders by trying to challenge the Silver Fangs.
Smilers will work with any Garou or Kinfolk who feels slighted
by the Silver Fangs or holds a grudge against them. They have
even allowed metis to join and have used Wyrm minions to
further their goals. They also seek to embarrass Fang and Get
leaders by finding their weaknesses or shameful secrets and
exploiting them. A typical tactic is to find and expose metis
Garou who are the unacknowledged spawn of their leaders.

The Avenging Mother

This group is a small subfaction of the altruistic Black Fury
Order of the Merciful Mother, which operates overtly as a
ministry to humans in troubled areas all over the world. The
Avenging Mother group covertly tracks the Silver Fangs,
using its global focus as a cover for probing weaknesses and
anticipating rulings. The Merciful Mother has gained a mea-
sure of trust within the Silver Fangs, who view the that camp
asa valuable conduit to mortal society. The Avenging Mother
has exploited the Silver Fang's trust by using their position to
spy on critical intertribal functions. The Avenging Mother
lacks sufficient strength to mount a credible challenge against
the Silver Fang leaders, but they would make a powerful ally
that could tip the balance of power should they decide to join
with another faction.

Crest of the Horn

ThisChildren of Gaiasubfaction operates withina larger group,
the Servants of the Unicorn, which is dedicated to resolving
intertribal differences. The members of the Crestare less interested
in smoothing over differences than they are in exploiting differ-
ences to wrench power away from the Silver Fangs. They keep
track of the grudges that each tribe nurses against the Fangsandare
building a powerful coalition to take power. They do not want to
take power directly asmuchas they want to reject direct, autocratic
rule and supplant it with a Garou Parliament. They have found
allies in every tribe, including powerful Stargazer seers who have
predicted that the Silver Fangs will fall by their own hand.

The Crest is very close to marshaling its allies in nearly every
tribe to enforce a bloodless coup. However, some members have
recently cautioned that the group needs toslow its eagerness. They
suggest that too many Garou depend ona rigid hierarchy and clear
chain ofcommand, and that takingaway dominance could lead to
the unraveling of the fabric of Garou society. They suggest a return
to Children of Gaia policy, which is to work to openly guide and
influence the Silver Fangs to make better decisions. Other Horn
members find this talk to be cowardice at the moment when
courage is needed most.

Fang Breakers

Militant members of the Red Talons and Wendigo have
forged an unusual alliance of convenience to return control of
the Garou Nation over to the fiercest warriors and shift policy
back to one of containment of humans. They count a few allies
from other tribes but remain a fringe group. Their hostility
toward humans offends the other tribes, who have worked
hard to cultivate strong ties with the human race.

The Inner Path

The smallest of the rival camps, the Inner Path is a secret
faction of Stargazers dedicated to taking over the Silver Fangs
by mind controland shaping policy from within. They are very
secretive and operate without the knowledge of their tribal
masters, who would stop them if they knew of the Path's plans.
They work to secure an alliance with the Silent Strider camp
called the Harbingers, but now fear that the Harbingers have
deciphered their true purpose, and may stop them. The Inner
Path has succeeded in winning converts within the Silver
Fangs, most notably the Silver Fang secret society called
Renewal.

Renewal

There are rivals to the power of the Silver Fangs even
within the halls of the white wolves. The secret society
called Renewal dares to dissent from tribal orthodoxy, and
seeks to replace the old, inbred, senile leaders with fresh
and sane ones. They don't want the Silver Fangs to relin-
quish power over the other tribes, since they think this will
spell doom for the Garou Nation. They have recently made
overtures to the Stargazer group called the Inner Path, and
are exploring ways they can work together.

|


The Silver Pack

Over the last few hundred years, the members of the
fiercely independent Silver Packs have come to realize
that they are enforcing Silver Fang rules and decisions
that ultimately hurt the Garou Nation. Some have died
rather than execute orders they found to be unjust. Now,
there is a widespread sentiment among the Garou en-
forcers that the time has come for them to breach their
sacred impartiality and bring down the Silver Fangs.
Many are working to break down the political walls
separating Garou factions, but in so doing they risk
becoming the pawns of the factions who help them.
They will accept the help of Garou who sincerely try to
help them resolve differences and build alliances.

But the Silver Packs have gained bitter enemies who
resent their judgments. These jealous Garou fail to
accept that the Phoenix has precedence over all other
tribes and all other totems. Working to help the Silver
Packs could make secret enemies for the characters.

Opportunities for Political
Intrigue

There are many good settings for political intrigue, but
the best are the Garou gatherings.

Chapter Two: Culture

Each monthly tribal moot is designed to bring the Garou
together, but it is more often an opportunity for Garou to
vent their frustrations, forge alliances and challenge adver-
saries. Common topics for each tribe are the declining
effectiveness Silver Fang leadership and whether their own
tribal leaders have an effective plan in the face of this
declining leadership.

Sept moots are designed to celebrate and strengthen a
caern, but they are often rent with division as members of
each tribe jockey for position with one another and nurse
old grievances. Trials held at moots used to go uncontested.
Now many Garou openly question the judgment of their
leaders and undermine the power structure.

The Garou in charge of running the moot often lack
control and have trouble restraining or even channeling
the anger into productive directions. When moots arrive
on the brink of disaster, the masters of the moot are forced
tocut short the schedule and call for the Revel. Sometimes,
revels are the only time all the participants act in concert,
and they often have a calming, healing effect on the group.
By enacting a ritual of unity, the fractured Garou experi-
ence unity.


WAS
SS

Grand Moot

Grand Moots bring together entire tribes. They area rich
source of political drama, as camps within a tribe air their
differences and attempt to gather allies. The Grand Moot
will seldom be a focus of a standard Werewolf game session,
since it is only open to members of one tribe. However, it

makes a great backdrop for a solo game session and provides

an opportunity for one character to seek help from greater

members of her tribe. [tis especially important when games
focus on arbitrating tribal politics. If a character needs to
accuse a member of his own tribe of treachery, he may be

called to bring in other witnesses, say the members of his
pack. This can get all the player characters into the game
for a rousing session.

Concolation

Concolations became more common as global transpor-
tation became easier, and now they occur every few years.
They are wild and unrestrained affairs that showcase the
best and the worst of the Garou Nation. Since it is open to
all Garou, the characters can arrive in their pack

The Concolation is the setting for the arbitration of the
greatest intertribal disputes. The rival factions that seek to
challenge the Silver Fangs make their power plays here.
The Silver Fangs dread the Concolations, because each one
is more contentious than the last, and more challenging to
their power.

In response, the Silver Fangs have used the Concolations
asa place to clamp down on dissent and demand increased
oaths of loyalty. They have even used the Concolation to
send dangerous rivals on potentially deadly missions, offer-
ing insufficient resources, inadequate knowledge and
negligible backup. If the rivals protest, the Silver Fangs
imply that the rivals are cowards and try to use the as-
sembled crowd to shame the rivals into accepting. This
tactic keeps working, but it is only a matter of time until a
pack survives the death mission and returns to be showered
with enough glory and Renown to challenge the Silver
Fangs.

Because Silver Packs are renewed or created at
Concolations, many different groups champion their own
members for admission. They try to stack the pack in their
favor so that they will have a friendly ear and receive
preferential treatment. However, many Silver Pack mem-
bers do indeed become impartial when placed in the Silver
Pack, and refuse to award extraordinary treatment or spe-
cial consideration.

One way to use the Concolation in a game is to make it
the payoff to an extended campaign. At the start of the
campaign, the Concolation can already be scheduled, which

would allow the characters to look forward to it (or dread it)
as it approaches. If the campaign is an ambitious affair
involving high-stakes events, the Concolation could come
about as a direct result of the character's actions.

Se yy

|


For example, the pack could precipitate a Concolation if
they stumbled across Wyrm plots of unprecedented scope.
If they obtained compelling evidence of a Defiler Wyrm
plot to take over the entire body of the Wyrm, ora Seventh
Generation scheme to taint all remaining caerns, they
would be justified in prevailing upon their tribal leaders to
launch a Concolation. If they successfully get the word out
in the Garou community, the clamor fora Concolation will
cause one to spring into being.

Also, player characters are famous for getting into ter-
rible scrapes. If they get in way over their heads, it's
conceivable that they will wind up in so much trouble that
their tribes alone cannot rule on their actions, but a full
Concolation is required to sort out the mess. The pack will
have to rely on wits and clever role-playing to survive such
a high-stakes trial.

Likewise, joyous events such as discovering and charting
a completely new Umbral realm would be grounds for
calling a Concolation. Restoring a corrupted caern could
be sufficient cause to bring the tribes together as well.

The Concolation is a good setting for political intrigue.
Every power group that the pack ran into during the course
of the game will want to discuss matters with the characters,
and the characters will have to handle the meetings care-
fully.

Ultimately, most Garou believe that the multitribal
Concolations are essential, and that the war will be lost if
they don't come together. Hard-won coalitions, the ac-
cords in the Amazon for example, unravel quickly if they
are not constantly maintained. The Nation is splitting
apart as the Garou try to come together, and Gaia calls for
brave Garou who are not afraid of exploiting their political
clout to preserve the Nation.

Imperial Moot

The heart of Silver Fang power lies in the special ritual
called the Imperial Moot. Imperial Moots can only be
called by decree of the Kings of the Silver Fangs and only
in the most critical circumstances. There have been fewer
than twenty in all Garou history. In this special ceremony,
the Silver Fangs direct the energies of the entire Garou
Nation toward one purpose. This may be to destroy a very
powerful Wyrm being, to empower a dying caern or to
reclaim an area to the Wyld. There have been no Imperial
Moots since 1855, and many Garou believe that the Silver
Fangs are on the verge of calling the next one in order to
reconsolidate their power and to make a preemptive strike
against their rival factions. Some believe that the Silver
Fangs will use this moot to demand loyalty from every
Garou on pain of banishment or death. Some members of
rival factions have sworn that they will attack the Silver
Fangs rather than swear loyalty. Others take a more subtle
approach, having decided to swear fealty to the Garou
Nation rather than the Silver Fangs, and thus see the entire
Imperial Moot as an opportunity for a massive showing of
no confidence in the Silver Fang leaders.

Chapter Two: Culture

The Divided Heart

There is a large and subtle political fault line in the
Garou community that goes beyond the dissension be-
tween the young and the old, the males and the females, the
warmongers and the reconcilers, the old guard and the
modernists, or even the Silver Fangs and rest of the tribes.
It is an often quiet but very deep and very old wound based
on breed. Advanced Storytellers can add a lot of spice to
political infighting by accentuating the politics of breed.

The Garou have great difficulty resolving differences
because of their inherent dual nature — half human, half
wolf. Their two sides face problems and resolve differences
in utterly different, even contradictory ways. The clash of
the two breeds can leave both sides in a dispute more angry
than when they began. Rather than resolve internal or
external tribal problems, their divergent and often irrecon-
cilable approaches and solutions often make problems
worse.

Asaresult, the Garou community has split internally, in
asecret, rarely named division that cleaves every pack, sept,
tribe and the nation as a whole. The division is built into
the bone and marrow of every Garou because it is a division
of origin. Of breed. Homid and lupus thinking are so far
apart on so many issues that conflict is inevitable and
unavoidable. Metis are largely ignored in this conflict, as
their power is considered nonexistent. Few Garou will
acknowledge the conflict, and many younger members are
plainly unaware of it. It does not directly affect the young
and only indirectly imposes those Garou who gain Rank.
But as a Garou gains prestige and power within the Garou
nation, it becomes harder and harder to ignore. Only the
oldest and most powerful Garou discuss it or even have
words for it. It is of critical importance to them, and they
work hard to make sure younger Garou do not know of it.

The issue revolves around the method Garou will use to
apportion power and apply resources. It is to the advantage
of lupus Garou to make decisions through might and direct
combat, where they enjoy the advantage. It is to the
advantage of the homid Garou to set policy through debate,
argument and political maneuvering, where they have the
upper hand. The homid elders call lupus ideas on overt
dominance through animal strength "beast thinking," and
sneer that it is an oxymoron in terms. The lupus elders call
homid ideas on subtle political maneuvering "monkey
tricks," and disdain them as unworthy of true Garou.

This secret political division between homid Garou and
lupus Garou is deep set; its origins lie in the very manner in
which humans and wolves resolve social problems.

The Wolf Solution

In the wolf community, interanimal dynamics are com-
plex, but solutions are relatively simple. Pack structure is
clear, with an autocratic leader on top, the pack Alpha, and
wolves of lesser status below. The Alpha is an unquestioned
dictator. All attempts to deviate from his commands are

41


|

seen as a direct challenge to his authority, and must be
settled with a confrontation that can end only with imme-
diate abject humiliation or blood. If the challenger does not
immediately hang his head and tail in shame and offer up
his vulnerable underbelly, the two must fight. The winner
becomes the unquestioned leader, and the loser, if alive,
skulks off. There is no arbitration, no mediated solution
and no compromise. Those are human ways. Not the ways
of the wolf.

This method has the advantage of providing a clear
chain of command and promoting unambiguous loyalties
on the part of the community. Wolves follow the leader,
whoever that is. They challenge if they feel they can win,
and they obey if they feel they cannot. Many wolves yearn
for the perks of the Alpha's office, but few try to attain it
since the stakes are so high. This system tends to put the
strongest and craftiest wolves at the top. The attributes that
enshrine them in power are reflections of the skills they
need to fight other creatures of similar or lesser power and
intelligence. However, these attributes are seldom ad-
equate in a fight against the ingenuity of humans or the
supernatural powers of the Wyrm.

The Human Solution

In the human community, fighting is described as an
unacceptable way to resolve differences. In all but the most
primitive of cultures, leaders usually do not resort to overt
personal physical violence with other leaders to assert
dominance over the groups. The leaders either work out
differences constructively, they commit violence covertly
or they marshal their followers in mass violence against the
followers of the other.

But the followers often demand that their leaders accept
many of the follower's aims. This compromise has found
large expression in democratic forms of government but
shows up even in authoritarian regimes. Middle class mer-
chants have brought down kings, and dispirited foot soldiers
have lost wars. Wise rulers make sure they at least have
support of their followers in their most public goals, even if
they have little support for their less visible objectives. Too
many humans are too stubborn and willful to make very
good subordinates. They are not always easily subordinated
by Alphas using active-aggressive techniques to rule, and
the ruled use a plethora of passive-aggressive techniques to
resist orders they dislike.

This method has the advantage that the leader and the
masses are often forced ot give and take in closer connec-
tion than that experienced by an Alpha and the rest of the
pack. The will of the governed human is often a consider-
ation, if forno other reason than granting minor concessions
can avoid revolution. The leader can act with assurance
that his position is relatively safe — or at least that he does
not have to fear that at any moment his authority might be
challenged and his life taken by one of his trusted followers.
For the most part, though followers may try to usurp his
position, they usually must work through overt channels,

42 Werewolf Storytellers Handbook

TT

without the element of surprise. They may try to destabilize
the ruler thorough covert channels, but they risk the
censure of the community even if they succeed.

This human method has a distinct disadvantage, as well.
When leaders fail to resolve differences with other leaders,
they often marshal their followers in open warfare against
another leader and his or her followers. The death toll of
large-scale warfare as a form of conflict resolution is often
very high.

The tendency toward stubborn self-will in humans is as
ancient as humankind, and is described in detail in sources
as diverse as Genesis and the writings of anarchists. Many
lupus Garou maintain that all changes in human society
away from pack politics is Weaver manipulation. Mages
explain this asa function of the potential for Awakening —
a crucial psychic component that separates humans from
the beasts. Nevertheless, humans can be easily led by a
powerful Alpha, and many humans are very willing to
surrender their free will for a feeling of security.

The Garou Resolution

When lupus and homid Garou come together in the
Garou community, they bring with them their own deep-
set notions of problem solving and hierarchy. The homids
want to debate and outmaneuver their rivals, and the lupus
want to tear their rivals' throats out. These styles are in
direct conflict. The competing forms of Garou conflict
resolution are in themselves a conflict that must be re-
solved. The lupus find the homid forms to be weak, craven
monkeyshines, and the homids find the lupus forms to be
belligerent, short-sighted internal violence masquerading
as policy.

In reconciling the differences in forms, wise Garou
created the Litany. It is not perfect, but it attempts to walk
amiddle line between the two extremes without embracing
either. Some homids complain that keeping animal forms
of conflict resolution will consistently doom the Garou to
a lifetime of internecine strife and power struggles. Some
lupus complain that any compromise in hierarchy is unac-
ceptable, since compromise itself is a human concept. The
answers enshrined in the Litany are not perfect, but they
have has kept the community together for thousands of
years.

The trouble with the homid-lupus struggle is that nei-
ther side is right. Though some homids have had just cause
toscheme and plot against some foolish, overbearing lupus
tulers, others have not and have undermined excellent
leaders for their own gain. And though many lupus have
had good reason to tear into a homid Garou who was
engaged in destructive betrayal, many have provoked feuds
and carried out vendettas by resorting to violence long
before they had exhausted other means. The war of breed
is very old and very hidden, but it is very strong. It shows no
sign of easy reconciliation.

The rites performed by a given sept vary according to a
number of factors, with some septs performing only the
great seasonal rites and others performing some sort of
seasonal rite at least once per moon. The nature of these
tribal rites varies widely, ranging from the solemn, stento-
rian Rite of Long Remembering of the Silver Fangs to the
American Bone Gnawers' raucous celebrations on
Superbowl Sunday.

All tribal rites reflect, at least in some part, the essence
of the tribe that created them. The rites have all been
passed down through the centuries, and they survive be-
cause they hold some fierce kernel of the truth of Gaia

which the tribe values. However, although tribes such as
the Shadow Lords and Silver Fangs are loathe to admit it,
each rite has also undergone continuous change and re-
flects in some way the modern tribe as well. This combination
of the ancient and everlasting (the bone in Garou par-
lance) and the currentand ephemeral (the blood) reinforces
the C

The following rites are some of the more common rites

‘ou's connection to both Gaia and their tribemates.

performed by each of the thirteen Garou tribes. The accom-
panying chart shows each rite in relation to the four great
seasonal rites of the Garou. One seasonal tribal rite is given
for each of the tribes, but Storytellers should feel free to use
these as templates for other seasonal rites, perhaps per-
formed only by certain septs or in particular places in the
World of Darkness.

Unless otherwise noted, tribal seasonal rites follow the
basic em outlined in the Werewolf Second Edition
rulebook. This requires the ritemaster to make a Stamina +

Rituals roll with a difficulty level of 8 minus the level of the
caern (8 - level; if the rite is performed at a caern). For most

tribal seasonal rites there is no adverse reaction unless a

botch is made, in which case the participating Garou will
each receive a +1 to difficulty levels on all Rituals rolls for
the next lunar month due to the jarring of their psyches.
Alternatively, the Storyteller can choose another negative
effect he feels is more fitting, although the results should
last no more than a month. The result of a failure is that the
rite simply does not feel quite right, and any usual results do
not materialize.

The Mysteries (Level Three)

Tribe: The Black Furies

Time: First new moon following the Winter Solstice (Decem-
ber 20, 21 or 22)

In the womb-dark of the first new moon following the Winter
Solstice most Black Furies tag in what they term the
Mysteries. The Mysteries, as d despread rites, vary from sept
tosept, butthe essential nai tren of thisriteissurprisingly

and questioning. Duri .e Furies ceremoniously

The ritemaster, usually the eldest in the gathering, then tells a
taleofone ofthe many women whowalked the spiral path into the
labyrinth, into the death-darkness where knowledge lies, perhaps
into the arms of the enemy. There are many such heroines:
Persephone, Inanna, Kore. As she speaks, one by one the Furies
begin a dance, often mimicked by maypole revelers, during which
each Fury weavesher threadamonghersistersasshe makesher way
down thespiral path. When they havefinished theirdanceand the
ritemaster has ended her tale, the sisters sit in the darkness and
share cup of blood-wine, the drink of spiritual awakenings. Until
recently, a touch of hemlock or other poison was always added to
the brew to aid in visions, but the dangerous process is not always
practiced today. The rite ends at dawn.

Superbowl Sunday (Level Two)

Tribe: The Bone Gnawers
