Time: January (Superbowl Sunday)

Every year American Bone Gnawers gather around radios and
theoccasional TV setand get ready towatch the BigGame just like
8bazillion red-blooded humans in their cozy livingroomsand bars.
Superbowl Sunday is the date of a peculiarly Bone Gnawer rite.
Theritealmost definitely descends from an oldbettingrite wherein
the limited resources ofa sept were for one nightput at the disposal

during the pre-game iber of the sept tells what
he thinks the sept should do for:
include scouring the streets to help kids or women running from
their drunk and abusive family members. (After all, Superbowl
Sunday is the most violent day of the year, so it's not like it's hard
torun into such folks!) Other common suggestions include going
after drug dealers, checking on Kinfolk, conducting a rite to flush.
out any Maneaters (Garou partaking of human flesh), etc.
Despite, orperhapsbecause of, thesurprisingamountofhelp the
Bone Gnawers give to whomever they direct their attention that
evening, the Gnawersalso view thisrite asa great excuse fora party.

44
lh —_——

As the sept gathers round to watch the Big Game, the ritemaster
passes around an old hat or the like and each Gnawer throws in
some small token of value (a CD, an Indian head nickel, a Spawn
comic, etc.) and declares what he wants to do when he wins. He
then predicts who will win and by what margin. As the hat passes
rounditcollectsenergy from the participating Garou, and iftherite
issuccessful itactually becomesa temporary fetish. Thishat is worn
by the winning Garou. Its power lasts for the night, drawing the
Garou unerringly to his target of vengeance or need. A sept often
uses the same hat for many years.

No two Garou can bet on the exact same result, so there are
often tussles over who gets what numbers. But the mommas and
poppas soon slap the youngsters into shape, and all bets are made
before kickoff. Watching the game is part of the rite, as is severely
mocking the halftime show, with the best mockers gaining some
Renown for their skill. Throughout the game winners of various
side bets and contests are given objects from the betting hat as
rewards. At the end of the game the sept takes off on the mission
chosen by the winning bettor. The rite ends at dawn or whenever
the Bone Gnawers get too tired.

Imbole (Level Three)

Tribe: The Fianna

Time: February 2

AtImbole the Fianna gather around large bonfires (although a
reasonably sized fireplace will do ina pinch) to perform one of their
more powerful rites. Until recg most all Fianna septs
performed the Imbolc rites. a good number of septs still
perform the rite, though aof the British Isles rigidly

keep the tradition. Altho bolc rites almost always take
place atasept's caer, the ly have to be performed
there.

At sunset the bonfires @e built up and lighted to the rhythms
of Celticmusic. The mood ally intense with anticipation,and
many Fiannaclaim tofind perceptions involuntarily slipping
into the Penumbra e preceding day. As the flames
begin tolightupd itemaster tells the tale of Fionn.
mac Cumbhail, the the Fianna, and the greatest

among their Kinfolk. Af e first tale is finished, the ritemaster
moves on to several more classic Fianna ballads and stories
involvingthefairfolk. Asshe speaks, the ritemastercarefully grinds
upa small number of faerie seeds with a mortar and pestle. These
seeds, which have been gathered during the Fianna's occasional
forays into faerie trods or the Arcadian Gateway realm, are
powerful indeed. Mixing the seeds into a potent home-brew, the
ritemaster invites each Garou present to partake of the newly
created spirit-brew.

As each Fianna scoops up a mug of the brew, she calls out a
stanza of poetry, a short riddle or a few lines of song as an offering
to Gaia at this time of awakening. Once all have filled their cups,
each of the Fianna raises her cup and drinks in turn to Fionn mac
Cumhail, the new cubs of the Fianna, and their friends of faerie
(some Fianna have hypothesized that this is actually a toast to the
past, the present and the future of Gaia, but most Fianna dismiss
this hypothesis). Drinking three times deeply, the Garou step
sideways into the Penumbra. There (unless the rite fails) they find

Feralia (Level Four)

Tribe: The Silent Striders

Time: February 13

Variously knownas Feraliaand The Dead Time, February 13th
great importance tothe Silent Striders of the world. The

some sort. Even the Eaters of the Dead participate (although their
version of the rite may be slightly different; some Striders have
reported finding "burt out" Painting Stones they believe were
used by the Eaters). If members ofa Silent Striderseptorpack know
ofa fellow Strider suffering from Harano, they will normally do all
within their power to convince the suffering Garou to participate
in the rite, for it has been known to cure the Harano-stricken.

Throughout The Dead Time, Silent Striders gather at places
across Gaia wherever the objects known as Painting Stones are
located. Other tribes are unsure how Silent Striders know where
to locate such stones when traveling in a foreign area, but it is
rumored that the wandering Striders sniff out the powerful stones
in the Penumbra. Painting Stones are not named for any marks
they bear throughout the year; the name instead describes part of
the Feralia rite.

Atexactly the middle of the night, the designated ritemaster
walks silently up to the Painting Stone and traces the symbol
of the Silent Striders on the stone. The tracing may be in mud,
berry juice, blood or any other natural substance. As she
finishes, the ritemaster quietly names one of the signs of the
coming Apocalypse that she has learned during her life, and
she then says whether she has seen evidence of this sign since

Mg

Chapter Two: Culture

the last Dead Time. In turn, each Strider present paints the
symboland speaks ofa sign and returns to her place in the pack.
When all have spoken and placed their mark on the Painting
Stone, the ritemaster rises and circles the stone three times
counterclockwise. She then leaps over the Painting Stone,
passing into the Dark Umbra, the Umbra of the dead, at the
top of the arc. The other Striders follow in turn.

Within the Dark Umbra the Striders are met by members
of their departed Kinfolk, who whisper pieces of prophecies
and knowledge to their living relations. Throughout this time
the Striders run westward, evermoving as they listen to the
wisdom of their Kin. Itis said that as long as they keep running,
they are protected from the wraiths. Should a Strider falter,
though, even for an instant, she may become trapped within
the Dark Umbra of souls, perhaps forever. The Striders con-
tinue running and listening to the whispers until they see a
gleaming rock in front of them. Leaping over this new stone,
the Garou find themselves at another of the Painting Stones,
just as any Garou there are leaping into the Dark Umbra. This
unexplained phenomenon can result in an odd sight in the
physical world, as one Garou leaps upwards only to have an
entirely different Garou complete the leap.

The rite sweeps westward with the night until all partici-
pants have completed their leaps. The Striders often learn
much from their time among the dead; however, the informa-
tion is always fragmented and unclear, and the Striders spend
much time attempting to determine its exact meaning and
import.

System: The base difficulty for this roll is 7, but there are
only a few Painting Stones within the area of a caern, so
ritemasters are usually on their own. Failure indicates the
ritemaster does not manage to open the gate between the
physical world and the Dark Umbra. This results in a loss of
Honor (3 points) for the ritemaster. A botch indicates that the
ritemaster loses her footing in the Dark Umbra and may
well become lost (by failing a second roll).

Garou leaders (in Homid form unless no non-Kinfolk humans

sheltered the pups that became the first of the Children of
Gaia. Following the planting the participants are all invited to
share a meal and to dance, play music, sing or otherwise
celebrate life and their love for Gaia and each other.

System: The Children watch over all Peace Trees planted
for they are very sensitive to the ebb and flow of spiritual
energies; a successful Perception + Empathy roll will reveal the
general balance between Weaver, Wyrm, and Wyld near the
tree. However, if the initial rite fails the trees are simply trees,
while a botch indicates the trees are somehow tainted by the
Wyrm and not only will not provide information but will
radiate a slight aura of hostility, encouraging conflict in the
nearby area.

Talons continue the deep-throated, ululating growl that is the
refrain of the Song of the Impergium. At dawn the Red Talons
normally return to their normal territory, far from all human
habitation.

During this lyrical and joyous rite, the ritemaster leads the
way out onto one of the sweeping plains of their land. The

others of the sept trail along behind her in no particular order,
often pelting each other with any snow still on the ground or
leaping in mock ambushes. Spirits run high and that is as it

shouldbe, forthe energy encouragesall life toburstforthinjoy. JF
As they walk, the ritemaster tells the tale of Tuacholka, a
Wendigo ancestor who climbed the highest mountain in the
world to see Gaia Herself when She was grieving so fiercely for
the loss of the Croatan that even the earth, Her body, could no
longer grow warm. Tuacholka told Gaia that the Wendigoand
their brothers and sisters of the Uktena would never forget the
Croatan, and that they would gladly take the weight of their
Mother's pain if only she would return Her warmth to the
world. Grateful for Her children's love and strength, Gaia
returned the warmth to the lands, and Her tears turned to
flowers of love.

Asthe ritemasterspeaks, she ceremoniously gathersenough
flowers to form a wreath. Shedding a single tear each upon the
delicate flowers in memory of the Croatan, she passes the
wreath toherseptmates to add their tears. When all have done

so, the ritemaster tosses the wreath far out onto a river or the
ocean so that it might carry their pain and love to the Croatan.
The Garou then turn to the fields and flowers they love and
commence a wild, romping salute to the beauty of life and
Gaia's blessings.

Tribe: Silver Fangs

The Rite of Long Remembering is performed by every
Silver Fang septon August second of every year. Although the
date has been known by various names, this day is said to be the

Once the Drama of the First Wolf has been reenacted, the

seems remarkably self-serving to the few members of other

ite of the Opened Claw (Level Four)

Tribe: Shadow Lords

Two weeks following the Autumnal equinox, the Shadow
Lords of Japan and the Far East observe the Rite of the

Opened Claw. WesterngShadow,Lords may also observe

and the watching'Garou of the sept are ever alert for a
mistake or hesitation by the ritemaster. Although the sept's
leader may designate as ritemaster any Shadow Lord in his

After the pouring of the Ke-Chuin, the ritemaster searches

Mother Gaia and Father Thunder have chosen to partake

the spirit, revealing it in its true glory or depravity. Those
Shadow Lords who know this rite claim to see a burning
halo or aura around those chosen. Those Garou chosen
must step forward and drink deeply of the bitter brew. The
ritemaster closely watches the imbiber's aura, claiming that
any sign of Wyrm taint or corruption will immediately be
revealed. This may indeed occur, as the Garou named
corrupt inevitably die within minutes of drinking the Ke-
Chuin. Members of other tribes have, perhaps uncharitably,
remarked how often the ritemaster's enemies or those who
have displeased him are among the Garou who die of their
exposed taint. Those whose auras reflect purity after drink-
ing of the Ke-Chuin often gain position in their sept.

System: If the rite is unsuccessful, the ritemaster will be
unable to truly detect any sort of aura from the assembled
Garou. A botch indicates that the ritemaster will have a
fatal reaction to the Ke-Chuin tea.

Rite of the Three Wells (Level Three)

Tribe: Get of Fenris

Time: October 31

The Get of Fenris take to the Umbra every Samhain
(October 31) to seek out the three wells at the base of
Yggdrasil, the World Ash Tree. The Get claim that Yggdrasil
isa vast splinter from the original World Tree of Gaia, whose
three roots each draw energy and wisdom framone of the three

‘comes nigh, Ygedrasil
wolf or steed that will

the Wyld), Mimir Honor and the Weaver), and
Hvergelmir (the Of Glory and the Wyrm). During the
night of Samhain, the Get make a pilgrimage deep into the
Umbra to reach one or more of these wells. Itis sometimes said
that Yggdrasil exists at the center of the Get's Homeland, but
others say the tree exists in a realm all its own. Regardless, the
ritemaster must successfully seek out a well or suffer the sept's
wrath and great personal shame. Upon reaching a well, the
Get are always faced with a challenge. The nature of the
challenge varies, although combat is common (especially at
Hvergelmir). Ifthe Get overcome the challenge they may look
into the waters of the well and catch glimpses of their indi-
vidual fates, the fate of the tribe, and of the world as of that
moment.


(a

Upon their return, the Get quickly go over any images they
have glimpsed within the wells, and the elders interpret their
meaning. There is little if any squabbling over the interpreta-
tions, for the Get do not waste time on such things. Fate is the
Fates, and elders whoare nearer to their inevitable embrace are
best at knowing the minds of the fates.

System: If the ritemaster fails the roll, the tribe will be
unable to locate the World Ash Tree. Two successes indicate
the ability to find two of the wells, and three or more means the
sept may journey to any or all of the wells. A botch means the
ritemaster leads the sept into a very dangerous place in the
Umbra where they are attacked by spirits of some sort.

ite of the Wyrm-Eaten (Level Two)

Tribe: Uktena (and Wendigo Ghost Dancers)

Time: Thanksgivings in the United States and Canada

The Rite of the Wyrm-Eaten is a relatively brief rite filled
with ironic poignancy. Taking pladén,the European-Ameri-
cans' day of Thanksgi ay trayal as the Uktena
and Wendigosometii i rite isastark reminder

esenting all of Gaia's great

were touched by the Wyrm's fatimt. Focusing the energies of the

plunges her claws into the fatted pig or another piece of meat.
Ripping it open, she stares at the entrails, as their condition is
said to speak of the condition of the Pure Lands. In recent years
rot and maggots have all too often greeted the ritemaster's
efforts.

Regardless of the condition of the food (for any of the food
reflects the level of Wyrm taint), the Garou each take a bite
from every dish so that they may eat of their Mother's pain and
better understand her ills. So far, there have always been a few
dishes untouched by corruption, but the rot discovered at the
feast has been increasing in recent decades, and this greatly
concerns the Uktena.

System: Any Garou who participates in a successful Rite of
the Wyrm-Eaten receives a -1 difficulty level modifier for any
rolls to detect evidence of Wyrm taint. This benefit lasts for
one lunar month following the rite. If the rite botches any
Garou participating become violently ill from the taint, and
receive a +1 difficulty to all Physical rolls for the following
lunar month.

Sky Hunts (Level Three)

Tribe: Stargazers

Time: Any lunar eclipse

All major astrological concolations are important to the
Stargazers, but the lunar eclipses have special importance to
this tribe. During such eclipses; many Stargazers embark on a
rite known as a Sky Hunt. Asjin many things, the Stargazers
differ from their brethren Garg: when jt comes to tribal rites.

the Stargazer wills herself to do likewise.

She moves out of her body into the mirror, and from there
into what some members of the World Tree camp refer to as
the Astral Plane, or the Heavens or Upper World. While
traveling this strange and fluid domain, each Stargazer looks
for the truth in her own way. She can continue her Sky Hunt
until the last shadow slips from the moon's surface, at which
time she finds herself back in her body. Except for a certain
number of the World Tree camp, the Stargazers are unable to
enter this revelatory aspect of the universe except during the
time of the Sky Hunts.

System: Stargazers who successfully complete this rite
actually enter the Astral Plane (or the Astral Umbra) for the
duration of the rite eclipse. Their physical bodies remain
behind, thus they may travel to places normally inaccessible to
the Garou. If the rite is botched the Garou separates from her
body but is unable to enter the Astral Umbra. Such a Garou
is trapped until someone covers the reflective surface used in
the rite. Stargazers have been known to become forever lost in
such situations, their bodies dying while their spirit lives on. It
is a terrible thing, since they may not be reclaimed by Gaia
until they find a way to return to their bodies and true death.

More details on the Astral, or Upper, World can be found
in Mage sourcebooks.

On the Importance of
Being Renowned

By Sam Chupp

Asa Storyteller, you
ways: as a reward, Storytelling
element — all vali ecHanism, Renown
exists in order to k ‘ters from gaining power
too rapidly, to allenge and a goal to achieve.
Since even a, from one level to the next
means suc!
before yor
Renown And advancement and make this information
known to your players.

jown in many

You may, for example, choose to make Renown only a
minor part of your chronicle: you tell the players ahead of
time that they'll be playing Rank one (or two, or whatever)
Garou for the entirety of the chronicle, plain and simple.
This frees you in many ways, but it still requires you to
supply some other reward or punishment system to commu-
nicate to the players that they are doing things well or
executing plans poorly.

On the other hand, your chronicle could be about how
asmall pack of callow cubs rises to elder status by participat-
ing in a series of wild and glorious adventures which make

Si

them known throughout the Garou Nation. Whatever
your initial decision, you need to make your players aware
of the role you expect Renown to play in your stories so they
can anticipate when they'll receive their ultimate reward:
new Gifts, fetishes and the new-found respect that comes
with Rank.

As a reward for good behavior, Renown is perfect for
channeling your players into doing the things that you feel
their Garou characters should be doing. Ultimately, your
main rule of thumb in assigning Renown points is that you
should look not only at how it will affect the character you
are upgrading, but also at what you are encouraging the
player to do by giving them this Renown. If you would
prefer the Garou characters to be political and scheming,
reward them with Glory and Honor and Wisdom when
they are politicking in the court of Lord Morningkill. If
you'd like them to be monkeywrenching, reward them
when they go after the Pentex affiliate in town and when
they link in with Gaia Net.

Your players will have to learn how to tailor their actions
to get the Renown that they deserve. Many players do not
like playing characters that don't have at least a hint of a
chance to rise in Rank; nobody likes to be ina dead-end job.

The best use of Renown, however, to is to make it part
of the story. Let's say you tell the players that they'd get
more Renown if they had a Galliard to represent them
during the moots and at the Galliard Moon Circles —
instantly, the group finds a story element which will pro-
vide a nice subplot for several sessions: finding a Galliard
and adopting him into the pack. Another story idea is that
the players know of a Garou who is skyrocketing in Renown
and Rank — much more so than normal. Your pack may
decide to investigate this superstar Garou and try to dis-
cover the secret of his success: perhaps he is genuinely a
great Garou, but it is also possible that the Wyrm has
something to do with his rapid growth and success.

Remember that Renown is not just a list of checkmarks
on the character sheet: it represents the stories and songs

* told about the character around the moot fires, the amount
of, fleeting — or enduring — fame the character has
_-achieved for an action. An entire game session can involve
the retelling and acting out of these tales of dashing Glory,
unwavering Honor and crafty Wisdom.
= The Storyteller decides which actions of the characters
— which stories — get propagated throughout the Garou
Nation. Soon, characters may hear epithets added to their
names from their Renown stories: "Hello, Maximilian
> Tron-Claw!" or "Hey there, Mall-Walker!" Renown stories
are wonderful examples of Garou culture at its finest, and
that is where the power of Renown truly comes into play:
Garou become living myths and legends, re-playing out
ancient stories and ancient problems — all of the stories
recorded and sung by the Galliards.

|


Having the players tell these stories themselves before
the "fire" is great fun. This style of Narrative Renown —
rewarding Renown around how well a player tells of his
character's exploits — can be great fun. You may even be
lucky enough to have a musical player who happens to also
play a Galliard; if so, get her to compose some songs and
perhaps the pack can spend some time during the game
listening to them. There is nothing finer than hearing your
character's name sung in proper Garou praise.

Don't let this hurt players, however. Not everyone is a
performer, and many roleplayers don't like being on center
stage. Use Narrative Renown toadd to the fun of rewarding
Renown, but don't let it get out of hand and unbalance the
troupe.

Of course, if you use Narrative Renown, you mustn't
forget that there is such a thing as ignominy. Galliards tell
scornful or even humorous tales of characters' misadven-
tures on a regular basis. Such tales are extremely popular
among the Garou, even more popular than the great tales
of Honor. Many are the Garou who have tried to intimidate
a Galliard into not telling a tale of ignominy; it's up to you
as a Storyteller to decide whether or not you allow this to
occur.

For more information on whata Narrative Renown story
may be like, take a look at the Werewolf short story
anthology, Drums around the Fire, which has many tales
of Renown in it. Also, Narrative Renown lends itself well
to Live-Action roleplaying, as in The Apocalypse, Live-
Action Werewolf.

You must keep Renown in mind at all times as your
players move their characters through the story you've
created. Even though another Garou may not be around
when the pack leader curses out the Silver Fang elder, you
should knock off a few Honor points just because the spirits
in the area would have heard and perhaps whispered this
report to spirit-keepers in the sept. You may wish to decide
to be generous with temporary Renown but extremely tight
with permanent.

Whatever you decide, you may bring Renown into full
flower in your games by making sure you are paying atten-
tion to the affect it has on your players' roleplaying, your
own Storytelling and the story that you're running. Re-
nown should never usurp the process; instead, it should be
an extra color in your palette, a color you use to bring a
deeper shade or texture to the game canvas.

Scent of the Invisible
World

By Dan Greenberg

There is a world beyond that of the conscious mind and
senses of humans. It exists in both the mundane and the
Umbra. It's a universe informed not only by color and
sound, but by the pungent descriptions and complex illus-
trations written in odors. The smells of both the physical
and the spiritual world create a vast, silent, invisible layer
of information imbedded in the land. Bold, powerful, om-
nipresent odors blanket the landscape like heavy fog and
dominate the horizon. But softer, subtler smells must be
carefully coaxed out of the terrain by a cunning nose and
careful investigation of the area. Garou often lead with
their noses when following a trail. Whether in Homid or
Lupus or any form in between, they dash madly over the
area, sniffing every bush and water cooler, seeking delicate
traces of smells and rooting out indications of previous
contact. They trust delicate, half-perceptible smells of the
quarry over overt signs of recent passage. Seen changes can
be faked. The smell information rarely can.

Creating this utterly alien landscape isa major challenge
for Storytellers, who lack the requisite sens

© to paint a
picture of an olfactory world. Here isa guide for Storytellers
who seek to bring this potent sense into their Werewolf
games.

Chapter Three: Setting

[RO nn

Smells of the Natural

Werewolves are steeped in the primal senses of their wolf
kin. For Garou, smells are a potent source of knowledge
about the world

en humans, with their very limited sense of smell,

have powerful reactions to certain odors. Scents bypass 2

person's developed brain and shoot directly to the part of
the brain that stores memories, where powerful recollec-
tions and associations are instantly triggered. Smells conjure
up primal emotions the way that no other senses can.
Human scientists barely understand the murky world of
pheromones — chemical markers that have a profound

subconscious effect on the ways humans interact.

For animals such as wolves, scents describe a world of

constantly shifting territorial markers and domin

ance-
submission relationships. The strong social bonds between
‘e enforced by scent. All wolves know one

pack membe
another by their scent, and the Alpha makes sure that the
scent of his urine and feces is omnipresent in the pack
encampment. This helps him keep order and promote pack
cohesion.

When the pack is on the move, the Alpha regularly
deposits his urine and feces on conspicuous objects along

the trail. Subordinates are expected to leave their wastes in

inconspicuous areas. By smelling the dominant objects ina
field, other members of the pack can locate the Alpha's
familiar scent and follow the route. Wolves can communi-

53


Sree cera rane caren ner. va ry aa rem mnarremamnerenseh

cate in a limited fashion through these spoor deposits,
which last fora long time. They use them to maintain their
territory against outsiders as well as to communicate within
the pack.

Smells of the Supernatural

The Garou have all the olfactory sophistication of their
wolf kin, and more. Like wolves, they have none of the
revulsion to smells that affects humans. They don't object to
"bad" organic smells such as feces and rotting food. In smells
that most humans find vile and nauseating, the Garou find a
wealth of fascinating and thoroughly enjoyable information.
The smells the Garou find unpleasant are antiseptic chemical
smells, heavy perfumes and, of course, the many scents of the
Wyrm. The hypersensitive hearing of wolves and dogs can be
a source of pain and actual damage when the animals are
exposed to powerful sounds that are too high for humans to
hear. Likewise, a hypersensitive sense of smell leaves the
Garou vulnerable to overpowering chemical smells. Ammo-
nia, pesticide and most solvent odors are so repellent and so
overwhelming that Garou are almost physically driven away
by them. The more intelligent agents of the Weaver and
Wyrm know this and drench their headquarters with solvents
that are only mildly annoying to most humans, but are
physically distressing to the Garou.

Like wolves, the Garou enforce order in their hierarchy of
dominance and submission through scent. They leave their
powerful pheromones along trails and use them to mark their
territory. This odoralone is strong enough to unnerve humans,
who sometimes feel tremors of the Delirium when they smell
it. It is powerful enough to frighten away animals, who know
it signifies a powerful, supernatural presence. When a Garou
defeats another leader, or takes over after the death ofanother,
she sprays the old leader's territory, fetishes and possessions
with her urine and feces to claim them by scent.

Besides marking territory and leaving trails, Garou use their
pheromones to leave encoded messages for their allies in a
private language that they communicate through scent. They
can communicate simple concepts — danger, help, caern,

Antiseptik

This colorless solvent with a powerful antiseptic
smell was developed by Pentex to help guard their sites
from Garou incursions. It is used three ways — sprayed
over an area, heavily coating an area, or concentrated.
Garou who smell it must make a Willpower roll against
its stench. If the Antiseptik has been lightly sprayed

over an area, as in facilities that are of limited impor-
tance to Pentex, the difficulty is 3. If it coats the walls,
as it does in Pentex inner sanctums, the difficulty is 6. If
the Garou smells it in raw, undiluted form, the difficulty
is 9. If the roll fails, the Garou suffers a -2 penalty from
all Dice Pools. On a botch he runs away, gagging, and
stays away for at least five minutes.

54 Werewolf Storytellers Handbook

victory, Wyrm, spirit, tribe — and simple location clues, for
instance North of thismountain. Individual packscreate scent
languages in order to leave messages for one another. Some
septs create private scent languages as well. This language
cannot be used to make complex sentences. Heavy rainfall can
obliterate the markers, but short messages can retain their
meaning for weeks.

Garou can also leave markings in the Umbra. The spirit
world is conducive to this sort of communication, and Garou
can leave messages that are more complex than is possible in
the physical world. Their messages can communicate simple
sentences and refer to individuals known to both the "speaker"
and the audience. These messages do not fade with time, and
last indefinitely unless they are deliberately obscured or de-
stroyed by a natural Umbral element, such asa storm ora lava
flow. Garou have made pilgrimages into the Umbra to smell
the messages left by Garou heroes long since deceased.

Reading and Writing in
Smells

Leaving a message in odor requires a Manipulation +
Primal-Urge roll against a difficulty of 4 in normal condi-
tions and 7 in difficult conditions (rainfall, snow). To read
the message, the smeller must roll a Dice Pool of Perception
plus the number of successes the writer gained while leav-
ing the message (Per + writer's successes); the difficulty is
normally 5, but this can worsen with weather conditions.
This system requires that the Storyteller keep track of the
pungency of each message. Garou can rewrite messages if
they feel the message is not clear enough. Each attempt
takes three minutes.

Painting Pictures in Odors

Storytellers can describe whole new worlds by using the
language of smell. Odors can add a new dimension to the
game. Adding sense information is evocative and creates
images in the players' minds. In any roleplaying game, as
well as in any story, symbols are far more powerful than
straightforward facts. Indirect information paints pictures
of greater power than facts because the reader or player's
imagination fills in many more details than words can
describe. This is especially true of descriptions written in
odors.

For example, instead of saying "You smell Meat Pup-
pets," a Storyteller can paint their presence by saying "You
smell a delicate, fresh-scrubbed-baby-skin scent laced with
the sour essence of rotting meat." This evokes the essential
nature of Meat Puppets even more than the name can, and
yet leaves open a bit of mystery about what the creature
really is. Even after the players are aware of this olfactory
description of Meat Puppets, the vivid description can be
chilling — especially when the Garou smells rotting meat
first, and then realize that it is tinged with the odor of
innocence.

Chapter Three: Setting 55


|

If | never see the "Glory of Gaia" again, it will be far too
soon. And I still say the Red Talon are ignorant savages
living in the Stone Ages. Maybe I'll move to Alaska; they
kill wolves there, don't they?

Survival is basic, but not a need that many Garou are
prepared to handle. There is more to survival than simply
packing the proper camping gear; the basic needs of exist-
ence cannot be fully supplied by a tent or from a backpack.
Fresh water can be very hard to find, and a great number of
people have suffered the consequences of drinking water
that tasted just fine but held toxins. The first important rule
about drinking water in the wilds is to pick a supply of water
that is moving. Still waters may run deep, but they are often
in the first stages of stagnation and can carry some of the
same bacteria that are responsible for food poisoning. Most
Garou can survive these poisons, but they are likely to suffer
from debilitating stomach cramps and even a severe fever.

However, just finding a running stream is not enough.
There are several types of plants that are toxic when
consumed, and certain portions of host streams carry the
poisons that the trees and plants exude. A large dose of one
of the poisons can be fatal. Even in mild doses the toxins
can cause great discomfort and a slow lingering death.

One example of a poisonous water plant is the water
hemlock; the roots of water hemlock hold the poisons, and
even small doses will cause illness. Normally the plant itself
must be consumed to cause harm, but in fast moving waters
where the plant is often found, a diluted form of the poison
ches into the waters as a natural side effect. If the plant
as been damaged in severe rains or by a careless accident,
the toxicity is substantially increased and is deadly enough
to paralyze and perhaps kill even a Garou.

Shelter

Microchip's Journal, Day 4:

It rained last night, a torrential downpour if there ever was
such a thing. Before the storm was through, my tent had
collapsed under its own sogey weight, and the clothes on my back
were stuck to me like a second skin. I think if the rains had come
earlier, | would have defected from my tribe on general prin-
ciples. Man has designed conveniences to defeat the elements,
and I am very much aman or, if you prefer, a homid. But the
last three days have been something of an eye opener for me; |
had forgotten just how refreshing a long hike could be. Perhaps
my jogging time in the office gymnasium has dulled my senses.
I can see so much out here that I've been taking for granted, and
the moon is so bright away from the city's lights.

Another problem of surviving in the wilderness is shel-
ter. Most of the heavily forested areas are easily
accommodating, but dangers still exist. For lupus Garou,
shelter is found in a good warren or a comfortable area
between a few strong trees. But for the homid Garou there
is the matter of knowing which areas are safe and which are
deceptively safe.

56 Werewolf Storytellers Handbook

OEE TE TE a Ty

Recreational vehicles are often used by humans for
roughing it, but they are not likely to squeeze into the
woods or down a dirt path very easily. If the campers' plans
are for the wide open spaces, then they'll be okay. But
otherwise, the RV is of little use.

Most homid Garou depend on modern day conveniences
to make their lives easier, more as a matter of upbringing
than out of any actual need. The taint of civilization has left
too many city-born Garou unwilling to trust their instincts.
Glass Walkers and Bone Gnawers both suffer from a strong
urge to resist their lupine instincts and survive on their wits.
One of their big mistakes stems from believing that a tent
will keep the wilderness at bay.

Tents work well enough in most cases but hold little
hope of keeping out the aroused forces of nature. A tent will
easily collapse under the onslaught of rain and wind in a
heavy storm, and as most experienced campers can tell you,
they have a tendency to leak if the sides are touched during
a downpour. A hidden problem with tents is that they are
often not nearly as large as the labels lead campers to
believe. A 10-person tent will only sleep 10 ifall agree to lie
perfectly still throughout the night and leave the majority
of their gear outside. A safer bet is that this tent will hold
six comfortably.

Placing a tent properly can also prove a difficult task.
The ground in the forest is almost never level, and when it
is fairly level there are almost never any trees to assist in
anchoring the tent more securely. Most campers tend to
stay in areas designed by humans to accommodate camping
gear more easily, where the dangers are minimal, or at least
mostly human made.

Many of the Uktena and Wendigo Garou are more
knowledgeable in surviving in the wilderness, primarily as
aresult of their upbringing. While some Uktena are willing
to concede the uses of modern day camping equipment, few
of the Wendigo would ever be caught using a nylon tent
instead of the more traditional trappings from their heri-
tage.

Lean-to's are also fairly common for purposes of camping
in the woods. This simple construction of branches, twine
or ivy and woven grass or cured skins is easily built with a
little patience and know-how. Lean-to's are literally walls
built out of the forest's supplies and then attached to a
strong tree or placed between two trees for simple shelter
against the worst of nature's elements. Likewise, the more
complex tipi can be built, but the level of skill necessary for
construction is much higher, and they are meant to remain
in one place for an extended amount of time, not to be
assembled and torn down in short periods.

Inone form oranother, almost all campers come equipped
with the ability to make fire. Fire is essential for cooking
meats (if that is a homid's preference), lighting the area,
and in some cases, for sterilizing water so that it can be
consumed with less risk. While campfires are still common,
another safer alternative for lighting is gas lamps. Gas lamps
range in size from small hand held lanterns to lanterns large


enough to light a 100-yard radius. The advantages of gas
lamps is that they are controllable, easily lit, easily doused
and less likely to cause forest fires. The disadvantages are
that they are moderately fragile and require reserves of fuel
to burn. Gas powered stoves are also available, and suffer
from the same disadvantages and advantage as the lamps.
Gas stoves are seldom light enough to carry with any real
ease.

Campfires are responsible for an enormous number of
forest fires, One careless person is all that is necessary to
burn down hundreds of acres of forest land during the dry
seasons. Too many people believe that a simple barrier of
stones at the base of the fire is enough to make the area safe,
but the majority of softer woods are filled with oily resins
that can explode and send sparks into the nearby trees and
underbrush. Additionally, the coals from a campfire can
burn unnoticed for hours or even days after the fire is "out."
Proper and judicious use of water and dirt, to bury the
remains of a campfire are necessary to protect Gaia's do-
main.

Human-Made Dangers

Microchip's Journal, Day 8:

I cannot believe the insensitivity of some people. I came across
acampsite this morning, one that had been abandoned for at least
a week, Perhaps that thunderstorm earlier in the week was a
blessing, because the damned fools had not extinguished their
campfire properly. The trees in the area all show scorch marks

from the start of what could have been a serious fire. The
underbrush is all gone, and in its place I found at least a dozen
empty beer cans. Can't these idiots take a few minutes to make
certain that they leave the forests intact? How difficult can it be?
I swear if I could have captured their scents I would have tracked
them down and torn their throats out! I found an eagle's nest in
the area, the mother and her hatchlings all dead because some
stupid bastards couldn't be bothered to clean up and make
certain their fire was completely out

Does that sound as much like a Red Talon as I think it does?
Well, maybe they are not without their own form of wisdom after
all. More later; I have to move on now.

Garou should always respect the natural environment.
Even more, they should go out of their way to protect the
few remaining places untainted by the Wyrm. Now and
then, the characters might need reminding; as with every-
thing else in the World of Darkness, the reminders should
be harsh. Glass Walkers and Bone Gnawers have become
accustomed to a certain level of pollution in the city. They
might not think to remove all of the remains from last
night's meal, or they might not care one way or the other.
Other Garou should be swift to point out their errors

The litter and waste of a few humans and homid Garou
is hardly enough to cause the ecosystem to collapse, but the
added weight of countless thousands doing the same thing
constantly does have a strong impact. Disposal does not
take care of itself, and nature is not equipped to deal with

57


human's plastics and glassware. Many of man's modern
conveniences simply are not biodegradable. Long after the
cola is drained from a bottle, the bottle will still be there.
Most of the less militant lupus Garou tolerate the idea of
using plastics and other recyclable materials — barely, but
they will — but they should not tolerate the refuse of
homids in the woods. Humans have already built their scabs
and garbage heaps, let them keep their filth in their own
dens.

Aside from the near invulnerability of plastics and glas
ware, these simple objects have a few surprise side effects
that can prove detrimental. Too many curious animals
have died slowly as a result of unwittingly trapping them-
selves in plastic bonds that will not break, and the sun
running through glass at the proper angle can and does
cause forest fires. While paper and cardboard products are
not as hazardous, the lupus still look on these things as
products of humans, and therefore unclean.

The most severe human-made dangers awaiting
uncautious Garou are the many traps laid by humans to
ensure the easy capture of prey. Steel bear traps and rope
nooses are not just annoying, they maim and kill with little
difficulty. And they are indiscriminate — they will wound
with equal efficiency whatever comes across their path.
Hunters, once spotted, can be avoided, but hunters make
noise and stink of humanity. One good rain, however, will
remove all odor froma trap, and some traps are forgotten by
the fools who place them in the woods.

Werewolf Storytellers Handbook

Natural Dangers

Microchip's Journal, Day 12:

I've never seen such a sight. I wish that I could adequately
explain what I felt when the tornado hit near me. The storm was
brewing, and I had just managed to pitch my tent ina reasonably
comfortable area when the wind just stopped. There was nothing
at all to hear, except my own breathing. Then the twister came
down. Out of nowhere there was this horrible howling, and for
a second I thought I'd found another black bear's resting place
and that I was going to have to fight for the right to stay

It was all so fast, one second I was next to my tentand the next
my tent was lifting into the air and sailing away into the night
I think if I'd been in anything but the Crinos, I would be gone
now. I've never run so fast in my life. I saw trees as old as the
United States Government tom from the ground and flung aside
as if they didn't matter in the least. I am certain that only Gaia's
kindness saved me from death. There are things out here that
make the strongest of Garou weak in comparison. I would
sooner face a pack of rabid Get of Fenris than deal with another
tornado. One tends to forget just how powerful the Wyld is in its
own right.

Still, it was exhilarating. I wouldn't have missed it for the
world. I'm just glad I had my Powerbook in my hands when it
hit, or I'd be writing this on bark.

Nature holds several types of destruction that humans
have, fortunately, been unable to duplicate. Despite the
best efforts of people to conquer and control Gaia, she
refuses to surrender gracefully. Thunderstorms, tornadoes


and hurricanes are all capable of devastating forests and
cities alike. They are equal opportunity destroyers capable
of unparalleled damage. They are also a part of nature that
cannot be ignored in the wilderness. Mankind is able to
predict with a certain amount of accuracy when the forces
of nature are about to go wild, thus allowing many people
to prepare themselves for the worst affects of violent storms.
But the forest has another story entirely. Campers in the
deep woods have very little access to information except in
the form of radio communications, and for a radio to
function, there has to be a source of power. Constant use of
modern day batteries will drain them in fewer than 15
hours, and before they are completely drained they lose the
ability to receive weaker signals. Additionally, mountains
and valleys often block the strongest signals, even when the
batteries are freshest.

Other assaults from nature are no less dangerous. What
seems like a nice little downpour can often lead to flash
flooding in the valleys and in some cases over an entire
region. The only escape from severe floods is to be else-
where when they hit. Earthquakes can last from a few
second to a few hours, and the stronger ones are capable of
leveling the best-built structures known to humans. Even
areas that are not well known for earthquakes are still
susceptible from time to time, and no region in the United
States is entirely without a tectonic fault line.

The western coast of the United States is not only
known for earthquakes, but also has a very long expanse of
dormant, but active, volcanoes running from Canada as far
down as the lower portions of California. There is nothing
that can stop an earthquake or volcano, and the best
detection devices of today can still not predict with any
degree of accuracy when an earthquake will happen or a
volcano will erupt. The certainty is that earthquakes will
continue, and volcanoes will eventually awaken. Ironi-
cally, the forests and woods are probably a safer location
thanare the cities during major quakes. Trees tend to stand
the force of tremors better than buildings, and there are
very few bridges that could collapse on you deep in the
woods.

Earthquakes or volcanic eruptions in the oceans depths
can also cause tidal waves, walls of water that move with
immense force, crushing buildings, people and Gaia's chil-
dren upon landfall. Once on the move, there is little save
sufficient solid land that can stop a tidal wave's forward
motion.

The easiest natural attacks to forget are still some of the
most devastating; droughts and floods may take longer to
kill creatures but they still cause major damage when they
occur. Heavy flooding can destroy the soils necessary to
anchor a tree, and droughts can starve the same tree of life-
giving water. Perhaps the worst part of a drought is that it
often leaves an area devoid of its natural defenses against
fire and vulnerable to massive fires that are carried by the

wind and an actually spread for hundreds of miles if left
unchecked.

There seems to be no rhyme or reason to the events
brought on by nature, at least none that humans can
fathom.

Some Garou claim otherwise, pointing out that the
largest earthquakes seem intent on causing massive damage
to the worst of the human's scabs, and noting aloud that
tornadoes have a penchant for trailer parks. Volcanoes
often bring desperately needed nutrients back to the soil in
areas where starvation for plant life was a certainty. Fire
kills the forests with wild abandon but leaves behind a layer
of ash that, again, adds nutrients to the soil and provides a
strong foundation for new growth. Many Garou claim that
the natural disasters are simply Gaia's way of cleaning
house, removing the litter and making certain that all is
cleansed of pollutants.

Hurricanes, tidal waves and floods often seem attracted
to areas where humans dwell, and that suits most Garou
very well. Nature is persistent, and in time all that is wild
returns anew. All, that is, save what humankind has de-
stroyed. Aside from the Garou, the forces of nature that
humankind so fears are all that stand against the tide of the
Wyrm's corruption. While wary of being caught by Gaia's
weapons, the werewolves understand their need, and ac-
cept their inevitability.

Hunting

Microchip's Journal, Day 15:

T have been hungry, and I have lost a great deal of my softer
flesh, replacing it with muscles I had allowed to grow lax. I have
feasted today. After three days without food, I finally broke
down and gave in to my instincts. | do not understand what I was
afraid of , but I pray I never grow afraid again. I have stalked and
chased down my first kill, a wild boar that gave me more of a fight
than I ever expected.

My ribs still hurt from where his tusks tore into me, and my
legs still hurt from his first charge. I have never before felt so free.
Somehow, the battle against a worthy foe made the meat
sweeter, and even without a fire to cook his flesh, that boar's
meat is the finest meal I have ever had, his blood the sweetest
wine to ever pass my lips. A pack of wolves in the area joined me
in my feast, and I let them. There was a part of me that I had
forgotten, a part that wanted to fight for the meat and stop then
from sharing in my repast. I held it back, but only because I was
so lonely after so long, and | desperately needed the company
they provided, if only for one night.

Evenwith the ability to become a wolf myself, | had forgotten
how beautiful the wolves are and how noble they can be. I think
they wanted me to join their pack. I'm almost scared by how
enticing the offer was. Still, | know that a true union with them
is all but impossible. Iam merely a Garou, and they are so much
more. Damn the Wyrm for corrupting so many of the humans,
and praise be to Gaia for protecting so many of her creatures
from his influence. The moon is full, and my throat is sore from
howling my sorrow to the Lady. Iam so very happy; | am so very
sad.

As important as water is food, the necessary fuel that
allows a being to continue without consuming itself for
sustenance. In the city the food is easy, ifat times unappeal-
ing, to find. But in the woods the search for food can be long
and difficult. Wolves tend to consume as much food as
possible, preparing for the chance that there will be no
further food for extended periods. Garou can do thisas well,
but few of homids understand the need. While Garou are
omnivorous and can eat virtually any nontoxic plant to
sustain themselves, few of them understand enough of the
ways of nature to know which plants are nutritious and
which are lethal. Most prefer to hunt wild animals and
consume them, giving in to their natural predatory in-
stincts,

Animals

Hunting is not as easy as it may seem, and is made more
difficult if the Garou is using only the natural abilities
provided by Gaia rather than depending on weapons to
achieve success. For many Garou, the thrill of the hunt is
something that is never lost and attempting to hunt with
anything more than their natural abilities would reduce the
excitement

Several examples of animals can be found in Ways of the
Wolf, but few are given as examples of prey. If you want to
add a new level of excitement to the game, try letting the

characters stalk and kill their own dinner.

Wild Boar

Attributes: Strength 3, Dexterity 3, Stamina 4, Perception 2

Abilities: Alertness 2, Athletics 2, Brawl 2, Intimida-
tion 2, Primal-Urge 2, Survival 3

Attacks: Body Slam, then Gore (Str + 1, difficulty 5)

Wild boars are well respected as enemies, primarily
because they are unpredictable in their reactions to danger.
While most will simply attempt to flee from an enemy,
some will turn and fight, especially if they are protecting
their young. Full grown boars, especially the males, are
often aggressive and will attack ifa predator comes too close
for their comfort. Males also bear large tusks which are
capable of rending flesh with the same ease as a wolf's fangs.
Wild Boars are limited in their methods of attack, and will
normally attempt to Body Slam an opponents and then
Gore them with their tusks.

Rabbits

Attributes: Strength 0, Dexterity 3, Stamina |, Percep-
tion 3

Abilities: Alertness 4, Athletics 3, Survival 1

Attacks: Bite (one die of damage)

Rabbits do not fight, rabbits run and dodge and crawl to
any safe spot where a predator cannot reach them with ease.
Just the same, rabbits should not be toyed with; they will

attack if there is absolutely no other option

Hornets

Attributes: Strength 0, Dexterity 2, Stamina 0, Percep-

tion |

Abilit Brawl |

Attacks: Sting (one die aggravated in swarms, no dam-
age singly — but painful nonetheless)

Hornets and other hive insects are not generally consid-
ered food by the Garou, or by much aside from a few of the
larger spiders. They are, however, often found in nests
above and even in the ground. Individually the damage
caused by a hornet is negligible, but hurts a great deal. In
swarms, the hornets get one attack, and cause one level of
aggravated damage (this can be soaked). Hornets and other
similar insects do not believe in surrender, and normally
only attack if they feel threatened or if pheromonically
motivated to protect the hive. If you feel a few players need
a lesson in humility, or if a character botches an attempt to
stalk and kill dinner, you might allow them the opportunity
to meet an angry swarm of hornets. Fire and immersion in
water, aside from certain Gifts, are the only sure ways to
escape a swarm.

The standard rules for hunting are given in the Werewolf
Second Edition rulebook, but if you want to roleplay out
the combat, follow the rules for tracking in the rulebook
(pp. 224-225), and then let the characters attempt to kill
their prey using normal combat rules and the animal Traits
given above


Plants

The Uktena, Wendigo and many lupus Garou are also
knowledgeable in which plants can be used as medicines, and
which can simply provide the necessary nutrients for life.
While many of the plants are common, there are several that
are only useful if the right part is consumed. An example is the
potato; the tubers are vitamin rich and contain the necessary
starches for energy, but the leaves of the plant are a strong
poison and will cause severe stomach cramps, diarrhea and
even death.

Ways of the Wolf provides a substantial list of edible plants
(pp. 47-48; 53), and the Werewolf Player's Handbook
provides examples of what some plants are capable of when
they are awakened by the Rite of Spirit Awakening (pp. 128-
129). The following isa list of plants that are useful for treating
minor ailments. These plants do not need to be awakened, but
some of them do need to be cooked for the best results

Aloe: The sap from aloe plants is effective in treating minor
burns and overexposure to the sun's rays.

Ash Trees: The bark, when cooked in warm water, pro-
duces both a tonic for invigoration and a strong astringent for
cleaning infected wounds.

Balmony: This weed is often used to treat jaundice, worms
and ulcers. The weed may be consumed raw, but is more
effective when cooked.

Beech: The oil from Beech trees nuts is often used as an
expectorant for treating bronchitis and severe colds.

Cowslip: Used asa tea, the flowersand leaves from Cowslip
work to calm muscle spasms and prevent epileptic seizures.

Damiana: When dried and consumed in small doses —
larger doses being potentially unhealthy — Damiana works as
a laxative, a stimulant and as an aphrodisiac.

Garden Nightshade: The leaves of Garden Nightshade
work as a mild pain reliever when boiled in a tea. The berries
are poisonous unless boiled first. After cooking, the berriescan
be consumed for nutrition.

Hydrangea: The dried root is useful for relieving kidney
disorders, and is more effective when boiled to a syrupy
consistency.

Larkspur: The roots and seeds of the Larkspur are effective
in killing parasites and as an insect repellent when used as a
poultice or wash. Larkspur can be toxic if taken internally.

Maple: The inner bark and leaves of Maple trees, when
brewed as a tea, work to clean poisons from the kidneys, and
work externally as a poultice to clean boils.

Skull Cap: Used asa tea brewed from the entire plant, Skull
Cap eases muscle tension and cramping.

There are many other plants thatare useful for minorhealth
problems, and some claims have been made of plants that can
cure cancer if used properly. Several books on herbology,
available either at the public library or in your local bookstore,
can explain the proper uses for plants in the United States and
abroad.

Travel

Microchip's Journal, Day 18:

Thave come to accept that most manmade shoes were never designed
to.accommodate the rough terrain that I have passed through. My shoes
are gone, tom apart by rocks and water alike. All that remains of them
‘ests at the bottom of my knapsack, and that is long devoid of anything
save my Powerbook (thank Gaia for the Gaffling that powers it!) .

Tranacrossapavedroad the other day and for just the briefestmoment
was ata loss for remembering what it was. A part of me was outraged
by theintrusion of so vulgar aline cuttingacross Gaia's skin. I understand
‘now that] was wrongin what I said to Stone-Eater, horribly wrong. For
thatone instant, I think I had an inkling of what all lupus must feel when
they first see the scars left by humans. For that briefest of times, I wanted
to see all the humans destroyed.

Thadalittle trouble eanlierin the day, tryingtocross the Chattahoochee
River. The waters were higher than | expected, and the rain yesterday
assured me that the travel was difficult. If not for my ability to change into
afull Crinos, I doubt that I would have made the distance to the far shore
without at least a strong rope as an anchor. Every challenge I meet is a
leaming experience. I don't think I will ever be able to look at rivers the
same way again. They are so much more than just running water,
especially up here, where the land is almost pure.

Traveling through the wildemess isa task that is often slow and
difficult. Inareas where the trails have already been carved and foot
paths weave between the trees, there is little to worry about. But
the true wilderness is sometimes unforgiving, and one small
mistake can cost a traveler not only days spent recovering, but
sometimes even their life.

Every partofthe United Statesstill hasplaces left where humans

have not removed the risks, and in some cases where the risks are
simply too high for humans to even try. There are thousands of
miles of desert in the United States, and the vast majority of the
desert regions have never truly been explored. The Mojave Desert
is too dry to sustain human life, and only the most adaptable forms
of animal life manage to dwell in what appears to be a wasteland.
The temperatures in the summertime can rise above 120 degrees
Fahrenheit. The sun is unrelenting, and the air so dry that
dehydration isalmost inevitable. Traveling through the Mojave is
effectively like walking in an oven. Walking there is dangerous
even to strong Garou if they do not know which plants contain
enough moisture forsurvival. Evenwithsuch knowledge, exposure
to the intense sunlight and heat can cause severe damage on their
own.
Worse still, some parts of the desert still burn under the shadow
of nuclear testing. The human-made radiation can cause a slow
death from internal hemorrhaging. Best by far to travel the desert
regions in a covered vehicle, even a car.

The mountain regions in the United States are also filled with
risks. During a great portion of the year, heavy snows keep the
mountain burried. Walking where the humans have not at-
tempted to conquer the lands isa dangerous task. In some areas the
snowfall drifts to fill deep canyons with a powdery white illusion of
security; a misplaced step can plummet a careless hiker hundreds
of feet down into a frozen coffin. The mountains often hold tons
of frozen precipitation balanced carefully on sheer cliffs, and even

61


!

small vibrations such as those caused by talking loudly can cause
avalanches. The impact from an avalanche is often enough to
mock a Garou off of her feet, flinging her hundreds of yards down
amountain'sedgeand then burying her ina blinding sheetofsnow.
‘Anyone fully surrounded and encased in snow is likely to suffer
fronva complete loss of direction. The crushing weight ofsomuch
snow can imitate the familiar sensation of gravity, causing the
illusion that up is actually down and vice versa. Once disoriented
by the fall, few people are experienced enough to calmly find their
way back to the surface.

Even in the warmer months, when snow is less frequent and
causes less ofa hazard, the terrain of the mountainscanstill be fatal.
Rocks loosened by the temperature changes from season to season.
and damaged by the wind can fall in imitation of the winter's
avalanches. Rock slides hit with far preater force, and often canty
blade like rocks and fragments with them. Landslides are not as
frequent as avalanches, but they are more lethal, and anyone
exposed to a landslide will certainly suffer broken bones. For a
human, a broken leg in the wildemess is almost certain to bring
death if there are no others to assist in the travel. Even for Garou,
a broken leg may slow them down for short time.

The winds off of mountaintops are normally much fiercer than
the windsnearsea level, and in higher elevations the airis thinner,
accelerate the onset of physical exhaustion among those not
adjusted to the lack of oxygen. Additionally, mountainous regions
are normally very rough terrain, and extra time has to be spent
scaling cliffs or traveling around the obstacles that cannot be
climbed. Sturdy ropes and, often times, special climbing equip-
ment are virtual necessities for traveling through mountainous
regions.

Forests hold their own special threats. Trees that have fallen
down and formed deadfalls often litter the deepest sections of the
forest, andare extremely hazardous toscale. Deep cleftsin the earth
are sometimes hidden beneath years and years of dead leaves and
fallen branches. Both of these obstacles can lead to broken limbs,
and a person lying helpless in the woods could very well starve to
death while surrounded by plenty, simply because a water supply
or food supply is just out of reach.

Serious threats in the forests can be found in the indigenous wild
life. Venomous snakes are found in virtually every section of the
United States, and their bites often cause death. As with many
forms of wildlife, the snakes may simply be protecting themselves
from a perceived threat, but their defenses are often fatal if not
treated immediately. The same threat comes from various spiders
and other arachnidsas well as insects, and in the case of the spiders
can go undetected until it is too late for treatment. Garou are
stronger than humans in nature, and are more resistant to toxins
than most humans. But without the appropriate Gifts, they arenot
entirely immune to the venoms of Gaia's inhabitants. While
steppingonarattlesnakeand being bitten will rarely killawerewolf
as it might a human, the poison can still hurt. (See Poison &
Disease in Ways of the Wolf, pp. 44-46.)

Traveling around or through lakes and streams can also lead to
misfortune. A homid with the appropriate woodcrafting skills
could make a crude raft or even a canoe fora journey, but without
the right skills disaster is almost guaranteed. Disaster does not

62
~~ ————

a 2 eee

necessarily mean death; it can also mean the loss of important
supplies. Anyone without the know-how to survive on what
nature offers is all too likely to suffer the consequences of their
ignorance unless the proper supplies are brought along. The loss of
a medical supply kit could well mean the difference between life
and death should serious injuries occur.

Fast moving currents are often deceptively calm on the surface
and attempting to ford a river is risky in the best conditions.
Slippery rocks orsoft mud can dropa person into the powerful force
ofa river: once unbalanced, it is almost impossible to regain one's
footing. Garouare just as susceptible to drowning as humans; it just
takes them longer to die.

Lakesarenormally safertoadegree, buttherisk oflosingsupplies
is still a serious one, especially if any form of raft or boat is lacking.
Lakes are also miles across, and swimming is not easy work,
especially with a full pack strapped across your shoulders. Clothes,
toocan hinder movement through the water, but, modesty aside,
clothes are sometimes the only protection against minor hazards
such as poison ivy or angry spiders.

Several important Abilities are useful in the wilderness. First
among these is Survival. Without at least a rudimentary knowl-

edge of basic survival skills, serious injury is almost unavoidable.
Primal-Urge is also of importance, and especially so for lupus
Garou. Hunting for food is often an long and draining task,
particularly ifthe prey is capable of running at greater speeds than
the lupus. For similar reasons. Stealth is very important: a Garou
that cannot stalk prey is likely to starve.

New Secondary Abilities

The following Secondary Abilities represent skills that can
most often be resolved with the Survival Skill. They represent
a greater knowledge of specific parts of wilderness survival. A
character with one of these Abilities will be able to perform
actions or know things that other characters — even those
witha good ratingin Survival —would have ahigher difficulty
for or require more successes with.

Wood Lore

Thisisa Talent for lupus characters, a Knowledge for metisand
homid characters.

Wood Lore allows a character to understand the wilderness.
The similarities between numerous types of plants is often intimi-
dating, and knowing thesmall differences between certain fungi or
berriescan mean the difference between lifeand death. Addition-
ally, Wood Lore allows characters to use certain features of plants
forfindingdirection. Forexample, the Spanish Moss thar growson
trees only grows on their northern side, and is a solid useful guide
in lieu of a compass. Wood Lore also allows a character to avoid
certain natural traps, such as quicksand, and to know whether or
not the ice on a frozen pond is strong enough to support a
character'sweight. WoodLoreshouldnotbe mistaken for Herbalism
(Werewolf Players Guide, pg. 34)

* Novice: You can manage to find your way around your
backyard with minimal risks.

** Practiced: You can tell the difference between a mold
spore and a mushroom.

06 Competent: Youcannormally find your wayhome from.
anywhere in the woods, and you know which plants are edible.

© © Expert: You know the safest places to rest when search-
ing for shelter from a storm, and you know how to avoid nature's
little death traps.

about flora and fauna to survive indefinitely in the woods.

Wood Craft (Knowledge)

Wood Craft is the ability to use nature's gifts to build
shelters and even means of transportation. You know which
types of trees are best for building durable housings, and you
know which vines have the best elasticity. In a crunch you
could successfully fashion a bow and arrows, complete with
poisoned tips.

¢ Novice: Youcan builda lean-to, and can avoid using
termite infested wood. You know how to extinguish a camp-
fire.

e Practiced: You could probably carve a decent walk-
ing stick and can start a fire with nothing more than a few
twigs.

eee Competent: You know which vines are best for use
in construction and which trees yield the best wood for your
project. Youknow which plantsaps make the best sealants and
glues.

But the sights were worse than the sounds; the Wyrm was to be found
everywhere. On the outskirts of the city, gases spewed into the sky from
the factories humans built for making their meaningless lives easier. Still,
I passed through the barren suburbs and refused to tum back.

As | walked into the city which jutted into the skyline before me, all
T could see around me was the artificiality and the dirtiness. Around me,
humans sped by in their iron cages on wheels, along their roads that marr
the land. Filth choked the air. I continued onward, walking along the side
of the smaller roads. I already missed my home. There were no fragrant
forests or crystal streams within miles of the place. But I would not quit.
Instead, I continued walking, past the Wyrm-riddled crack houses,
factories, gun stores and fast-food joints, and the Weaver-dominated
shopping malls, banks, office parks and car lots.

T journeyed "down town' into the claustrophobic confines between
the immense towers surrounding me. Around sunset, I was even
accosted by a gang of rabble, which I slaughtered mercilessly. In fact, the
challenge helped me alleviate some of my welling anger. As I wiped the
blood from my hands, I could feel a change in the air. Some presence was
watchingme. The City was watching me. I could feel its eyes on the back
of my neck. Idid not fear it, but it bothered me for the rest of the night and
I could not stop thinking about it. Looking up at the steel and glass teeth,
hoping to look into the eyes of the city, I could not help but feel the
overpowering unnaturalness of the place.

Thad planned to sleep in the z00 that night, but I could not. The scent
ofdeath and lost hope filled the air and the hollowness in my wolfbrothers'
and sisters' eyes hurt me too much. I would have freed them, but I could
see they had forgotten how to be wild. They would die in their prison,
curiosities to be gawked at by the smart monkeys who put them there.

Lfmally found myself a suitable place in the park, where I would not
be bothered. I tried to rest, but the images of the wolves haunted me inmy
nightmares and the ghastly glow of the city by night pained my tired, red
eyes. In the distance I saw a Bone Gnawer wandering from trash can to
trashcan, scroungingfor leftover Wyrm food. Humans would have seen
him as just another bum, but no humans were present in the park after

nightfall. I stalked the Garou for an hour before I left it alone and tried
sleeping again. The Urrah never once sensed me.

The next moming | awoke to the sounds of humans scurrying about.
For what reason I still cannot understand.

Itseems they force themselves to go to other places to do things they do
not want to do, serving the Weaver, so they can gain money to spendon
items made by the Weaver. And there are others who do the same, but
allin the service of the Wyrm. They have forgotten how to be free. It was
insane just watching them scurrying about. Instead of enjoying their
shallowlives, they wallow in self-pity , become "stressed-out," spend their
time racing to acquire more Weaver products and power over other
humans. Even when they are notworkingthey aredisgusting. They work
so hard they are too tired to play when they get the chance. Instead, they
sitin front of their televisions absorbing Wyrm and Weaver propaganda.
Butenoughof that... AsI said, thenextmoming, forthe entireday really,
the humans moved from place to place packing the streets.

I spent the day trying to track down my prey. Her Kin Fetch had
brought me to the city, but with all the sensory overload, pinpointing her
proved difficult. Itwas night before I found the young Garou. Hername
was Sheila, and she was workingasa topless waitress inastripclublocated
between a tattoo parlor and a liquor store. The club, known as the Black
Angel, was filled with perverted human males watching naked females
conwulse to "music," which sounded to me like groaning metal and

I drew the girl to me with fifty dollars and my own Gift of Persuasion.
After she got off work, we spent the night together talking about her life
so far and what her new life would be like. I explained to her the wonders
she had yet to behold and how she would one day be a great warrior. She
listened nervously and finally asked me to leave. She said she wouldnever
leave the city. Even if I was telling the ruth. City was too important to
her life, to her own goals and dreams of becoming an actress.

I could not understand. The sewage, the television, the guns. Hiding
inahole called an apartment surrounded by humans who would kill her
for no reason. Eating Wyrm food, breathing in diseased filth which
humans called air. Reveling in the perversity of city life. Bathing in the
stench of humans. Forever without a forest to hunt in. Forever removed
from Gaia' s voice. Howcould she notfeel the same Haranoas that which
was already mounting in me.

T could have just kidnapped her, but I didnot. When I used my Gifts
upon Sheila, | could tell she had already been comupted by the Wyrm.
Her heart had grown as ice cold and empty as those of the humans she
had lived with all her life. All she had ever known was violence, pain and
empty pleasure. She was not really one of us. I knew what I had to do.

The body was never found.

As I tumed my back from that place and made my wary back to my
sept, I knew I leamed a great lesson — I do not belong in the city. Itis
too bad we cannot begin the Impergium anew...
