The Piper

Heard the piping, have you? Across the far hills to the North,
beneath the Ragabash Moon? Beware, young one; the Piper, the
Rage-Thief, dances these lands again! Its melodious song catches the
ear of unsuspecting Garou, then leads them into a wild dance from
which they awaken trapped in their breed form for days, weeks, or
sometimes months...

No, child, it is not of the Wyrm, at least not as we know the
Wyrm. Some old songs call it fey, while others speak of the bog-
master's daughter, drowned for loving a Fianna. The only one I've
know who'd seen the thing said that it capered like a spirit but left
footprints in the mud. He knew ghosts and Faerie, Raewellan did;
the Piper, he said, was neither. Since the day he saw it, they say , his
coat's been white as a Silver Fang's.

Explore the North Hills if you must. I'll stay here by the fire, to
sing moum-songs when they find you..

Tolose one's Rage isa terrible thing for Garou. A being that
can steal it with ease would bring more terror than a Black
Spiral hive — Black Spirals, at least, you can fight! The Piper
isa Garou bogeyman of the worst kind; a foe you cannot fight.

The Piper appears as a glowing human flutist — sometimes
aman, other times a woman, still others of indeterminate sex.
The Piper dresses in rags or a hooded cloak or nothing at all.
Its garb will often contradict the season — a heavy cloak on a
hot summer night, total nudity during a blizzard. More often
than not, player packs should only hear the piping, a wistful air
that urges them to dance evenas it chills their blood. The first
time they hear it, the song will not affect them beyond
lingering sadness and curiosity. They may hear it on and off
after that, it will summon up melancholy feelings but no more
than that. If the pack deliberately seeks out the Piper, how-
ever, they will find it...

The pack may never actually see the Piper itself. Its song
precedes it wherever it goes. This song calls to whatever
bittersweet longing each character bears: a lost love, distant
family, fallen comrades or aching shame. The Piper's song
weaves itself around that sadness and tugs at a Garou's inner
self, stealing her Rage while enticing her into a joyless dance
that soon leaves her unconscious and drained.

In game terms, the Piper's song entrances characters, then
forces them to dance while draining both Willpower and Rage
points. The more Rage a werewolf has, the more susceptible to
the Piper's song she is, and the longer its effects linger. Seeking
out the Piper while at war can be fatal.

If the Piper drains a few points, these points recover
normally. If it drains all of a character's Rage and Willpower
points, however, that character must go on a quest of some
kind — some attempt to recover the vital part of herself that
she has lost. Such a quest must be followed in the character's
breed form — she cannot transform again until she has
regained the changing gift.

Werewolf Storytellers Handbook

eee ae /


|

This draining effect steals one Willpower point and one
Rage point per turn until the Garou either breaks the spell or
flees. Characters can resist the urge to dance (and the resulting
drain) by making an extended Willpower roll versus difficulty 8.
The number of successes needed equals their normal Rage.
Characters who succeed can act normally, although the piping
will still draw out their deepest sorrows. Extended exposure to
the Piper's song has been known to cause Harano or worse...
Attacking the Piperonce ithas begun itsdancingsong requires
a Willpower roll against difficulty 8. [fattacked, the Piper fades
away, leaving only the ghost of its song on the wind.

The origins of the Pipershould remain shrouded in folklore,
should contradict each other and should paint a fearsome
portrait. It should provide atmosphere, chilling the players
with its unknown strangeness. Optimally, the Piper should be
overheard while the player pack explores some new territory
or travels through familiar ground on some errand. If the pack
inquires about the Piper, they hear terrible stories but no real
facts. Perhaps they hear of it at a moot, or from some shattered
elder who had a run-in with the thing during a bad time in his
life. These tales might give them pause. Then again, they may
not...

The Pipershould be used to evoke a sense of fearful mystery,
notas an agent of destruction. The Piper isan enigmatic stealer
of Rage, not an unstoppable killing machine. Its nature should
give wise players pause; the wrathful lose both control and
their anger. The Piper does not appear by accident, either. To
find it (and suffer its worst effects), characters must seek it. The
Piper should make the pack feel uncertain, watchful in the
woods and painfully aware of the fleeting glory of their Rage.

The Pumpkin Man

Numerous legends from around the Southeast tell of the
Pumpkin Man, a hideous creature that dwells near pumpkin
patches and thrives on the souls of bad little children. He is
often described as being a very gaunt man, with a jack-o'-
lantern in place of a head. In some regions he is dressed in
antiquated finery; in others he is dressed in rags. In the worst
of apparitions, he is a monstrous fiend whose skin resembles
that of a pumpkin, and whose claws could easily rend steel
asunder.

The Pumpkin Man is very real, and he still punishes the
sinners, even if the sinners are Garou. There are some who
claim he is an associate of Satan, there are others that say he
is a faerie. Whatever the case, he is a relentless hunter who
seldom allows any of his intended victims to escape, even ifhe
must follow them to the ends of eternity.

The Pumpkin Man can take two forms: one humanoid and
one monstrous. It only takes the monstrous form when it is
after truly vile prey. To switch forms, it rolls Stamina + Primal-
Urge against a 7 difficulty.

The Traits are given as follows: humanoid/monstrous

Physical: Strength 5/9, Dexterity 4/7, Stamina 5/8

Social: Charisma 0, Manipulation 0, Appearance 0

Mental: Perception 5, Intelligence 5, Wits 4

Talents: Alertness 5, Brawl 4, Dodge 4, Intimidation 5,
Primal-Urge 3

Skills: Animal Ken 4, Melee 5, Stealth 5, Survival 3

Knowledges: Enigmas 3, Investigation 2, Medicine 5,
Occult 5, Rituals 3

Powers (humanoid): (1) Heightened Senses, Open Seal,
Resist Pain, Resist Toxin, Sense Wyrm, Shroud, Truth of
Gaia; (2) Awe, Curse of Hatred, Sense Guilt.

Powers (monstrous; as fomori powers): Body-barbs, Lash-
ing Tail, Umbral Passage

Garou Gifts (in addition to those in humanoid form): (1)
Razor Claws; (2) Disfigurement, Sense of the Prey, True Fear;
(3) Umbral Sight; (4) Adaptation, Catfeet, Combat Healing,
Disquiet, Mark the Enemy

Also, the Pumpkin Man can regenerate from any injury in
either form, but as a Garou, cannot regenerate and attack
simultaneously. If he is destroyed, his remains melt into the
ground.

Rage 0, Gnosis 5, Willpower 8

Health Levels: OK, -1,-1,-2,-2,-5, Incapacitated (add two
OK levels in monstrous form)

Armor: + 2 soak (only in monstrous form)

Attacks: Silver cane (humanoid form), Claws and Bite
(monstrous form only)

Image: In humanoid form, the Pumpkin Man is tall and
thin, with clothes of rags or ancient finery and a walking stick.
The walking stick has a silver handle.

The monstrous form of the Pumpkin Man is also tall but
hardly lean. In this form the Pumpkin Man is just under 10 feet
in height and has a very athletic build. The creature's skin is
rough and orange, with thorns growing from the body and
limbs. The general form is similar to a Crinos but is designed
more for speed. The mouth is filled with razor-sharp teeth
made for cutting not for chewing. A long tail complete with
still more thorns adds counterbalance when running.

Ecology: The Pumpkin Man exists only to punish the
guilty. He does not need to eat or sleep, and he is always
refreshed and ready toattack. The Pumpkin Man does not give
warning. He simply stalks the guilty and punishes them. Most
are never seen again. The monstrous form of the Pumpkin
Man isa killing machine. It will stalk its victim to the ends of
the earth to destroy the transgressor.

The average punishment always fits the crime: if some-
thing was stolen, then something of equal value is taken
from the thief. If violent crimes were committed, then the
exact same crime is returned upon the attacker. If the crime
was simply not coming to the aid of someone in need, then
the person who has done nothing suffers the same fate as the
one left unaided.

The monstrous form of the Pumpkin Man only appears
to attack multiple foes or enemies that could easily defeat
the manlike form of its other incarnation. There is abso-
lutely no mercy from the creature, and it never leaves its
victims alive. Even destroying the body will only delay the

Wyld-Things

Angelo Costananga sat behind his desk, punching the latest
financial updates into the computer. The last three months had been
like paradise , his investments in the Warburton Land Development
Company had paid back over ten times what he'd invested, and
almost everything he touched seemed ready to tum into gold. Best
of all, he'd been able to convince his backers that sticking with the
natural landscape was a good idea. Gaia was not harmed by the land
development, and the recycling center built nearby was sure to make
a clear profit of over 50 percent by his early reckonings. Life was
good.

When the knock came at his office door, Costananga didn't even
bother to look up, just waved vaguely at the glass panel and finished
his typing. When the voice called to him, he finally managed to tear
his eyes away from the cathode ray tube and stare at the woman in
front of him. The woman called his name, her tone making it a
question, and he nodded. She smiled, and then she changed.

Her lean frame expanded, shifting almost constantly in small
ways. Her pretty mouth grew larger, as did the rest of her face
Where a second before there had been a beautiful young woman, a
brute thing now stood. In some ways it resembled a Garou, but the
fur that grew was quickly replaced by feathers, and they in turn were
quickly buried under scales. The pretty brown eyes were replaced
by orbs that grew and shrank randomly, moving like liquid across the
woman's face. The creature's smile became a snarl, and Angelo felt
his hackles rise in preparation for his own change

"What are you?" he demanded, as his own body started chang-
ing, revealing the cybemetic implants that only showed themselves
when he was in non-Homid form

"Really pissed off," was the reply.

He saw the Glyph glowing beneath her skin and finally under-
stood what he faced. "Oh, hey. It's not like that. I'd never betray
Gaia. I just have a different way of defending her..." the Wyld-
Thing snarled, its body shifting and blurring, changing again and
again as it moved towards him

"You haven't betrayed Gaia. You've betrayed the Wyld. Face
your death, Weaver-spaun..."

The Wyld-Things are extremely rare, and possibly no more
than three exist at a time, but they are also very dangerous.
Wyld-Things are believed to be Wyld-fomori by some Garou;
others don't even hazard a guess. The Wyld-Things do not
really seem to care about Gaia, but only about the Wyld. Some
have stated that they are the Wyld's revenge personified, but
no one really knows for sure. The only certainty is that they
actively hunt any werecreature that does not follow the Wyld.
Bone Gnawers and Glass Walkers are among their favorite
prey, but they've been known toset aside theirarguments with
these Garou in favor of a battle with minions of the Wyrm.

Physical: Strength 7, Dexterity 7, Stamina 6

Social: Charisma 2, Manipulation 1, Appearance (varies)

Mental: Perception 4, Intelligence 2, Wits 5

88

———


Talents: Alertness 5, Athletics 5, Brawl 5, Intimidation 5,
Primal-Urge 5

Knowledges: Animal Ken 5, Stealth 4, Survival 5

Powers: (as fomori powers) Berserker, Extra Limbs, Lashing
Tail, Plasmic Form, Umbral Passage

Rage 10, Gnosis 5, Willpower 6

Health Levels: OK, OK, OK, OK, -1, -1, -2, -2, -5, -5,
Incapacitated

Attacks: Wyld-Things normally just cut loose and attack,
tearing into an opponent and doing their very best to destroy
their targets. They will bite (Strength + 2), claw (Strength +
3) and grow extra limbs to assist in causing as much damage as
possible.

Armor: Wyld-Things can add up to four dice to their soak
rolls by growing scales and thick hide.

Image: Wyld-Things can imitate humans, but there is no
certainty that they ever were human. In their natural state, the
Wyld-Things shift in form constantly, adapting to the forms of
damage inflicted by an opponent and adjusting their form for
whatever is needed. When running they are aerodynamic;
when they wish to fly, they will sprout wings; and when
swimming, they grow sleek and powerful fins. If a creature
belongstothe Wyld, the Wyld-Thing can imitate it. Itcannot,
however, imitate the actions ofany Wyrm or Weaver creature.
Much like Wyld-Spirits, the Wyld-Things are unpredictable
and dangerous. Their motivations are their own.

Ecology: Wyld-Thingsroam constantly, moving from place
to place in search of new prey. They do not appear to have a
gender, and they do not need to eat or even breathe. They do
need to rest from time to time and, like Garou, cannot heal
their wounds without taking time away from combat. Wyld-
Things will not attack lupus Garou, nor will they attack Black
Furies or Wendigo, unless they are attacked first.

Urban Horrors

Urban folklore is known to many of us. Who hasn't heard
thestoriesaboutalligators in the sewers or the lady who bit into
a fried rat instead of the fried chicken she was expecting or the
mouse in the soda bottle? To the more discerning among us,
these stories are seen as what they are: legends passed around
orally, usually with a moral attached. Some do have real-life
events which created them, but most cannot be traced to fact.
However, in the World of Darkness, most of the stories really
did happen, and usually to someone you distantly know, or a
friend of someone you know, or a cousin of that friend...

Yes, that decomposed mouse really did show up in a soda
bottle — it was bottled by a Pentex subsidiary. Yes, your
chewing gum really does have spider eggs in it — thanks again
to Pentex. The reason these events cannot be traced back to
fact usually involves some form of corporate or supernatural
coverup (whether through the Veil or the machinations of the
vampiric Masquerade).

Below are some urban legends and how to use them in a
Werewolf game.

From the Spawning Pool

The Nosferatu vampires have a gruesome method of creat-
ing sentries for their subterranean warrens: they make a pool
of potent vampiric blood and let the local fauna partake of it,
creating deformed and often monstrous ghoul animals. Many
of these beasts have been witnessed by humans and the legends
have spread concerning them, monsters such as giant alliga-
tors or rats, and even animate molds and slime. Children
everywhere secretly fear and thrill at the thought of what lurks
in the local sewer systems.

These animals are left to roam the sewers freely, and usually
serve as a first defense against unwanted intruders. However,
the Nosferatu are not the only ones living underground;
others, such as Black Spiral Dancers or even the occasional
Bone Gnawer, share the subterranean world. These Garou
have learned, of necessity, how to exist with the preternatural
fauna around them.

Garou who try to enter the sewer systems for whatever
reason (the best entrance into a Pentex plant, attacking a
Black Spiral Hive, etc.) may have to deal with these bestial
denizens. Black Spiral Dancers will use Gifts such as King of
the Beasts to direct the ghoul animals against intruders, with
or without permission of the beasts' Nosferatu masters. There
are many ways the following beasties can be worked into a
story, throwing a strange and bizarre enemy at unsuspecting
werewolves. Most of the Nosferatu ghoul animals are not
Wyrm-tainted, just deformed. Thus, the Gift of Sense Wyrm
will not detect them.

Sewer Gator

Bon Bon Louie cursed as his flashlight batteries finally gave out.
He groaned. Why now, as he was taking a shortcut through the
sewers across town? Bon Bon didn't like the sewers, unlike some of
his Bone Gnawer kin. They smelled. And there were things down
here. He tried to peer through the gloom ahead but it was too dark
to make out anything but the vague outline of the walls and
waterway. He started walking again, telling himself that the stories
of creatures were just told to keep others out of Gnawer turf. But
weren't there a bunch of vampires down here, too? Down real deep
where the Gnawers didn't usually go? Least, that's what Mom and
Pop said.

Something thrashed in the water ahead. Bon Bon came to a
sudden halt, trying to see what it was. He remembered the spare
batteries, the ones he had taken from the old boom box yesterday.
He fumbled through his pockets quickly and pulled them out. They
were low on juice but they'd let him see what the hell that noise was.
He unscrewed the flashlight cap and slipped the batteries in, screwed
the cap back on tight. He clicked the button and pointed the light
towards where the noise had come.

He was staring into massive, toothed, lizard-like jaws gaping
open. Then all was dark again as the jaws clamped down on his
hand, swallowing it and the flashlight whole...

Chapter Four: Enemies 89

LES LT EY


Everyone knows the myths about baby alligators flushed
down city toilets only to survive and grow up in the sewers,
feeding off of the toxic refuse of humankind. Well, sewer
alligators exist in the World of Darkness, regardless of how
they got down there. The Kindred blood they feed on at the
Spawning Pools allows them to grow to immense propor-

tions, and occasionally, one may venture forth into the

sunlit world above to terrorize a housing development or
neighborhood before returning below for more blood suste-

Psycho Killers

Probably one the most feared — ye

,-2,-5, Incapacitated

also revered — villains
of the modern world is the psycho killer, the nut who freaks out
and commits mass murder until he himself is killed. Even
worse are those who carefully stalk and kill chosen victims who
fitsome sort of weird agenda. The fascination with the modern
style of such creeps began with Jack the Ripper and continues
to this day.

The increase in numbers of psycho killers have many bases
in the World of Darkness: The End Times are coming, and the
minions of the Wyrm are stepping up their activity. The

growing nihilism among humankind allows Banes easily to
possess hapless humans and then to turn a minor neurosis into
a raging psychosis. Banes such as Psychomachiae, Kalus and
Scragsall work to spread the horror. Other beings also contrib-
ute, however, such as a few maddened Chimerae (see above)
and, of course, vampires, whether they be a careless drinkers or
inhuman Sabbat

There are so many dark designs against humanity and so
many fiends to implement them that it is hard even for a
knowledgeable person to discern which force was at work
behind any psycho killer incident reported in the paper.
Indeed, the instigators sometimes combine, creating a mon-
ster of a psycho killer, such as when a Psychomachiae possesses
a vampire.

Given below are some psycho killers that could appear in a
Werewolf story

The Hook

Storms-At-Dawn quietly padded through the sparse woods. He
slowly crept towards the spot where the lights could be seen over by
the ewo-lane road. He watched from the edge of the woods as the two
humans began the initial mating procedures. He hated humans,
especially when they mated. He stalked slowly and quietly towards

the car


Suddenly, the female pushed the male away. Storms-At-Dawn
stopped, in case they had seen his motion. The male, angry now,
would not take no for an answer, and forced himself on the female.
She screamed, but then the male screamed also, and Storms-At-
Dawn saw motion over them. He peered more closely and saw
another human slashing at them with a sharp hook where its hand
should be.

Storms-At-dawn growled and the hook-man looked up at him,
startled. No human could steal Storms-At-Dawn's kill and get
away with it. He charged.

The hook-man laughed, and Storms-At-Dawn stopped, growl-
ing again. He recognized that laugh. The laugh of the Wyrm. This
was no normal human...

This legendary being has appeared in many small towns and
wreaked his havoc on young lovers across America. By most
accounts, the Hook is an escaped convict who had his hand
chopped off by his girlfriend (some accounts say his mother).
He hasreplaced the hand with ahook, and now getsa vicarious
revenge on teenagers who park their cars on lonely roads or
lookouts at night. When the teens are engaged and oblivious
to goings on outside the car, the Hook creeps up and reaches
for the door handle. It is at this point that the teens still have
a chance to gun the engine and get out of there (sometimes
with the hook, which is caught on the door handle). If the
lovers are too slow, the Hook opens the door and makes grisly
work of them, leaving their bodies hacked up.

The Hook can be encountered by Garou who patrol the edge
of the woods, the margin between the suburbs and the true
wilderness, for it is here that the Hook lurks. The Hook is actually

a human derelict given supernatural abilities by a Psychomachia;
there is one Bane, but he has used many bodies throughout
America, creating the legend in many different places. Ifa Garou
can actually kill the Bane, he may destroy the Hook.

Pup Pid

Goes-Far stopped to rest by the slow-moving stream. He hada long
walk behind him but an even longer one ahead. He looked around
him in the dim half-moon' slight. The stream passed through a bridge
nearby, and Goes-Far saw the sewer pipe cleverly hidden in the
shadows there. He knew now not to drink the water. But what was


that movement? He looked closer and saw a figure squeezing out of
the pipe, followed by two smaller, rat-sized figures.

This being was strange. As it stood up, Goes-Far could see it was
but a skeleton dressed in rags, bearing in its right hand a rusted
cutlass. The two rats clustered about its feet, squeaking madly. The
sewerman stalked off with his rats up the nearby hill, towards the
human neighborhood.

Goes-Far felt a horrid chill shoot down his spine as the sewerman
turned and looked straight at him, as if he knew he had been there
all along. Goes-Far could swear he had smiled, even though those
teeth had no lips. Then, the sewerman was gone, over the hill. But
not before Goes Far caught the scent he had flung his senses out for:
the stench of the Wyrm.

Goes-Far stood up and marched resolutely up the hill. He knew
what he had to do. He just hoped he could do it before the sewerman
killed an innocent...

Pup Pid is a bizarre and dangerous type of urban folklore
character: the supernatural psycho killer. There are many of
this type told about by kids everywhere; Pup Pid is just one
example. These beings are perhaps brought to life and fueled
by the imaginations and fears of children, thus their weird and
illogical nature and relentless power.

As thestory goes, Pup Pid isa dark revenant who lives in the
local sewers and drainpipes, creeping out at night to eat people.
Ivis said that Pup Pid was once a pirate and still wears his pirate
hat with the skull and crossbones emblem on it. He also carries
his cutlass, which is stained with dried blood. The most
horrible thing about Pup Pid's appearance is that he is a
skeleton with fragments of muscle hanging off him, but with
no skin or organs left. He is accompanied by his companion
rats, two vile and vicious creatures the size of small dogs. One
is missing a tail and the other an ear.

But Pup Pid does not only come out at night; he wanders
during the day also, but in disguise. In sunlight he appears as
an old, prudish lady who is out with her two poodles (one
missing a tail, the other an ear). She is said to stop and watch
children from afar, with a disapproving yet hungry look on her
face.

These are the facts of the Pup Pid legend. So who is Pup Pid
in the World of Darkness? A Nosferatu? No, he couldn'tcome
out during the day then. A Black Spiral Dancer? Possibly, but
why the skeleton? A fomori? Maybe. A materialized spirit?
This seems possible also. As a Storyteller, you can choose any
option to bring urban folklore to life in your Werewolf story.
Below are some possible Traits for Pup Pid, assuming he is a
spirit (a Jaggling, with two Gafflings rats).

* Pup Pid (Jaggling)

ity 5, Stamina 4, Alertness 4, Athletics 2, Brawl 4, Dodge 3,

Str + 4, difficulty 6; Health: 10), Shapeshift

Intimidation 1, Stealth 3; Health: 7), Shapeshift

Suburban Horrors and Freaks
The Creepy Guy in the House Down the Lane

This guy seems to exist in nearly every neighborhood. You
know the type: the old, cranky guy whom nobody knows
anything about, who keeps to himself, doesn't like kids (hates
them in fact), and peers warily out at his neighbors from
behind closed curtains. What is this guy really up to? How
comesalesmen disappearandneverretum once they've been tohis
house? If someone could get into his basement, maybe the secret
would come out...

This figure gives the Storyteller a lot of freedom to add
strangeness to a suburban setting. If one the characters is trying to
live a normal life in the ‘burbs, or at least is visiting her Kinfolk
there, then the Creepy Guy in the House Down the Lanecancome
into play. This can provide a fun diversion to adventures about
Wyrm hunting or epic battles in the Umbra.

So just what is the Creepy Guy? Is he a fomori? A Black Spiral
Dancer? A vampire, or a ghoul serving a vampire? Is he a Son of
Ether mage trying to quietly perform his experiments in the
basement, away from the pryingand misunderstanding eyes of the
populace? Or is he just a crazy old psycho killer?

What you decide on will determine the type of story you run.
What is in that basement anyway? Does it lead to someplace
strange? Do wraiths haunt the house, tormenting the poor man
who lives there, making him cranky and solitary? Can the ghosts
be driven offand the old man left with some peace? What if he is
apolice informant, hiding out in the witness protection program?
If the characters get involved with him, will they come to the
attention of the FBI, and thus the Special Affairs division?

One single character can lead to many story ideas and those, in
tum, lead to even more.

The Witch Lady

Similar to the Creepy Guy, the Witch Lady can often be found
on the outskirts of suburbia. She is the old woman whom legends
and gossip say is a witch who years ago did in her husband with a
Black Rite to get the insurance money, and now rarely leaves the
house. Asscaryas this personisin local lore, people nonethelessare
known to schlep to her door at night and ask for concoctions and
potions to cure various ills or secure a lover's kiss. The Witch Lady
is the town magician, scoffed at by day, but respected by night.

So, who is the Witch Lady, really? Is she a real witch, and ifso,
just a hedge magician or a real Verbena mage? Perhaps she is an
elder Garou, whom the pack must go to for aid, fetishes or cures?
(Some townsfolk swear they've seen her howling to the moon at
night...) Whatever you decide she is, she can provide a jumping
off point for many stories.

The Devil Dog

This beast is known and feared by children all over: it is the

mean dog down the street, ready to chomp off heads with one bite.
Itsmad barkingand growling bringchillsto thespinesofeveryone.
The Devil Dog can be used in many stories: as the guardian of the
Creepy Guy or the Witch Lady (above), or it can be a ghoul who
has been fed by the blood of its undead master and who guards his
master's haven at night. Perhaps it is a Progenitor Construct,
placed in the neighborhood to watch suspected Garou Kinfolk, or
an Iteration X Hit Mark V (a machine, not really a dog at all). It
couldalsobea Black Spiral Dancer in Lupus form orafomori mutt.

The Devil Dog most often represents the guardian at the
threshold, the test that must be passed to enter on to the adventure
beyond (see Mythic Cycle Stories in Chapter One). Storytellers can
use this monster canine as the guardian at the gate in any weird
suburban adventure.

The Kid Chained in the Cellar

This urban folkloric figure is often found along with the Creepy
Guy or the Witch Lady. The Kid is a poor soul trapped in the
basement or cellar as punishment for an unnamed crime or
condition. The speculations on the cause are rampant: the Kid
broke some minor household rule and is being unduly punished;
the Kid was bom deformed and the parents are ashamed of it
(lockingitaway out ofsight);or the Kidishomicidal and wouldkill
if he gor loose.

The Kid in the Cellar isa story motif the Storyteller can use
if he chooses the more sinister options of the Creepy Guy or
Witch Lady mentioned above.

Wilderness Monsters
The Bog Monster

The Bog Monster only appears where the land is swampy and
dangerous. Most times it leaves unmolested anything that walks
through its territories, but if anyone attempts to damage the
swamps, it becomes a true monster and mercilessly destroys the
offender. The Mokolé are known to associate with the Bog
Monster, perhaps even as some claim, following the thing and
worshipping it as a Totem of the Swamplands.

Form, which is most of the time, the Bog Monster tries to smother

its enemies inside its body. See the suffocation rules (pp. 197-198,
Werewolf Second Edition rulebook).

Lake Serpents

Ieseems that just about every rural Lake region in the world has
a lake serpent associated with it: Nessie of Loch Ness in Scotland,
Chessie of the Chesapeake Bay on the east coast of North America
or Champy of Lake Champlain in New York. These are just
some of the mysterious inhabitants of the world's lakes.

But just what are these creatures? Are they, as some
scientists believe, actual prehistoric sea creatures, such as
plesiosaurs, that have somehow survived the ages? In the
World of Darkness, they are most often (but not always)
Great Beasts, prehistoric creatures that once roamed the
seas when Gaia was young. Whether they physically exist
in the world or must be called from the Umbra, they can be
found hidden in the depths of large lakes or bays, emerging
above the waters at times to be sighted by amateurs photogra-
phers.

In many cases, these serpents were summoned by the lupus
Gift: Song of the Great Beast, and for one reason or another,
never went away. Such is the case with Champy, of Lake

Champlain, who roams in and out of the Penumbra and the

physical world (explaining why it can't be found when scien-
tists search for it).
Below are sample Traits for such a beast.

difficulty 7)

Creatures of Native
American Myths

Not all of the creatures below are necessarily evil; some of
them, such as the Nuhnehi can and do ally with the native
Garou.

Little People

Calf Killer paused tolisten. The music came from somewhere behind
him. But that was impossible. He hadl been walking for hours and had
seen no one. Stil, he could not deny what he heard. The rhythmic
pounding of a drum and voices raised in song filled the night. Curious,
he temed around and started back down the path to investigate.


The music seemed to come from a tiny clearing. But the clearmg had
been empty only minutes before. Alert to possible danger, Calf-Killer
stepped off the path andapproached through the forest. Hemovedsilently ,
using the foliage and shadows for concealment. The music grew louder,
and he could see the glow of a fire.

Herreached the edge of the clearing and stared in amazement. Within
the circle were forty to fifty tiny men and women. Only about three feet
tall, theydanced around the fire singingand laughing. Themen, their skin
a coppery brown color, wore long breechcloths of leather, feather and
bone hairpieces, and quilled moccasins. The women, who were even
shorter than the men, wore buckskin dresses, with bands of silver
encircling their arms.

Ashe stood there watching, Calf-Killer heard a twig snap behind him.
He spun around and saw two of the little men sneaking up on him. One
of the men held a crude leather sling. Before anything could be said, the
little man twirled the sling and launched a rock. The stone struck Calf-
Killer in the center of his forehead. Darkness followed.

Little People livedeep in the forest, as faraway fromhumansand
their polluted cities as they can possibly get. They carve their
modest homesout ofrockandcave formations, spending theirtime
between this world and the Umbra.

Physical: Strength 5, Dexterity 3, Stamina 3

Social: Charisma 0-4 (depends on kind), Manipulation 1,
Appearance 1
Mental: Perception 4, Intelligence 2, Wits 3
Talents: Alertness 3, Athletics 2, Brawl 4, Dodge 4, Primal-
Urge 3, Subterfuge 2
96 Werewolf Storytellers Handbook

Skills: Animal Ken 5, Stealth 5, Survival 5

Knowledges: Enigmas 3, Occult 3

Powers: Little People are believed to have the ability to make
themselves invisible. Actually, they can't disappear, but they can
easily step sideways into the Umbra, thus appearing to vanish
before a person's eyes (roll Gnosis versus the Gauntlet, but the
difficulty is 2 less for Little People). They may also have powers
which resemble the Garou Gifts of communication with and
control over animals.

Rage 3, Gnosis 6, Willpower 5

Attacks: Sling (Str, difficulty 6, Range:Strx4), Bowandarrows
(Str + 1, difficulty 7, Range: 90)

Image: There are three kinds of Little People:

Pygmies or dwarfs: From two to four feet high, these Little
People protect the animals of the forest and have been known to
drive away or injure hunters, especially those who kill without
showing proper respect for the animal or its spirit. These tiny
peopleuseslingsinstead of arrows for hunting. And, inspite oftheir
size, are strong enough to rip oak trees out of the ground.

The second class of Little People are nearly two thirds as tall as
humans, and are associated with bow and arrow hunting. Much
friendlier than their dwarf cousins, these Little People sometimes
play with children or bring home a child that has become lost in
the forest.

The third type of Little People are known as the false face. As
suggested by the name, they are tiny creatures with large headsand
spindly limbs. These are the most dangerous of the Little People
and contact with them usually proves fatal. Little isknown of these
people, for few have seen them and lived to tell about it.

History: Reports of contact with Little People date back long
before the first Europeans ever set foot in North America. Where
they originally came from, or even where they now live, is a
mystery. Around Franklin, North Carolina, several fabricated
caves thatare believed to have been the homesof the Little People
have been found. The cavesare sosmall thatan average-sized adult
has to get down on all fours to move about in them. And in the
Great Smoky Mountains thereare several mountaintops where no
trees grow, only weedsand grass. These balds, as they are called, are
saidtobe the places where the Little People once campedand held
their dances.

According to legend, the Little People once lived in contact
with the Garou, sharing their knowledge of medicine and sacred
things. But that was long ago, and the Little People have all but
vanished from the land. Some say they now live beneath the
mountains, but exactly which ones is unknown.

Unakas

Like the calm before the storm, the night grew strangely quiet. Gone
were the chirps of the crickets and tree frogs. Gone too was the harsh cry
of the whippooruill, so boisterous only moments before. Alert to possible
danger, Ghost Dancer stood upand stepped away from his tiny campfire.
Heallowed his gaze to wander slowly over the forest that surrounded him,
buthe saw nothing out of the ordinary. If someone was hiding, they were
doing a good job of it. And though the wind was blowing his way, the air


ae AA

carried no strange odors on it, only the scent of pine trees and decaying
vegetation.

But as he stood there, the ground beneath his feet began to tremble,
asthoughamilion bugs crawled below its surface. Ghost Dancer stepped
back and watched in awe as the fleshless hand of ahuaman skeleton clawed
its way out of the ground.

A second hand followed the first. Clutching, tearing at the earth. A
skull appeared, jaws hanging open, eye sockets glowing red.

As the skeleton pulled itself out of the ground, Ghost Dancer allowed
the Rage tocome overhim, willed himself to change. He transformed into
Crinos form and waited with teeth bared.

A second skeleton appeared. And a third. They climbed out of the
ground and formed acircle around him. Several more hands appeared as
other skeletons clawed their way to freedom. Ghost Dancer waited no
longer. He attacked.

Ghost Dancer launched himself at the closest skeleton, tearmg it apart
with fangs and claws. But even as he ripped the skeleton apart, it
continued to fight back. Hands no longer attached to arms grabbed him,
rakedhis flesh. Feet without bodies kicked him. The other skeletons joined
in the fight. They jumped on him, tore at him with their fingers and teeth.
Ghost Dancer howled in pain...

The Unakas are evil spirits that appear in the form of animated
human skeletons. Though they posses neither stomachs nor

internal organs, they are cannibals and rend the flesh of their
victims with extremely sharp teeth. Itis believed that the eating of
flesh brings fleeting pleasure to these demented creatures. Fierce
fighters, they have butone failing: they cannotcrossrunning water.

Charms: Materialize (must use originally body to Materialize
into. Power cost 15; Strength 4, Dexterity 3, Stamina 3, Brawl 4,
Bite: Str + 1, Health Levels: 10)

Image: The Unakas are human skeletons with glowing eye
sockets. Dressed in the tattered remains of the clothing they
buried in, they carry clubs, spears and other makeshift weapons.

ere

ervants of the Wyrm, the Unakas embrace all that
is evil. They are enemies to the Garou and those who follow the
path of Gaia. The Unakas live in the darker regions of the Umbra,
but walk the earth at night in search of prey. They often lurkon the

one way to destroy an Unaka, and that is to crush its skull and

scatter the pieces over running water, either a spring or river.

Yuhnehi

Sam Nakai's head throbbed and his breath came in short raspy gasps.
Pain blurred his vision and sent white-hot lighming bolts dancing through
his arms and legs. He wanted to stop and rest, but dared not. Death
snapped at his heels.

How many Black Spiral Dancers were there? Three. Maybe four.
Too many to fight alone. If only he could get to someplace safe, then he
could restand tend to his wounds. But the caem was still overamile away
and Sam didn't have the strength to go on.

From behind him an eerie howl sounded. Sam tumed and watched
as three shadowy shapes emerged from the forest. The Black Spiral
Dancers had caught up with him. No doubt the fourth would be circling
around to cut off his escape.

a ——


Determined to die with honor, he loped across the open field, hoping
to make it to.a small hill that rose in the center of it. The elevated ground
would be the best place to make a final stand. But before he could make
it w the hill, Sam stepped in a hole, tripped and fell. His luck had finally
mun out. He prepared to die.

But as the first Spiral Dancer reached him, it stopped suddenly,
a puzzled look upon its face. That look quickly changed to one of
fear. The other Dancers also stopped

"Now what?" Sam asked, expecting the worst. But the Black
Spiral Dancers no longer paid him any attention. Their gazes were
fixed on something behind him. Sam turned and beheld a truly
amazing sight.

From out of the hill swarmed an army of angry spirits. All but
transparent, the ghost men wore Native American style clothing —
leggings, breechcloths and moccasins — and carried wooden war
clubs and tomahawks. Screaming terrifying war cries, they attacked
the Black Spiral Dancers with a fury that chilled Sam's blood.

Nuhnehi means "those who have always been here." They
are spirits that have inhabited North America since the
beginning of time. Keepers of magic and sacred knowledge,
they are friendly toward Garou and Native Americans and
have even been known to offer their assistance from time to
time.

Willpower 7, Rage 7, Gnosis 7, Power 25

Charms: Airt Sense. The Nuhnehi can attack targetsin the
physical world without materializing. They attack as per
normal for spirit combat (using Willpower to hit and Rage to
damage). This costs them 3 Power points per attack,

Image: Although usually invisible, when they are seen, the
Nuhnehi look like Native American warriors from eastern
woodland tribes. Their clothing is primitive, their heads are
shaved — except for scalp locks —and their faces are painted
for battle. Just the sight of the them is enough to send their

enemies running. But they are even more terrifying when they

are completely invisible. For then, only their weapons can be
seen, magically floating through the air to deliver killing
blows.

History: The Cherokee frequently speak of the Nuhnehi
and even tell stories about how the spirits helped to drive off
their enemies in times of war. Protectors of Gaia, they are
enemies to all who serve the Wyrm.

The Nuhnehi can be found underground, beneath running
water, or around certain burial mounds. To seek them out, one
must fast and go to where running water disappears back into

the earth.

Utluhtu (Spearfinger)

The elderly woman sat upon a large rock beside the path, bathed
in the sunlight that flickered through the trees. She wore a simple
printed dress, her kind face framed by two long white braids. She
smiled as Ruth Ann approached, as though she had been expecting
her.

"Come, child," the woman beckoned. "You must be tired from
your walk. Sit beside me and | will brush your hair."


Ruth Ann was hesitant at first, reluctant. But she was tired from
her long walk through the forest, and it would feel good to have the
tangles brushed from her hair. Accepting the invitation, she took a
seat beside the woman on the rock

Delighted that her offer had been accepted, the woman pulled a
brush from her leather pouch and brushed Ruth Ann's hair in long,
gentle strokes. She spoke in soft whispers as she worked, her voice
soothing, telling tales of the forest and how it was long ago. Lulled
by the voice, and the brushing, Ruth Ann closed her eyes to enjoy
the moment. Itwas the first ime she had relaxed since fleeing the city
and her hateful stepfather.

Butas Ruth Annsat there, she felt a tiny prick on her lower back,
followed by aslight pressure. She opened her eyes, turned around.
and screamed.

The lovely lady was gone. Inher place was an ugly, dwarfish old
woman with wrinkled brown skin and matted gray hair. The index
finger of the woman's right hand was a tong — twice as long as a
normal finger — and tipped with a spikelike fingemail. Blood
trickled down the woman's finger and over her wrist

In her left hand the ugly old woman held a piece of raw meat,
brown and bloody, As Ruth Ann watched, she took a bite out of the
meat and smiled.

"Thank you for your liver, child." she hissed. "It makes a most
delicious snack."

Ruth Ann staggered back. Though she had felt no pain, the
woman had somehow reached inside her body and plucked out her
liver. Ruth Ann knew that she would die. She screamed again, but
there was only one creature to hear her. Spearfinger took another
bite of the raw liver and laughed.

Chapter Four: Enemies

———

Spearfinger has long been one of the most feared monsters
to the Indian tribes of the southeast. She has a long, bony
finger on her right hand which she uses to magically stab and
remove the livers of unsuspecting victims. Since no pain is felt,
and there is no wound or scar, the victims are usually unaware
of the loss until they begin to weaken. By then it is too late and

Image: Spearfinger is a shapechanger and can appear in
many forms, her favorite being that of a kindly grandmother.
Her true image is of an ugly, old woman. Her skin is as hard as
rock, with the only weak point on her body being the spot
where her spearlike finger joins the wrist.

History: Spearfinger travels far and wide, but her favorite
haunts seem to be in mountainous regions of Tennessee,
North Carolina and Georgia. Legend has it that, long ago, she
fell intoa pit dug by Cherokee Indians and was killed when an
arrow pierced her hand. But she has since returned, possibly
brought back to life by a follower of the Wyrm.

With a Little Help
from My Friends

By Robert Kaminsky

For most people friendship is a part of everyday existence
that we think very little about, yet we are all constantly
relying on our friends for all manner of favors and support.
Ican hardly imagine what life would be like if] didn't have
For a Garou
however, things are very different. Due to the very nature

my friends around when I needed them

of the Garou, the friendships that I take for granted are very
hard for them to create or maintain. Despite this, strong
friendships and allies have been a key element in almost
every story I have been involved with as a player. As a
result, it is important for a Storyteller to think about and
understand the factors that make friendship what it is, both
in life and in the game. Below are some of the main issues
that help to illustrate the factors that one must consider
when designing full and well-rounded friends for your
players to interact with.

Chapter Five: Friends

[JE SS ana

Why is friendship so difficult for the Garou?
There are many problems and dangers a Garou must face

if she wishes to maintain her friendships with non-Garou

The first problem is the lifestyle of a Garou. It requires a
tremendous amount of secrecy, yet it also requires a great
deal of time. Asa player, I found out very quickly how hard
it is to lead the double life of a Garou and a "human." It is
challenging to make and keep friends when you are fre-
quently disappearing without a trace to take care of things
that you can't even talk about

Unless a Garou feels comfortable revealing his or her
true nature to his friends, it could be near impossible to
maintain even basic levels of trust or understanding with
any of them. Imagine trying to keep a relationship going
witha girlfriend when she doesn't even know where you are
half the time, or trying to stay on your college basketball
team when you have to miss practice so often. What's more,
the more friends you have, the more difficult it becomes to
keep certain aspects of your life hidden.

This leads to the next problem that many werewolves

run into: false friends. False friends seem to be your friends

but let you down when you need them most. For people,

101

|


ee rs

learning that someone is not whom you thought he was is
upsetting, but it does not usually threaten your life or your
future.

For Garou, these problems are much more drastic. One
false friend could ruin not only your life, but the lives of your
family, pack or even your entire sept. In most cases the false
friends of humans tend to be selfish individuals who care
more about their own hide than anything else. For Garou,
these deceivers are more often true enemies, such as Wyrm
creatures and Pentex employees who are purposely trying to
win your confidence so they can destroy you.

It is one thing when someone you trust lets you down; it
is quite another when someone you trust is actually out to
get you killed. Just think about how hard it would be to
discover this kind of deception before it was too late.

The final major problem with friends is a matter of
conscience. Because the life of a werewolf is so difficult and
violent, their friends may be in grave danger just because
they know the Garou. Whether they are being used specifi-
cally as bait to get at a character or if they are just in the
wrong place at the wrong time, most friends will not have
the ability to withstand once the punishment that many
Garou take on a frequent basis.

If friends are such a problem, why bother?

Despite the fact that many of a werewolf's emotional
needs and problems can be addressed by other Garou, there
are many issues that fall outside their group's ability to
handle. First, because the Litany is so important and perva-
sive in much of werewolf society, there are many things that
are difficult to discuss with other Garou. Having friends
outside of this society makes it possible to discuss these
issues with an unbiased, objective listener. For example,
what happens if two Garou mate with one another in a
shared moment of weakness. Whom can they turn to for
help and advice? A Philodox may be understanding, but
that isn't something I would count on. Truly, only a non-
Garou can truly look at the problem without the bias that
the Litany imposes.

Second, there are often times when things must be done
for the pack, sept or tribe that are outside the expertise of
the Garou that you know. There is a proposal to build anew
nuclear power plant for the city near to where your sept
operates, and there is a rumor that the project has been
fomented and funded by known agents of the Wyrm. Does
the sept have someone familiar with local city politics who
has enough clout to influence them? Does it have someone
who understands enough about architecture and nuclear
physics to discover if something is overtly wrong with the
proposed plant? Most likely not. Questions like this are best
answered by finding friends you can trust who have the
knowledge to find the solutions for you.

Third, non-Garou friends can give you a different per-
spective on a situation. Any large, isolated group of
individuals will settle into a limited pattern of problem
solving that usually remains fixed until someone else points

102
lh w————,

out the rut. This is an especially important limitation for
packs to overcome.

Fourth, Garou must make friends outside Garou society
in order to provide a future for the Garou as a whole.
Werewolves are a dying breed and not every child of a
Garou will be a full werewolf. Therefore, it is very impor-
tant for Garou to find a mate that they can have children
with. Since mating with other Garou is forbidden (and
futile for continuing the species), establishing friendships
with wolves and humans is very important.

What is a friend?

Many of usdefine friendship differently. To some, friends
are people to hang out with. Others see them as people who
can be relied upon for more important things. As a human,
making distinctions between the various types of friendship
is done largely subconsciously and can be nearly irrelevant
in most situations. As a Garou, however, it is vital to know
what sort of friendship you really have with the beings that
you associate with. As a Storyteller, it is always useful to
keep in mind what sort of friend a character is dealing with
when deciding on the friend's reactions. There are three
major categories that I think sum up most of the friends
people make: acquaintances, friends of similarity, and true
friends.

Acquaintances are those people you meet at work, in
school or where you live and whom you are friendly with
but know very little about. They are company for fun with
and can often be relied upon for small favors, but never
anything big. Also, it does not take long to establish a
friendship of this type, nor are they necessarily long lasting.
For Garou, acquaintances are useful for finding out minor
tidbits of information or just having a little fun. There is
actually very little danger involved with this type of friend
because so little is expected of them or shared with them.

Friends of similarity are those people you meet who have
a good deal in common with you. They are your drinking
buddies, fraternity brothers or the wolves you run with.
These friendships take much longer to form and require
much more effort to maintain, but usually some common
interest or duty allows you to identify better with one
another. Asa result it is much easier to ask these friends for
advice and favors that would strain relationships with
acquaintances. Despite this, you still don't spend all of your
time with them and there is still much that you don't know
about their daily lives and motives, so the potential for
danger is very high. If you run into a false friend, this is the
type friendship that would be easiest and most useful for
them to copy.

True friends are those people that you have spent a great
deal of time with and have come to know very well. These
people are the old friends from high school and college, the
co-workers that you spent many long nights working and
talking with or anyone who has proven beyond the shadow
ofa doubt that they will stand by you when the cards are on
the table. This category also includes long-term sweet-

Werewolf Storytellers Handbook

tie //

|


hearts and human or wolf mates. Anything you've ever
done and anything you ever do can be shared with these
people and there is practically nothing that they would not
do for you. This sort of friendship can take a lifetime to form
but is priceless. The only problems with having non-Garou
true friends are the difficulties in hiding your Garou life
(which many don't succeed in doing) and the potential
danger that these friends may face. Despite these difficul-
ties, there is nothing more valuable to a Garou or a human
than someone who is willing to give her all, no matter what
the cost.

What will a friend expect of the Garou in return?

One of the problems I have noticed in many gaming

groups is weakly realized non-player characters. One of the

classic example is the frequent misuse and abuse of hire-
lings, henchmen and followers in many game systems. Who
has not heard of someone who has always tried to push his
or her followers ahead of the characters into the most
dangerous situations. In the Storyteller system, few things
can be more fatal to a good chronicle than a story in which
the characters can easily use and abuse all the people
around them to achieve their goals. As a result, it's always
good to consider the feelings and motives of all the personas
that you have created as the Storyteller. If a character
befriends someone, then they had better give as much as
they expect to get.

Despite what I have said about the faithfulness of friends,
they should never stand for being treated as some lever or
commodity. Acquaintances make ask for a ride at an
inconvenient moment, or they may stop by at difficult
times. If they are mistreated, they will go away. With better
friends it's even worse. If you are wondering what sort of
things a friend may ask you to do, sit down fora minute and
list all the things you asked people to do for you today
Then, think back to some of the more important things that
you have asked people to do for you in the past. Next
consider the people that you went to for these favors or
opinions. What category of friend do you think they fit?

Finally, you can use the results of your requests to help
determine some of the reactions a friend might have in
similar situations. If, after all of this, you determine that a
character is mistreating one of his friends, then let the
character have it. Acquaintances may just walk away, but
closer friends could have much worse reactions that range
from direct, angry confrontation to smoldering, hidden
hatreds.

Regardless of what actually happens between your play-
ers and the personas they have created, all the creativity
and time you put into designing your characters will make
the story you are telling a memorable adventure.

Below the Salt

Kinfolk occupy an awkward position in Garou society when
they're involved in itatall. Allies, agents, breeders and protector-
ates, Kinfolk, both human and lupine, take on rolessimilartothose
of women in many human societies — valuable second-class
citizens.

Many Garou view their changeless Kin as precious pawns,
valued more for what they are than for who they are. This
impression is by no means universal but is common enough.
Kinfolk bear (and often raise) Garou children to their First
Change, and act as go-betweens, couriers, spies and sometimes
cannon fodder for the embattled werewolves. Regardless of the
Kinfolk's function, few Garou regard them as equals — gifted, yes;
precious, yes; equal, no. The changing spirit is, of course, the mark
of Gaia's favor. They may be friends, but rarely partners.

Kinfolkare, in many ways, buffers between humans and Garou.
Werewolves prize themas good breeding stock, but often uninten-
tionally condescend them — after all, they're not Garou! Some
Kinfolk have grown to resent this dismissal; Samuel "Skinner"
Haight and his tribe of Skin Dancers are prime examples of
resentment exploding into hatred. Other Kinfolk accept their lot
happily, glad to be involved in a cause worth fighting for. Still
others never realize the truth behind their strange talents and
moody temperaments. They go through life blinded by a different
sort of Veil.

Werewolf Storytellers Handbook

EE TS me 7 -

Types of Kinfolk

Your children are not your children.

They are the sons and daughters of Life's longing for itself.

They come through you but not from you,

And though they are with you yet they belong not to you.

— Kahlil Gibran, The Prophet

Inthe old days, Kinfolk were often watched and jealously
guarded. But with the dwindling wolf and Garou popula-
tions and the heavy concentrations of human society, this
has become a difficult task. Some pockets with strong
Kinfolk strains remain protected by the tribes, but orphan
Kinfolk become more common with each year. The "thin-
blooded" can take on one of the following basic roles in
modern Garou society:

Allies

Many human families revere their secret pedigree; wolf
packs with strong ties to their cousins prosper where others
decline. These Kinfolk prize their heritage and will do
almost anything to help their Garou relatives. Many hu-
man Kin infiltrate organizations or form community political
groups that the werewolves could not run. Some Kin ruled
lands in the old days and still control influential families
and businesses. Other Kinfolk allies form networks like the
Sisterhood (see the Black Furies Tribebook) to aid the
tribal cause, while still more live and work alone as sentries
against the Apocalypse.

Enemies

Not all Kinfolk are happy with their lot. Many resent
their secondary status or covet their cousins' power. Some
Kinfolk, Samuel Haight for example, are abused by frus-
trated Garou parents who wait to see a gift that will never
appear. Other Kin become jealous, and the Wyrm eats into
their hearts. These become the most fearsome werewolf
hunters; they have knowledge, immunity to the Delirium
and a passionate hatred that drives them beyond normal
boundaries.

Note that humans are not the only Kin to turn on their
forbears. Some wolf packs, after years of aggressive forced
breeding, have attacked amorous Garou or have fled when
they approached. Animals, too, may feel resentment. Few
Garou will stand against an angry wolf pack; although they
heal quickly from a normal wolf's bite, the tragedy of
fighting one's sacred cousins would break most werewolves'
hearts.

Orphans

As the Apocalypse draws nigh, Garou frantically seek
out mates among the wolves and humans, hoping that the
blood will breed true. Sadly, most offspring never manifest
the changing gift, and as the casualties of the Final Days
decimated the tribes, most Garou offspring never meet
their Garou relatives. Though some of these human Kin-

|


folk discover their true heritage, many never do. The wild
urge burns just below their humanity, often alienating or
intimidating "normal" humans without either party know-
ing why. Orphan Kinfolk often become either hermits or
vagabonds, business or community leaders or criminal
masterminds.

Although orphan Kinfolk are not taught about the
supernatural elements around them, awareness often sneaks
in around the edges; many have a knack for stumbling into
the shadows without understanding them. Some become
hunters of one kind or another, while others go into radical
denial about the things they see or hear. Detective Janis van
Landingham in the Valkenburg Foundation story, "Hos-
tile Takeover," is a good example of an orphan Kinfolk
standing at the fringes of the occult without any formal
introduction to what she sees.

Calents and Temperaments

Though Kinfolk are not full-fledged Garou, primal urges,
animal rage and human reason flow strongly in them. They
tend to be more passionate, volatile and, conversely, more
honest and concerned than the average civilized human.
The call of nature is never far from their ears, though some
try to block it out without understanding why. The Wyrm
hovers around these latter Kin, looking for some way into
their hearts. In general, human Kinfolk tend to favor a
spiritual connection to nature, while lupine Kin compre-
hend Weaver things on a more complex level than do
"normal" wolves.

The slumbering primal spirit stirs and stretches in hu-
man Kinfolk. Many can work hedge magic, learn small
Gifts and rites, unlock psychic powers or even Awaken
their primal Avatars enough to use the True Magick of the
mage (though many mage Kinfolk become unwelcomed by
Garou out of distrust for mages in general). Even if super-
natural power is beyond their grasp, Kinfolk tend to be
hardy and skillful. Far from being mere allies or connec-
tions, Kinfolk are independent and capable in their own
right (see Creating Kinfolk, below).

No Shadow Lord would ever consider mere Kinfolk their
equals; this attitude in turn leads to resentment and, occasion-
ally, to treason. All too many Kin have been goaded to the
Wyrm's side by the constant trials, threats and discipline of
these relentless Garou. Some among the tribe have begun to
call for more respect for their cousins, but others see the fallen
Kinfolk as just one more reason to keep astern and heavy hand

lovers, of memories enough fora thousand lifetimes sparked by

Few Silent Striders will willingly place either human or
lupine Kinfolk in jeopardy. They respect and cherish their
Kin, knowing that the special types the Striders are drawn
to are rare. Still, even the Wandering Tribe advances its
purposes through their Kinfolk. While the Seekers pass
their arcane wisdom down to select human Kin, the Dispos-
sessed adopt other wanderers, then spread their dire
prophecies among them to hasten the coming doom. The
ways of the mercenary Wayfarers especially suit many
human drifters, while packless wolves attach themselves to
the Harbingers as a lupine honor guard. The romance and
mystery of the Silent Striders' Garou-Kinfolk relations bear
the seeds of many possible tales. Even other tribes are not
immune to the vagabond's lure.

Silver Fangs: The Kinfolk of the First Tribe are the
créme de la creme of human sogiety — the nobility, gentry

Fang's eccentricities 4 :

Throughout history, the Silver Fangs have wielded power
through their human cousins. Like the Get of Fenris and
Shadow Lords, the First Tribe has informed centuries of
human aristocrats. Unlike the other two tribes, however,
the power of the Silver Fang Kinfolk wanes with each year.
As democracies (real or imagined) spring up and titled
nobility give way to corporate giants, the Kinfolk are losing
their edge in human affairs. Instead of revamping, they
waste their time in posturing or satisfying elaborate social
codes, further distancing the primal call of their Garou
race. Most Silver Fang Kinfolk hold strong codes of honor
but lose sight of the real world. Like the Garou they descend
from, these Kinfolk, wolf and human, act peculiarly. Even
the wolves adopt habits that set them apart from their
brothers. Though they often head the pack, such odd
Kinfolk are questioned behind their backs. The others are
no longer so quick to obey.

Several infamous hunters have come from the Silver
Fang line. Perhaps the madness that eats at the tribe leaves
their Kinfolk open to extremes. One Kin, a Baron
Rutherford, kept a secret ranch where he hunted "normal"
animals, humans and even his own lupine Kin before a
mixed-tribe pack discovered him and ended his sport. The
Silver Fangs' pride still stings from this embarrassment.
More perversions will surely come.

Wendigo wolf Kin will suffer badly for it.

The lupine Kin of this tribe are mentally and physically sick.
Many pass these sicknesses on to their cubs, which, of course,

Kin attack both human and Garou settlements, fouling every-

Kin have fed the lupophobia that has fueled recent mass
killings of wolves. If protests are raised, the response is that the
attacks on farms and towns have proved the need for wolf
control. Though other Garou Kinfolk occasionally pick off
human intruders, the savagery of Black Spiral attacks chill
even the most militant Garou.

Creating Kinfolk

icarry your heart with me

icarry it in my heart

i'm never without it

wherever you go i go my dear

— EE. Cummings, "i carry your heart with me (i
carry it in)"

Kinfolk are individuals, often stronger and smarter than the
humans or wolves around them. So who is your Kinfolk
character? What makes her tick? How does she act, and why?
Storytellers should consider these questions when creating
Kinfolk characters.

Though the different Garou cultures will leave their mark
in some way upon the children of that tribe, the Storyteller
should take care that his Kinfolk have personality, motivation
and purpose. Remember also that Kinfolk are family. This will
color their relationships with Garou players. While blood is
thicker than water, it's also true that you can't choose your
relatives.

The suggestions below work for Storyteller characters in
general but are especially appropriate for the often-abused
Kinfolk Background of player Garou:

* Personality: A personal quirk or two — snapping chew-
ing gum, an unusual accent, a passion for chocolate —can pull
abland background character into the foreground. What does
she look like? What does she smell like? Your character should
make an impression. It's hard to get worked up over the
kidnapping of a set of statistics.

Most Kinfolk will have a stronger personality than the
average person. Pick out some aspect that makes them memo-
rable, then go for it. Just don't overdo this — excessive
campiness can spoil the mood.

© Motivation: Good characters don't act ina vacuum; they
have reasons for everything they do. Gerald Strumm won'tjust
tell his Glass Walker pal everything he knows for no reason.
Does he want to trade favors? Is he angry, and thus untrustwor-
thy? Ishe genuinely helpful, ordoes he have some more sinister
purpose? Consider which attitude your Kin holds towards the
Garou, and howhe mightact given his opinions. A character's
motivation will influence his actions.

* Purpose: Storyteller characters, Kinfolk or not, will have
some personal goal that they want to accomplish. That goal,
and the means they use to reach it, may make all the difference
in the world to your players. Kinfolk, in particular, will have
overriding goals and plans and will be used to getting their way.
This doesn't mean that Walks-Between-Walls' cousin will be
adversarial, but his short- or long-term goal may influence his
response to the Glass Walker's questions.

Gifts and Magic

Although most Kinfolk cannot use Gifts above the first
level, they frequently have access to different supernatural
powers. Most Kin, even humans, can be taught the Sense
Wyrm Gift if they work with a sept. Garou or spirits may even

Chapter Five: Friends

[POEL Ps ET Ds LT PTT Ts ST IS

teach more advanced Gifts to worthy or important Kin.
Kinfolk have no Gnosis or Rage, however, and cannot use
Gifts that require these Traits.

Storytellers have three options for Kinfolk magic: simulat-
ing hedge magic with Gifts that require some kind of ritual
instead of Gnosis, using the Numina, psychic abilities and
hedge magic presented in the Vampire book, The Hunters
Hunted, or simply making up whatever abilities she wants the
character to have. While an occasional Kinfolk Avatar might
Awaken in the mystic sense, true mages should be rare even
among Garou Kin.

If Gifts are chosen, the Storyteller should use her discretion
and choose appropriate low-level Gifts. It's extremely rare for
a Kinfolk to learn a Gift above Level One, but it has been
known to happen.

Some Gift examples include: Mother's Touch, Persuasion,
Eyes of the Cat, Sense the Unnatural, Detect Spirit, Spirit
Speech, King of the Beasts, Mindspeak, Curse of Aeolis,
Messenger's Fortitude, Sense Magic and Shroud.

Chapter Four of The Hunters Hunted contains a variety
of paranormal powers for mortals, including hedge magic,
psychic powers and True Faith. That chapter, and indeed that
whole book, offersup plenty of good material forthe Werewolf
Storyteller.

A Storyteller should feel free to let her characters have
whatever abilities she feels would be appropriate, within
reason. Game mechanics should not shackle a good story. Just
be consistent and fair; a Kinfolk with an arsenal of strange
magic may be more irritating than impressive.

Kinfolk as Player-Characters

How'd you dare to tell me

That I'm my father's son?

Well that was just an accident of birth

— Jethro Tull, "Wind Up"

There is no reason that a player can't choose a Kinfolk
character over a Garou. This might make for an interesting
pack, although the Kin player will be at a real disadvantage
when the fighting starts. Though they take no extra damage
from silver, Kinfolk heal as mortals.

Player Kinfolk should begin with the normal amount of
Attributes (6/4/3) and Abilities (11/7/4) for a mortal charac-
ter. Kinfolk should begin with five Background points and can
buy them up further if appropriate; a human Glass Walker will
have more Backgrounds than a Wendigo wolf. Assume a
starting Willpower of 3. Like mortal hunter characters, Kin-
folk begin with 21 freebie points instead of 15.

Kinfolk do not get Gnosis, nor do they have Rage. They
may learn a few Level One Gifts, possess psychic abilities and
Numina powers and buy Merits and Flaws. Though they have
none of their cousins' special abilities, they are immune to the
effects of silver and the Delirium, and do not always panic
animals by their presence. Garou law still applies to Kinfolk,
but they can get away witha lot more than normal werewolves.

109


pera ve ener reas ener are ere a reumorwrenenrens

Companion Kinfolk are often, but not always, sept
offspring. Many Garou choose Kinfolk lovers or make a
friend or two with whom they can be themselves. Some
characters may be siblings while others share a common
network — the Sisterhood or a Gypsy band. In any case,
the Garou will be protective of their fragile cousin —
pethaps too protective for the player's liking!

Kinfolk Templates

Assume that average Kinfolk have Traits about one
point higher than the usual for their species. Many
Kinfolk will have unusual Abilities as well — Stealth,
Security, various Knowledges — when appropriate. If
you want to create your Kinfolk from scratch, build them
as you would a player character, with 15 or 21 freebie
points and a Merit or Flaw or two if desired.

The templates below can serve either as Storyteller
cters or models from which to build original char-
acters:

Troupe Play

Really advanced players might take on Kinfolk char-
a revolving-cast troupe, a group where players
play one major character and one or two minor ones.
Troupe-play stories often shift their focus from minor to
major characters, depending on the situation.

acters ii

The Hungry Moon pack includes two Black Furies
anda Wendigo, plus three human Wendigo Kinfolk and
a Fury wolf-Kin. While most stories of the Hungry
Moons feature the Garou in starting roles, an occasional
tale might concentrate on a hunter stalking the wolf or
a clash between the F.B.I. and the Wendigo Kin while
the Garou are away. Without their supernatural abili-
ties, Kinfolk must find other ways of coping with tense
situations. These stories can give both Storyteller and
players a break from the usual fang-and-claw game
sessions, illuminate an unusual aspect of the Werewolf
world and explore a minor-key kind of drama.

Roleplaying Hints: You're a curious soul; now that

anything is possible. You want to know it all, then ferret

your findings to your brother-in-law's sept. Your laugh is
raspy, your voice thick with cigarettes and innuendo.

Background: You discovered your heritage by acci-
dent — poor Chuckie knew that his new bride was Kin,
but hadn't figured that her father had sired twins. He
tried to keep you and Gina out of sept business, but no
way! Spying on hustlers, skanks and dealers beat cruising
to N.Y.U. any day! It's dangerous, sure, but if you sur-
vived Edgewater Park everything else is easy.

Roleplaying Hints: You know more about Two-Legs

and must be fed. The Blessed came to your pack for
mates, but you warned them such sharing had its cost.
Two-Legs hasn't bothered your pack for nearly a season.
Perhaps soon the food will return.

Kami: Jncarnations
of Gaia

We know the sap which courses through the trees as we know
