This section details the "fomori" of Gaia, known among
the Garou as Kami (a Japanese word for spirit). These beings
are very rare and always unique. Storytellers should be
careful not to overpopulate the World of Darkness with
them. Every appearance by these beings should be some-
thing special.

Cypes of Kami

There are many kinds of Kami, including plant Kami,
animal Kami, mortal Kami, flesh-borne spirits and animate
lands. Each of these is described further below. Storytellers
should feel free to create Kami of other types as well.

All Kami are unique beings. While some may gather in
small groups performing important tasks for the Mother,
most work alone or with beings other than Kami. Kami vary
in their outlook on Gaia, their duties, their methods, their
personalities and in many other ways.

From Gaia's Womb

The Kami are simply another expression of Gaia's love for
diversity within nature. At one time, the Kami thrived in the
world. They were the manifest and living spirits of mountains,
trees, plants and the seasons. There were countless plants and
animals filled with unique power and beauty bestowed upon
them by Gaia. But the Wyrm went insane, and its continuing
scourge has left Gaia's womb barren. There are few Kami left
and the birth of one in this day and age is one of the greatest
of Gaia's miracles.

Relations with the Garou

Few Garou know of the Kami. Most consider them crea-
tures of legend. Every relationship between Kami and Garou
is based upon the individuals involved. Kami seldom work in
direct opposition to Garou unless commanded to doso by Gaia
Herself, for they know what Garou are capable of. On rare
occasions, Kami seek out Garou or other Kami for assistance.
Most Kami know very little about Garou culture, such as its
tribes, auspices, powers, or philosophies.

Chapter Five: Friends

 f RTL

Gaia's Blessings

All Kami possess certain powers. First off, all possess at least
human-level intelligence, though their thought processes are
not human (unless they were born human). In addition, all
Garou and spirits can feel something of a holy presence
radiating from them. This presence has no real affect other
than alerting those who are sensitive to it that they are in the
company of one of Gaia's chosen.

Silver does not affect Kami as it does Garou; they take
normal damage from silver weapons. However, most Kami are
vulnerable to at least one "normal" type of attack (i.e., fire,
cold iron, glass, plastic, lead, intense cold, etc.), and cannot
soak damage from such attacks.

All Kami possess Gnosis and some possess Rage, which may
be regained as the Storyteller sees fit. Some Kami with Rage
may even frenzy as Garou. A Kami's Health Levels are
determined by the Storytellerand is usually dependent on size.
Large plant hosts, such as trees, are hard to destroy, and an
animate land is even more difficult. Animate lands are only
harmed through the destruction of the land itself or through
defilement by chemicals, radiation, fire or some other hideous
means.

Kami Powers

The following listing includes the more common Kami
powers. Since no two Kamiare really alike, Storytellers should
feel free in giving the Kami they create powers not listed here.
These powers are merely guidelines.

Kami are meant to be Storyteller characters, not player
characters. If a Storyteller decides to let a player have a Kami
character, she must figure out the character creation process
for herself.

Animal Kinship — The Kami has the power to influence
animals, including lupus Garou (resisted roll: Willpower vs.
Willpower). The animals will view the Kami as a friend anda
leader. They will aid the Kami however possible, within
reason. This power is similar to the Philodox Gift: King of the
Beasts.

Animal Powers — (Cost: 1 Gnosis) The Kami can either
transform itself so that it has certain animal powers, or italways
possesses those powers. Often the Kami will have at least some
aspect of the animal's appearance. Some sample powers in-
clude: heightened senses, claws, fangs, cat-like grace and
balance, great endurance, bursts of speed, water breathing, and
leaping ability.

Animal Speech — The Kami has the power to communi-
cate with animals of all sorts. The Kami knows the language of
all animals and speaks to them through the sounds they make.
The communication is actually telepathic, but the language is
used as the vehicle for communication. This power is similar
to the Galliard Gift: Beast Speech.

Animal Summons — (Cost: 1 Gnosis) The Kami has the
power to summon animals to itself. The animals are inclined
towards helping the Kami. The types and number of animals

11

LF LTE SG


rae rere ee core rit ares ems weni rev

summonable are left up to the Storyteller. This power issimilar
to the Lupus Gift: Beast Life.

Animate Self — (Cost: 1 Willpower) This power allows
inanimate Kami to become animated. Most do so for short
periods of time, though some tend to remain animate almost
all the time. Kami which are attached to something, such as
Kami trees which are attached to the ground, may uproot
themselves and move, but this costs two Willpower points
instead of one.

Aura of Tranquillity — The Kami radiates peace, which
calms all within its presence, including allies. Garou cannot
use Rage for the duration of the scene, and all present will be
hard pressed to commit violence. The Kami makes a resisted
Charisma + Empathy roll versus each affected individual's
Willpower; victims who fail cannotact violently. This power
is similar to the Children of Gaia Gift: Serenity. Most Kami
with this power tend to radiate this aura at all times.

Autumn's Blessings — The Kami has the power to cause
a large area to take on the appearance and effects of autumn.
Leaves turn their fall colors, animals begin storing up food for
the winter, and the airfills with the chill of coming winter. The
Kami can instantly command all the leaves in a tree to fall at
once (cost: 1 Gnosis). If there are lots of leaves, those standing
under them may even be knocked down by the sheer force.
The Kami can also sense those who have left the prime of life
and are beginning to approach the winter of life.

Child of Air (Earth, Fire, or Water) — (Cost: 1 Gnosis)
The Kami can summon and command elementals of the
appropriate type (Manipulation + Expression, difficulty 7).
One elemental is summoned per success and the Kami can
command a number of elementals equal to its Wits rating.
Some Kami possess other powers relating to their element. It
is rare forany Kami to bea child of more than one element, but
there can be Kami who are children of combined elements:
Child of Steam (fire and water), Child of Lava (fire and earth),
Child of Mud (water and earth).

Command the Earth —The Kami can cause the very earth
to move as it commands. This may be used to form quicksand,
pits, tremors, landslides and other phenomena. The cost varies
with the region affected; the broader the area, the higher the
cost. An earthquake would cost 2 Gnosis, while a quicksand
pond would cost only 1 Gnosis.

Curse of Gaia — (Cost: 3 Gnosis) Kami with this power
can place acurse upon those who disrupt the balance of nature.
This power varies greatly in effect and strength. Examples:
victims are turned to stone, victims suffer Harano, victims
become diseased, victims suffer runs of bad luck, victims are
swallowed up by the earth. Curses can be anything the fiendish
Storyteller can think up. Most Kami are capable of inflicting
only one particular curse or a small number of different curses.

Enchanting Voice — (Cost: 1 Gnosis) The Kami has the
power to enthrall those who hear its singing to make them
inclined to approach the source of the sound. The enchanted
one must make a Willpower roll versus a difficulty equal to the
Kami's Charisma + Performance.

112
ll ————,

Gaia's Summons — (Cost: 1 Gnosis, | Willpower) The
Kami has the power to summon some powerful force of Gaia,
be it Wyldlings, one of the Great Beasts, or possibly even a
certain group (breed, tribe, sept) of Garou. Those who are
summoned will act in the best interest of the Kami. Those who
try to resist must make a resisted Willpower roll versus the
Kami.

Garou Kinship — Garou will be inclined towards accept-
ingthe Kamiasa friend and confidante. This issimilartoa Pure
Breed rating of three.

Great Destiny — The Kami cannot be stopped by anything
until it accomplishes the purpose for which it exists. Gaia has
chosen the Kami for some great and special task and anything
which would normally prevent the Kami from accomplishing
that task (such as death) is prevented by some miraculous
event.

Heart Sense — (Cost: 1 Gnosis) The K:
the soul of an individual and see which member of the Triat
they are most inclined towards. The Kami can also see and
interpret the past lives of the individual, recognize any guilt
they feel and why, see their dreams and desires, and recognize
their true form. This requires an Perception + Empathy roll,
difficulty seven. Each success increases the amount of informa-
tion learned.

Invulnerability — The Kami has an additional one to five
points of Stamina for the purpose of soaking damage. Often
the Kami'sskin will be unusual in some way, such asstone skin,
chitinous armor, or a faint glow surrounding the body.

Long-Lived — The Kami lives far longer than do other
members of its species. The Kami is not immortal, but Gaia's
energies slow the aging process in the Kami's body. For a
human Kami, long-lived may be three hundred years. For an
insect Kami, long-lived may be two weeks. For a mountain
Kami, long-lived may be virtually immortal by human stan-
dards of time.

Kami Characters

This section contains descriptions on each basic type of
Kami. In addition, sample characters of each type are pro-
vided. They may be used as described or modified to fit a
Storyteller's needs, and they also provide examples of Kami
creation.

Plant and Animal Hosts

Plant and animal hosts are plants and animals infused with
the energy and sentience of Gaia. Many possess telepathy and
some can even speak verbally in one or more human tongues.
Some hosts are unusual in appearance (size, coloration, shape,
aroma, or location), though most resemble their normal
counterparts. All plant and animal hosts possess special pow-
ers granted by Gaia.

Mortal Hosts

Mortal hosts are in many ways similar to animal hosts.
However, the spirits of animals are part of the living Umbra,
while the souls of humans go elsewhere after their demise.
Mortal hosts are unusual in that they have spirit-souls capable
of entering the Near Umbra. Mortal hosts are usually more
independent than other Kami, but they can also be the most
effective because they can easily fade in and out of human
society. Johnny Appleseed is a good example of a mortal host
known in folklore.

error of its ways. He has acquired a vast amount of wealth over
the years, but virtually all of it goes to charity. He is afraid of
Garou, and will avoid them if at all possible.

Flesh-Borne Spirit

One of Gaia's most blatant uses of power is the transforma-
tion of spirit into flesh. When powerful Kami are needed in an
emergency, and none are available, Gaia sometimes alters
Wyldlings, elementals and other spirits making them perma-
nently manifest in the real world. These flesh-borne spirits are
very powerful and single-mindedly devoted to their purpose:
service to Gaia. They often have very specific missions. Until
they complete them, they are disbarred from reentering the
Umbra (they cannothave Umbral Passage asa power). Should
they be destroyed on Earth, they return to the Umbra to
Reform. It takes them at least the same length of time they
were on Earth to Reform in the spirit world.

Wyldlings tend to be far more unpredictable and danger-
ous, while elementals and other spirits tend to be more
methodical, though no less powerful. Some Kami of this sort
gain the power to takeona human form. Aswith all Kami, they
are at least the equals of humans in terms of self-awareness and
intelligence.

Animate Lands

IfGaia wills it so, entire sections of land can become infused
with sentience. The land acts as one giant creature, with every
plant and animal living on it being part of its body. The earth
isits flesh, the water is its blood, and the air is its breath. Nature
is allowed to take its course, as it should. Often, humans are
evenallowed to farm or live on the Kami, as longas they donot
abuse it. When the Kami acts, all parts of its body act in unison
to carry out the action; therefore, these Kami are very power-
ful. Some animate lands allow Garou to live and hunton them
as long as they serve Gaia. Some say the Red Talons know
many secrets of these Kami, including a rite for awakening
them.

Animate Lands usually regain their Gnosis points at a faster
rate than other Kami, sometimes as much as 3 per hour
(dependent on weather conditions being favorable for the
land's environment).

Haunted Bayou

Image: The Haunted Bayou looks just like any other bayou
most of the time. However, it can make itself deathly quiet or

the Bayou on fire during one of their skirmishes. Legend has it
that many strange things roam the Bayou, from ghostly Native
American raiders, to giant alligators large enough to swallow
boats, to lesser Kami who serve the land. Deep in the swamp
late at night, a hermit supposedly performs strange rituals
directed towards feeding the spirit of the land, but what it feeds
the Bayou remains a mystery. A Pentex chemical research
plant was built on the Bayou twelve years ago. The Bayou
awoke in pain from all the chemicals being poured out into
its body. Within two weeks, the plant was destroyed, and
within two years not a trace of the plant remained.

It's good, as the Stoics tell us, to have tools that are simple to

and employ them at a moment's notice. I think the essential tools in
any worthwhile endeavor are incredibly simple. And very difficulty

Sharpen Vour Claws

By Brian Campbell

Werewolf is, simply put, a wonderful game. The job of
the Storyteller is to make it even better. The rulebook
contains all the basics of the game, and the sourcebooks add
to that. There are, however, many other resources to draw

on when preparing for an adventure. Perfecting the art of

Storytelling involves tracking down the right resources,
leaping at the opportunity to learn and tearing into the task
of learning. If you really want to improve your Storytelling,
it's going to take some work. You've got to harry your prey
before you can take it down.

The hunt is on. Sharpen your claws.

Chapter Six: The Ways

[PO ET ST a

Resource 1: Your Players

Becominga better Storytellers. learning process. The first
thing to learn about is your players. The Storyteller does not
run the game alone. The relationship between the Storyteller
and the players is not an adversarial one. The group cooper-
ates, and knowing how to draw your players into the game is

part of making a good story.

Youalready know about the use of the Prelude. Tailoring an

sonalities of your players and occasionally

adventure to the pe
challenging them, is a must. Don't forget, though, that your
players have plenty of things to teach you. Each player brings
real world knowledge into the game, and each gaming group
is a gathering of experience and expertise.

One example is the typical college gaming group. Each
player ina college group has a different major. A drama major

119


|

canteacha lotaboutacting technique; an anthropology major
is extremely valuable for teaching about comparative cultures;
a business major can make an incredible Glass Walker. In
addition, everyone has hobbies. Tying them in to the research
you do for a game can add authenticity. Players love to
volunteer to teach. Try to keep up. If you can lear more about
what your players are willing to teach you, you're on your way
to growing as a Storyteller.

The Werewolf rulebook briefly discusses the option of
troupe-style Storytelling. Your Ragabash player might want to
lead the group ina round of tall tales. Your Ahroun might very
well want to spend more time refining the combat rules than
you do. The Theurge player might run a fantastic Umbral
adventure for an hour or add lots of detail to the rituals at the
local sept. A Galliard player who can actually compose songs,
poetry or stories can make an adventure far more memorable
than can a set of dice rolls (as long as she can do it well. You
might have to cut her some slack). Regardless of whether you
actually rotate Storytellers for the same story, deferring to your
players and encouraging them to add details to the game
enriches the experience for everyone.

Resource 2: B cooks

White Wolf put together rulebooks and sourcebooks to
help players and Storytellers, but they're only one type of
resource. One common mistake I've seen among beginning
Storytellers is the idea that reading more sourcebooks alone
will make them better Storytellers. That's only partly true.
There are other books that can be used.

Your local library is free. Use it. Even if you only have time
toskim, there is more material there foradventures than you'll
find in a whole stack of sourcebooks. Travel guides, encyclo-
pedias, historical accounts, maps and nature books are just a
few examples. There's always something you can learn. (For
instance, how well do you really understand wolves?) If you
know more about your background material, youcanadd more
depth to your stories.

Resource 3: Realia

Bringing materials other than dice and pencils is certainly
an optional part of the game. Although we discourage using
props in Live-Action, having materials present at your table-
top game can make it more fun, and fun is the bottom line in
gaming. Just as a good Storyteller can evoke a story by calling
upon all five senses, the realia you use to augment your game
can make it more enjoyable.

Auditory Realia — The most obvious way to use realia is
through soundtrack. This is a rather length topic to address,
and it has been expounded on before. The same principle
applies to Werewolf. Letting music play softly in the back-
ground can subtly alter the emotions of your players. Exploring
recordings of Native American ceremonies or New Age music
is an adventure in itself. However, as with any other realia,
using it too much can destroy its purpose. The right song is no
substitute for good storytelling. Use sound occasionally, and
choose it wisely.

120

a See

Werewolf Storytellers Handbook

OE EE ny

Many players like to get into the idea of asoundtrack as well.
CD's are expensive, so feel free to invite your players to bring
music. The music they bring is another indicator of the types
of adventures they want to have. Try having one player work
as the DJ. This prevents you from having to fumble with the
CD player to cue up the right track for the right scene.

Sound effects are difficult to coordinate, but can do won-
ders. Atmospheric tapes, including live recordings of natural
surroundings, can be useful. The Nature Company is one
example of a place to pick up this type of recording. (For
example, their Tropical Jungle cassette works really well with
Rage Across the Amazon). Just be careful. Listening to the
same spider monkey recording for four games in a row can get
really annoying.

Visual Realia — If you've tracked down books, you prob-
ably have pictures, and one of them really is worth a thousand
words. Describing Central Park, for instance, is much easier if
you actually have pictures of the different locations there.
Movies are another type of visual realia. Playing the right
movie on the VCR before your players gather around the table
can really put them in the proper mood.

Lighting is relatively easy to implement, as long as its used
sparingly. Using candlelight for an hour can scare the hell out
of your players. If you use itall the time, every session, you'll get
sick of squinting to see your dice.

Tactile Realia—This is one way in which the artists of your
group can take part. The pictures of fetishes in the Werewolf
tulebook can give you some examples of items to pass to your
players. A patch of fur, drawings in dirt or even a pile of sticks
can give your players ideas. Again, restraint is necessary. If
you're carving a wooden boat in your backyard for your
"Werewolves and Whalers" adventure, your players will start
to worry about you.

Olfactory Realia — Calm descriptions of a tranquil glade
are quite nice, but the smell of a flower can be more pleasant.
Ifyoucan subtly lighta stick of incense, youcan really freak out
the players on your next Umbra adventure. If you can't be
subtle, they're going to dive for an aerosol can. Also be careful
about how you introduce Wyrm smells...

Gustatory Realia — Yeah, I'll admit I'm a pizza junkie.
Still, if a player in your group can actually volunteer to cook,
your group will be very thankful. What part of the world is your
next adventure set in? What do your players eat while they're
there? Use discretion. If you eat raw hamburger after your
character hunts, you're an idiot, and taking everyone to Taco
Bell before your run of Chaos Factor is just silly.

Live-Action —One more word on Live-Action: it doesn't
have to be entirely separate from your tabletop game. The
Apocalypse has a complete set of rules for Live-Action gam-
ing, but Live-Action doesn't always need rules. One example
of this is the Live-Action cutaway. Getting your players away
from the gaming table for a while can be useful. Having your
players act out a scene of your adventure adds another dimen-
sion to the game.

The three basic safety rules listed in the main rulebook still
apply: No Touch, No Stunts, No Props. Begin by describing


|

the room all of you are in. Some of the players might use their
normal characters, but describing an interaction between one
of the characters and some other people can help add exposi-
tion to your story. Don't worry about tests or challenges.
Letting your players actually act through a scene occasionally
sets a good counterpoint to a tabletop game. Keep it safe, lead
it back to the tabletop and keep it fun.

Resource 4: Jssues

Sure, Werewolf is just a game, but it's also a chance to deal
with real issues. Talking about environmentalism is all well
and good, and running a game where you kill the Wyrm and
heal the Earth can make you feel better, but limiting it to that
is pretty damn shallow. There's a lot more to the issue than
killing the Wyrm, and, as such, there's a lot more to the Garou
than Wyrm killing. There are plenty of organizations that can
give you information about environmental issues. If you really
want to draw emotion from your players, consider the amount
of real-world events on which you can base your stories.
Playing a game is not a substitute for feeling. When it's done
well, it wakes you up and makes you realize, through the
metaphor of a game, the important issues of life. Then you are
empowered to go out and do things correctly in the real world.

I'm not saying that your Werewolf group should be a
recruiting device for your local chapter of Greenpeace. Just be
aware that a story is as important, as relevant, as you want to
make it. Don't club people over the head with morality, but
make sure your players get a chance to think about the ethics
and motivations of their characters. Handling a real-world
problem as an abstraction makes it easier for us to face these
things in the real world. A really good story gains depth and
meaning from real- world issues.

Resource 5: Storytellers

Gamers aren't the only storytellers. The art of telling stories
is at least as old as human civilization. That means there's
already a long tradition of storytelling from which you can
learn. We've said it before: learning about myth and legend
can add more to your game than any set of rules.

There are a number of organizations that are struggling to
preserve the art of telling stories. (The International Order of
E.A.R.S. and the National Association for the Promotion and
Preservation of Storytelling are two major groups.) People
who promote Storytelling advocate something that gamers
believe: The power of a storyteller to make a story come alive
can be just as compelling, if not more so, than any current
story-incarnation from a mass medium. All the bells and
whistles you add can augment your experience, but the heart
of the game is your ability to tell a story.

(For more information about storytelling organizations,
write toE.A.R.S., 12019 Donohue Ave., Louisville, KY 40243
or to N.A-P.P.S., P.O. Box 309, Jonesborough, TN 37659.)

Chapter Six: The Ways

| acca ae a aes /

Feeding

So why go toall the work of extra preparation? What are we
really trying to accomplish? What, exactly, is a good game?

The answer is found through experience. First off, any game
should be fun. Yes, it is just a game. However, as you learn to
run the game, developing your Storytelling is like developing
any other artistic skill. Any experienced Storyteller can recall
a session where everything was perfected. Part of the rush of
beinga Storyteller is your presence at the moment whenastory
is really alive. In defiance of reality, the story — not the game,
but the story — draws in everyone so completely that the
normal world is set aside for a few moments. Those moments
aren't simple escapism. They're cathartic. They're sheer bliss.
Areally good game demonstrates the perfection ofan art form,
and it makes all the hard work worthwhile. Any really good
Storyteller hungers for those moments.

Finding resources to draw upon and learning as part of your
preparation helps you find those moments. Stalking that goal
is an emotional process, but the thrill is well worth the hunt.

You've picked up the scent by now. Your claws are sharp-
ened. Your prey is moving. Go out there and catch it.

* Break the Bonds (Level Six Philodox and Galliard) —
This Gift allows a Garou to break any bonds holding her,
whether mental or physical. This includes all manner of mind
control, whether by a mage Sphere or vampiric Blood Bond.
The Garou can use this Gift to break the bond even though her
master may demand her not to. However, she may not seek out
aspirit to teach this Gift if she is commanded otherwise. Thus,
this Gift is most often awarded toa Garou asa return for service
toan Incama or equally powerful spirit who is well aware of the
Garou's unnatural servitude.

System: The Garou is effectively immune to supernatural
coercion and can easily break any physical bonds holding her
(she has the equivalent of Strength 15 for doing so). When
used to stop such coercion on others, the Garou must spend a
Gnosis point and roll Manipulation + Leadership against a
difficulty 6. Only one success is required. Also, the Garou can
break another's physical bindings as if she possessed Strength 15.

© Firebringer (Level Six Ragabash) — This amazing Gift
allows a Ragabash — the trickster of Garou society — to steal a
power or ability from another being and tum it into a Garou Gift,
teachable to others.

System: The Ragabash must first be the victim of the power he
wishes to steal (i.e., come under vampiric Domination, be affected
byamagerote, etc.). Ifhe survives, hecan take what he has learned
and teach it to others. However, he cannot use the new power
himself! In addition, anytime thereafter the original power is used
against him, it isat one difficulty less —he isconsidered vulnerable
to it.

Even Wyrm-tainted powers can be stolen (fomori powers,
Black Spiral Gifts, etc.); the Ragabash's sacrifice is enough to
cleanse them of their taint. In this way, the work of the Wyrm can
be directly turned against It.

The exact natureand system of the new Giftis entirely up tothe
Storyteller. It takes only about an hour for the Ragabash to teach
the Gift (as ifhe were a spirit). The Storyteller is free to use powers
given in any other Storytelling games.as the bases for new Gifts, as
long as the character is willing to risk all to steal that knowledge.
Ragabash willing to do something so selflessly for the community
are very rare; one that does should gain much Renown for her feat.

* Rebirthing (Level Six Theurge) — This most holy and
rare of Gaia's Gifts enables the Garou upon his death to be
instantly reincarnated in the body of a newborn cub living
within 2,000 miles of where the Garou died. The reincarna-
tion is most often of the same breed as the Garou had in his
former life, but it can be into another breed — even metis —
if the only newborn within range is not of the original breed.
Ifthere are nonewborn cubs in range within one turning of the
moon from the moment of death, then the Garou isnot reborn
and goes where all Garou go upon death.

System: The cub will nothave any of the memoriesand powers
of the original Garou until after the First Change, whereupon he
will grow into them. Sucha cub, when discovered, will be guarded
and protected fiercely by all Garou until he fully comes into his
former powers (in addition to any new powers gained). He must
regain his old rank in the same manner as all cubs (step by step),
and will only rememberhisold powersup through hiscurrentrank.
When he gains another Rank level, he will then rememberall the
powers of that level. However, he will not retain knowledge of this
Gift, and must lear itagain (and few spirits will be willing to teach
ita second time).

© Unstoppable Warrior (Level Six Ahroun) — A Garou
who uses this potent Gift can regenerate aggravated damage.
This works against all attacks except those from silver weap-
ons.

System: Each turn, roll Stamina + Primal-Urge against a
difficulty 8; if successful, then spend one point of Rage per
Health Level healed (much like a vampiric Blood Pool). The
Garou cannot attack in the same turn, unless he has the Level
Three Ahroun Gift: Combat Healing (see Werewolf Player
Guide, pg. 38)

New Rite

ite of the Sparrow (Level Four
Mystical)

The Rite of the Sparrow is performed when the Garou of a
sept or pack wish to provide aid or support to a Garou of their
number who is currently on a quest of some sort. The Garou
performing the rite can only see his target when the questing
Garou is traveling within one of the Umbras or is within sight
of water. In order to perform the rite, the ritemaster must dip
asmall bird's feet (usually a sparrow's) into a mixture of blood
and ashes. The ritemaster then dabs some of the same mixture
onto the Garou before she embarks on her quest. The ritemaster
then settles into a trance from which he can watch the
questor's progress. If the questing Garou is injured or is
otherwise in need of aid, the ritemaster may draw on his own
strength and the strength of any other Garou who have
participated in the ritual to aid their companion. This aid can
come in the form of healing, Gnosis or the transfer of an object
tothe questor. When such help is given, the ritemaster releases
the marked sparrow into the air. More than one sparrow may
be used during a given rite.

System: The rite requires the expenditure of one Gnosis
point to create the bond. An additional Gnosis point must be
spent whenever any help is granted the questor. Only one act
can be performed per sparrow freed. In addition, any healing
done does damage to the ritemaster or another designated
ritual participant. Thus, the damage is actually transferred, not
healed. The same is true for Gnosis. Additionally, the Garou
participating in the rite must have the object they wish to
transfer with them. Placing the sparrow on the object initiates
its transfer.

Fetish Artifacts

There are some truly ancient and magnificent objects of
power that cannot be considered normal fetishes, even level
five fetishes. These artifacts are jealously guarded by their
Garou holders and are solemnly handed down to each succes-
sive generation. Sometimes, even the existence of the artifact
is kept secret, as the item is hoarded away for the coming day
when it must be reactivated in the battle of the Apocalypse.

Below are just some of the hallowed items. Storytellers are
encouraged to create their own:

Earth Rattle

Level 8, Gnosis 7

This turtle shell rattle appears as nothing more than a
Native American artifact — but looks are deceiving. It is in
fact one of the few remaining items of power belonging to the
Croatan tribe. The mere shaking of the rattle (along with a
successful activation roll) is enough to cause massive earth-
quakesoverthe entire region, leveling buildingsand swallowing


whole streets. The number of successes gained on the activa-
tion roll determines the mileage of the quake (1-mile radius
per success). Obviously, the quake will cause damage inesti-
mable in simple dice roll terms. This rattle has not been shaken
since the death of the Croatan. It is said that the rattle
temporarily awakens the Turtle, totem of the Croatan, on
whose back the very Earth is said to rest.

Elder Stone

Level 7, Gnosis 8

This small rock is said to be a chip from the ancient stone
at Table Rock, the mythical site where the Garou came
together ages ago to form the Litany. It has powers to
enforce the rulings made there, and any bearing it will be
given voice in any moot. When activated, the bearer can
roll Charisma + Leadership (difficulty 6) to give any com-
mand and have it obeyed by any Garou who hears it — even
Black Spiral Dancers. Victims can make a resisted Will-
power roll at difficulty 6. The command cannot cause a
Garou to violate the Litany, however. The rock also gives
+2 to the bearer's soak Dice Pool — even against silver or
radiation.

Klaital's Tears (Calen)

Gnosis 8

These small, unidentifiable gems are said to be the
crystallized tears of Klaital, the first Stargazer, shed as he
wept with Harano on his journey to the end of the world.
They dried up and crystallized as he past them on his
triumphant return from despair. Each tear, when activated,
willonce again become salty water and exude such a feeling
of despair to all nearby that everyone must make a Will-
power roll, difficulty of the talen's Gnosis (8) or else fall
into Harano. These tears are extremely rare, and are be-
lieved to have all been collected by the Stargazers and
hidden away.

Seed of the World Tree (Talen)

Gnosis 8

This small seed (most often oak, but sometimes of another
species) isan actual seed of the World Tree, the first tree grown
by Gaia and the tree which sheltered the first Children of Gaia
cubs, given new life by the Mother. When carefully planted
and activated, the seed will grow (over time) to be an incred-
ibly strong and powerful tree, exuding an aura of peace and
courage. All who live near it will be affected by these emotions.
While still a sapling, the tree will need guarding, for minions
of the Wyrm will try to uproot it, but once it has grown to 10
years in age, it can defend itself, for it has become an animate
plant Kami (see Chapter Five). These seeds are so rare as to be
thought of as mere myths, but it is said that they can still be
sought in the far reaches of the Umbra, in areas where they
have blown but can grow no roots. All Child of Gaia believe
it their duty to return such seeds to be planted in the Earth.

— From The Cycle of the Enigma Running Pack

Fetishes represent the ultimate marriage of the spiritual
with the material. They are power made manifest in this world
through attunement and the indwelling of spirit.

Being especially sacred to the Garou, fetishes are usually
always handled with the utmost respect (even by Ragabash,
who forsome reason rarely break a fetish but occasionally have
problems with losing them). The Garou hold that creating a

fetish isan honorable, even glorious event. They also carefully
guard the knowledge of fetish creation from all but their most
wise Theurges, lest the knowledge slip into the foul hands of
the Black Spiral Dancers. Still, the Black Spiral Dancers have
created their own tainted, twisted version of the rite.

Asa Storyteller, you should make learning the Rite of the
Fetish a major milestone in a Garou's life, not unlike that of a
human's graduating from law school or medical school. Of
course, talens are another matter altogether; talens are easily
made and many Theurges are required to make them to show
their knowledge of spirits and how they relate to the material
world (using the Rite of Binding). Many tribes require those
who would be fetish makers to go through a rigid testing and
cleansing in preparation for their new responsibilities.

However, once the rite itself is learned, the crux of creating
a new fetish is simple: a spirit comes to inhabit an object,
through the Rite of the Fetish. The planning, preparation,
questing, negotiation and finishing of the fetish is the hard part
of the process—and each phase must be followed correctly lest
the ritualist creates a cursed fetish.

Fetish Creation Phases

Throughout this section optional systems are offered for
each phase. If you are not comfortable Storytelling every
ou may simply require the rolls to

nuance of this proces
ch phase between each game session.

be made, one for e
This will mean that you don't have to worry about bogging
down your main story line if all a character wants to do is
make a Harmony Flute or some other level one fetish in her
spare time, or if you're concerned about giving the charac-
ter too much attention in the story. Keep notes on how the
characters progress through the process and make sure you
give the proper modifiers for each roll

Planning

The ritualist must plan what she wants the fetish to do.
She goes to the elders she trusts and asks them how to go
about it: she consults spirits, her Totem, the members of her
Auspice and even on some occasions, ancient texts.

The Uktena will often borrow a fetish of the same
general kind and spend days and days meditating over it. A
Fianna artificer must sit through story after story from their
elders (often accompanied by providing round after round
of drinks). The Shadow Lords must always have full disclo-
sure about the nature of the fetish and will often have
someone else do the Planning and Preparation phases so
that the ritualist doesn't know exactly how to duplicate the
fetish.

Storytelling the Planning Phase

All in all, you should require that the character who is
making the fetish gain as much information as possible
about how to constructit. As well, this isa good time for you
to require the player to write down exactly what powers he
is trying to put into the fetish.

|


Sere re een core ere coe ar ener en rem marrrenamnrarenh

Examine the powers of the fetish. Are they very com-
plex? Fetishes don't tend to be incredibly complex; even
the Glass Walker fetishes are fairly straightforward. This is
because a fetish must be powered by a single spirit. Now, it's
possible to make a fetish and then turn around and add
another fetish attached to the first fetish. It is even possible
to make the two work together, but all of this must be
planned out in advance. You can't decide later to add
another fetish.

If the fetish is too complex or doesn't fit the Garou's
paradigm (the obvious examples are a Wendigo making a
techno-fetish, ora Glass Walker making a Wyld one), then
you may disallow it. You can warn the player either directly,
or through roleplaying of the disapprobation and advice of
the elders: they will be against the idea of the fetish and will
not help the Garou plan it. Of course, the Wyrm is always
willing to help a Garou in need; you may be able to corrupt
a Garou by offering him the wisdom he needs for that killer
fetish he's designing.

At this point, decide what level the fetish is going to be;
this helps remind the player of the power of the fetish and
reminds you of how difficult it will be to make the item. A
level one fetish is almost everyday jewelry while a level five
fetish is a very powerful item indeed. You can use the level
of fetishes found in Werewolf supplements as a guide to
what level the new fetish should be.

Systems (Optional)

The ritualist rolls Manipulation + Rituals against the
Willpower of the highest rank elder that the character
speaks to, or you may simply set the difficulty at 7. A botch
indicates wrong information is given out and all subsequent
rolls are at + 2 difficulty at best, and at worst (particularly
in the case of making a level five fetish), the project is
ruined from the start. A failure on the roll indicates that the
character is rebuffed or set back and must repeat the
Planning phase. For each success, decrease the difficulty of
the Preparation roll (next phase).

Preparation

The preparation phase involves gathering all the mun-
dane materials for the fetish. It is alsoa time for purification,
meditation and quiet reflection. A Garou must not be out
slaying the Wyrm unless they can somehow maintain this
contemplative state while doing so. (Don't laugh: this is
not a problem for many Stargazers!)

The Uktena believe that, if a fetish is meant to be, the
materials will come to them — either by coincidence or
spiritual provenance. Many Uktena have awoken by dawn's
light and discovered the right feather or proper stone laying
next to their heads. The Children of Gaia believe that a
fetish must be carried for a year and a day to prepare it, and
many Children wear bags with their fetishes-to-be close to
their hearts. The Get of Fenris believe that a fetish cannot
be considered prepared unless it is doused in a bowl of the

Chapter Six: The Ways

LE TE

ritualist's blood. The Bone Gnawers consider it a great
honor to be allowed to dig in their elder's Stuffpile to look
for fetish materials.

Storytelling the Preparation Phase

This is another place where you, the Storyteller, can turn
the making of the fetish into a story. Requiring special
materials or strange purification or spiritual preparations
can either last for a scene or take up an entire story. Make
sure that these preparations equal the complexity and
power of the fetish.

Systems (Optional)

The ritualist rolls Intelligence + Streetwise, Survival,
Occult, or Enigmas depending on the nature of the fetish as
determined by the Storyteller. The difficulty is the poten-
tial level of the fetish plus three (level + 3): a level five
fetish would be difficulty 8. A botch on the roll means the
entirely wrong materials are gathered or that the ritualist
has become tainted in some way. Unless this is detected the
project could go on without the character realizing it; if it
is noticed, then the character must start over at the begin-
ning. If the roll fails, the character is frustrated at a lack of
materials or is unable to get in the proper frame of mind to
cleanse herself spiritually; she must repeat this phase. Each
success subtracts from the difficulty of the Questing phase
roll.

Questing

After planning and preparing, the ritualist must now set
out on a quest to locate the proper spirit. The Garou often
travels into the Umbra hunting just the right spirit on
advice from her elders or through direction given by vision
quests, Gifts or other sources of wisdom. The more powerful
Theurges decide instead to attempt to summon the proper
spirit to them; their preparation includes discovering what
sort of lure to use on summoning the spirit. Whatever the
case, the Garou must locate the spirit necessary to the
empowerment of the fetish she is seeking.

The Uktena Theurges make it a practice to bind spirits
they find interesting; they use these bound spirits as trading
tokens between each other, and many Uktena come by the
proper spirit in this fashion. The Glass Walkers have been
known to jealously guard those techno-spirits who can
make technology do amazing things, although they will
often sell or barter a bound techno-spirit for high dollar or
valuable boons. The Black Furies feel that binding spirits
for the purpose of later turning them into fetishes is a
distasteful practice: they always hunt for their spirits, even
for the ones that go into their talens. Of course, the Furies
also know the dangers of fetish creation; they have seen too
many botched and cursed fetishes pass through their claws
not to be wise to their ways.


|

Storytelling the Questing Phase

As a Storyteller, use common sense here. If the first two
steps were done exceedingly well (and you gotalotof story play
from it) you may wish to go easy on the ritualist with this step.
After all, if you drag this out much longer your Garou may
despair of ever accomplishing it. You must give the player
encouragementalong the way. However, if it isa very powerful
fetish she is seeking, don't be afraid to make her go far and wide
searching out the proper spirit. She may have to perform a
service foran Incarna or fora Totem in order to meet the spirit.

As well, the spirit must be of an affinity equal to the task of
the fetish: if the spirit is a spirit of healing, it can't reasonably
be used in a war fetish unless you can somehow tur it around
and convince to hurt instead of heal. A spirit of fire can't make
a fetish which hides you — the spirit burns too bright. The
Storyteller can decide that a unique spirit must be located —
aCity Father Jaggling or some kind of Net-Spider for example,
in which case no amount of summoning will work — you can't
summon what you don't know youshould have. Of course, this
information should have come out in the Planning phase.

Systems (Optional)

The player decides whether she wishes to hunt for the spirit
or summon it. If she wishes to hunt for it, she rolls Perception
+ Enigmas versus the level of the fetish plus three (level + 3).
A botch means she attracts a Wyrm or Weaver spirit that
appears to be the same kind of spirit she's looking for. A failure
means that she fails to locate the proper spirit and must try
again (next game session). Success adds no bonus, but if a
number of successes equaling the power level of the fetish are
received then the character discovers a very appropriate
candidate who is already predisposed towards the character.
The spirit begins at Curious on the Acceptance track when
negotiation begins.

If the player is summoning a spirit, use the systems for the
Rite of Summoning, given in the Werewolf rulebook. This
isn't always preferable, as many spirits are annoyed at being
summoned for this purpose.

Below is a chart which describes how powerful the spirit
must be to equal the power level of the fetish:

Fetish Level Spirit Type

Levell-3  Gaffling

Level 4 Jaggling

Level 5 Totem Avatar (such as a Pack Totem) or

Garou spirit

Negotiation

After finding the proper spirit, one must now get it to agree
to enter the fetish. This is quite difficult. What if someone
came to you and asked you to be locked up in a tiny room for
the rest of your existence, doing only one thing over and over
at the service of anyone who entered the room? Naturally, it's
not something that spirits want to do ona lark. Still, the spirits
of Gaia believe that the Garou are the holy warriors of Gaia

126 Werewolf Storytellers Handbook

a ee a nee (/

and many of them wish to serve the Garou in whatever fashion
they can. Also, it's not known for sure what sort of life they
have while dwelling within a fetish. Some Theurges believe
they have a mystic connection to a higher, more powerful
spirit (or to Gaia), and when bound in a fetish can experience
the physical world in way not normally possible for them.
The Fianna have made pacts with spirits in the past
requiring them to be released after 100 years of servitude. This
is not always enforced and many Fianna fetishes occasionally
turn nasty when their terms of service run out and they are not
released. The Bone Gnawers will often try touse guilt tocoerce
a spirit into serving them, or suitably butter the spirit up by
proclaiming its great power: "Oh, great spirit! [ couldn't help
but notice how strong and powerful you were! Oh, my! How
your flame burns hot! Couldn't you see your way clear to
sharing your fire with this Bic lighter fora few hundred years?"

Storytelling the Negotiation Phase

You may simulate all the rolls given below by properly
Storytelling the negotiation process. Keep in mind that spirits

will only very rarely wish to enter into a fetish. If the spirit is
obviously willing, it still must overcome fear of the Garou
before it can give itself to the fetish. The only exception to this
tule is to the use of Garou spirits in fetishes, such as in the
example from the Cycle of the Enigmas Running Pack given at
the beginning of this section. Garou spirits enter a fetish with
no negotiation required, if their last wish is to do so (and only
a dying wish will allow this).

A Garou's spirit entering a fetish is a rare and wonderful
event, one that should be the climax of an entire chronicle.
Just because a character may be dying does not guarantee she
has the will or the spiritual understanding to properly enter a
prepared fetish and empower it, and the Rite of the Fetish must
be performed by someone else before the Garou is dead. Not
all such fetishes become self-aware things, and some of these
Garou-spirit fetishes are easily tainted by the Wyrm. The
practice of placing a Garou's spirit within a fetish is a blasphe-
mous one to the Silver Fangs, who feel that the spirit should
be free to return to Gaia again — although the number of
Silver Fang heroes wielding ancestral spirit Grand Klaives is a
silent testament to how they truly feel.

Systems (Optional)

In order to get a spirit to enter a fetish willingly, the Garou
must convince it to do so. This is done by slowly wearing away
at the spirit's resolve, calling its attention to its duty to Gaia,
offering it bribes, taking on Geasa and threatening it.

When a Garou suggests that a spirit enter a fetish, the spirit
willusually be very skeptical of the Garou's intent. It's reaction
will change as the Garou works on it. The accompanying
sidebar shows the stages of acceptance that the spirit usually
goes through. Encountered spirits vary widely as to their initial
stage, but most are either Wary or Neutral. The ritualist's first
actions will determine whether the spirit initially goes up or
down on the scale.


Serre ew a: aerenine ns area ore ars aaron recnunrurmam meer

If the spirit has been summoned with the Rite of Summon-
ing, the number of successes the ritualist gets determines the
stage of the spirit when itarrives (see also Rite of Summing, pp.
145-146 in the Werewolf Second Edition rulebook).

Once the spirit reaches Committed, it is ready to enter the
fetish. The Garou can move the spirit down the track to
Committed in the following ways:

Call to Duty: The Garou may use the Gift Call to Duty as
a means of advancing the spirit down one stage.

Oratory: The Garou may try to orate, cajole or otherwise
talk the spirit into serving her or Gaia by entering the fetish.
The Garou rolls Charisma + Leadership (optionally Expres-
sion); the difficulty is the spirit's Willpower. If successful, the
spirit moves one stage down the track for each success. A
failure means that other means of negotiation must be used. A
botch means the spirit goes immediately to Angry/Upset (or
to attacking if the spirit is already angry or upset); spirits don't
necessarily like to be reminded of their place in Gaia's Plan.

Offering Bribes: The Garou may offer the spirit bribes of
various kinds by feeding it Gnosis, showing it the beautiful
fetish she has for it, or in some other means of spiritual
currency. The roll for this is Manipulation + Streetwise; the
difficulty is 9 minus the level of the fetish (9 - level). Many
spirits are honored to be part of a powerful, level five fetish,
although few are interested in being stuck in a level one fetish
for ages. The Garou must actually produce the bribe in order
for this to work, but for every success on the roll, the spirit is
advanced up one stage toward Commitment.

Geasa: Some Garou offer to take on Geasa if the spirit will
do as she asks. This means that the Garou will swear to do or
not to do something, usually in affinity with the spirit in
question. For example, a Garou negotiating with a tree spirit
might take on a Geasa that she will never again chop down a
tree. Sometimes Wyld spirits will demand silly or demeaning
Geasa, such as forcing a Garou to wear a certain shade of green
all the time or making the Garou dance whenever a certain
word is mentioned. Geasa are usually considered to either be
Minor Geasa or Major Geasa, depending on their nature and

# of successes Stage Effects

Fetish Making: Stages of Spirit Acceptance

The spirit is angry, upset or insulted that you asked. One more mistake in negotiations and it may
attack! Essentially, any step down in the stages from this point means that the spirit either flees
or attacks, depending on the situation and type of spirit.

duration. Some Geasa cause an automatic loss in either Honor
or Glory or even Wisdom, when they are initially accepted,
but later begin toadd Wisdom and Honor to the Garouas long
as they are consistently adhered to. The elders believe that you
should honor any pacts you make with spirits.

There is no roll for Geasa. Fora Major Geasa, the Garoucan
move the spirit down three stages on the Acceptance Track.
For a Minor one, the Garou can move the spirit down one
stage. Note that a Garou who violates the Geasa will find that
the fetish suddenly becomes cursed, as the spirit within takes
its vengeance.

Geasa are useful for getting spirits to do all kinds of things;
spirits like having an affect on the Realm in some small way,
and love commanding Garou (for a change!).

Some examples of Minor Geasa are: never entering a door
of a particular color, always wearing a specific token (such as
a hat or button), never eating a particular kind of meat, never
speaking the spirit's name aloud, always wearing a particular
color.

Some examples of Major Geasa are: performing a sacrifice,
getting tattoo or brand, swearing an oath, agreeing to a quest
or sacred journey, agreeing to adopt a new name (thereby
giving up your old name), freeing another captive spirit.

The Geasa requested by the spirit will often be something
in line with the spirit's affinity and will be something which is
easily verifiable and (except in the case of certain enigma-
spirits) easy to understand.

This often explains why so many Theurges adopt strange
superstitions and customs — although some Theurges use the
social excuse of Geasa to get out of certain mundane duties or
as a means of avoiding specific foods or places.

Threats: Ultimately, however, Garou are the chosen War-
riors of Gaia, and they have the right to demand assistance
from Her spirits. The ritualist may threaten the spirit, rolling
Charisma or Manipulation + Intimidation against the spirit's
Willpower. If the roll is a botch, the spirit immediately flies
into a rage and either attacks or flees. If the roll fails, the spirit

The spirit doesn't appear to be listening to the Garou's pleas, yet it is still present and doesn't

appear to be angry.

still not go for it. This is when many Garou take on Geasa to convince it further (see Geasa, below).

laughsand moves one up in acceptance stages, and the ritualist
must roll against a frenzy. If the roll succeeds, the spirit moves
down one stage for every success — but threat cannot move
a spirit to Committed without the risk of a cursed fetish. A
spirit can decide to curse a fetish at any point it feels
threatened. It is said that the Uktena have devised a Gift
which allows them to threaten spirits into entering fetishes
without fear of curses, although this Gift, if known, is not
widely taught.

Executing the Rite

After all this, you should be ready to finish the fetish.
The character performs the Rite of the Fetish using all of
herpreparation, planning, and the spirit involved. You may
wish to give the fetish to the character if she has been
through all the steps and done exceedingly well at each one.
Otherwise, the player must still make a roll.

A Few Final Thoughts

Fetishes are very rare and valuable things: they should
not be easily found. If you play your cards right, you can
make the creation of a fetish into something that is beau-
tiful and epic in scope. Although this system has been
provided to you, please don't feel as though you have to
abide by it one-hundred percent. It is meant to be a loose
framework to guide your thinking about how you can bring
fetish creation into your chronicle in a dynamic and story-
fruitful fashion. Don't forget to give the proper amount of
Renown to anyone who completes the process; they've
certainly earned it.

Simple Lessons
By William Spencer-Hale

With the heart and mind united in a single, perfect sphere
— Rush, "Hemispheres"

It seems like only yesterday that my best friend's father
purchased Dungeons and Dyafmg® as a means of keeping us
off the streets. AppreherGivély, | glanced through the book
so as to.gain enoughginfdtmatfong® play and,this task
completed, praGgeded toa F a

Although w:
game, ie, ie fe

experieng&a: . ipething won-
derfulblasgomted in ght Worlds which never
knew @xistedv fone toleXploreind gain
wisdom from. Pwill néver Peggét that night, it'will remain
in my memory as a sort of birthing, the time when I cast
aside my old self to make way for the new. That night I
learned of the power that the imagination held and I have
wielded it fiercely and proudly ever since. It remains one of
my fondest memories.

After I had played for many years, things became com-

monplace, almost boring. The monsters were the same with


|

each encounter, the villains were always dry and lacked
depth and true character. Even those whom I played with
became stagnant in their characters. Each one seeming no
more than a mirror image of the last intrepid dragon slayer.
Everything that I had fallen in love with had become dull
and lifeless. Before long, I found myself becoming uninter-
ested in the hobby I once found so much joy in and,
accordingly, I lost the desire to play.

It wasn't until some years later when my brother decided
he would begin a tragic campaign set in a world of his own
creation that I begrudgingly decided to play again. We had
asmall group, only four, and we set about the task of rolling
up new characters for this incredible adventure that my
brother had spent so much time boasting about. I thought
his game would be nothing but a means to waste a few hours
of time and perhaps relive a few old memories. I expected
nothing more. How wrong I was.

With the greatest of ease, he reopened the door to my
imagination, allowing me to see the world as I once had. He
made me once again realize just how much | enjoyed
roleplaying and in so doing, revived in me the desire to play
as oftenas I once had. The most amazing part was the simple
way in which he did this. What he added to the game was
something that should have been there all along, but few
had thought to add. Human emotion.

His non-player characters were more than statistics
scratched on a piece of paper. They had depth and feeling,
desires and goals. They seemed real, as if you could almost
reach out and touch them. This in turn made his players,
myself included, more empathic to the atmosphere of the
game, making us all more a part of what was going on. At
times, almost making us believe that we were really there.
The characters in that game were Dyr, Grom, Ech'myrr and
Stormwolf, and they not only saved the world but saved my
faith in roleplaying as well. I've played many games since
then, but few have been a better vehicle for this type of
three-dimensional roleplaying than Werewolf: The Apoca-
lypse.

The lessons learned from that game made me understand
what I had been missing. There is more to roleplaying than
slaying the dragon, saving the princess and stealing the
treasure. As with all things, the human side to this hobby
is often overlooked. Give the players something to strive for

Chapter Six: The Ways

besides the goal of the adventure. Present them with non-
player characters that have all the depth and ambition
found in real life. After all, isn't roleplaying a shadow of our
own reality?

When you present players with a three-dimensional
world they will respond by playing three-dimensional char-
acters. This will make the game more enjoyable for all
involved and will also make the game much easier to run
due to the interaction level. Inspire your players with more
than treasure and glory or even survival. Inundate them
with personas which will make them think and feel. Give
them allies that they will feel loyal to, enemies that they
will not only hate but will respect as well and maybe even
sympathize with. Give them the opportunity to realize that
their enemy is more than a faceless horror who serves only
to thwart their plans. Let them understand their foes and,
in so doing, understand more of themselves and their
characters' goals. Evil is not always black and white.

There is also another emotion which will spur your
players to become more deeply involved in the game. Love.
There is no emotion more inspiring than this. Give charac-
ters family and comrades they can cling tightly to. Afterall,
in Werewolf, your Kinfolk are everything. Supply the
characters with allies who will help them to make their
characters more than numbers and dice rolls. Also, present
them with a love interest. Someone who is interested in
their success and failure, someone who will provide them
with the ability to see beyond their own character's desires
and thus, will help to add that extra dimension to their
characters and the game. This will make the game more
enjoyable and memorable for all involved.

In short, make the game world as multifaceted as the real
world. Give the character every opportunity to experience
life full circle, to rise above the constraints of the character
sheet and live and breath in the imagination of the player.
This will make the game quite memorable and just might
teach the players a few lessons about themselves as well.
Roleplaying, like life, requires more than a goal. The path
that is followed to achieve an end requires that we celebrate
each moment as it comes and, in doing so, learn of the
wonders that surround us. This is a lesson for which I will
be forever grateful.

Tribal Weaknesses
(Optional)

An optional rule was introduced in the first of the
Werewolf Tribebooks: tribal weaknesses. These are quirks
each member of a particular tribe possesses, usually due to
the social or even genetic nature of a tribe. Weaknesses
should not always be enforced. There are some situations
where a Bone Gnawer may not suffer a higher difficulty on
Social rolls. These situations may be rare, but they can
occur. For instance, Black Furies suffer from an inborn
anger against men, but a Black Fury may not feel anger
towards a man with whom she has a trusting relationship.

It is up to the Storyteller to enforce these rules when an
appropriate situation occurs in the game. A player may be

unwilling to remind a Storyteller that her Uktena's curios-
ity will get her into trouble. Here is a list of all the tribal

weaknesses and the reasons for them.

Black Furies

Anger: -1 difficulty for frenzies against men

The Black Furies seethe with an age-old anger against
Man. For too long, Woman has borne the brunt of his
desires and whims. No longer... the Black Furies are fight-

ing back.

Appendix

OLE A

Bone Gnawers

Social Outcasts: +1 difficulty on all Social rolls involv-
ing other tribes

The Bone Gnawers are the scapegoats of Garou society
Alternatively scorned and ridiculed, they survive when
even their own kind mocks them.

Children of Gaia

Weak Veil: Witnesses at +5 on Delirium Chart

The Children of Gaia do not cause as severe a Delirium
reaction in humans who see them in Crinos form. Give all
witnesses a +5 on the Delirium Chart (the worst reaction is
"Conciliatory").

with all these weaknesses, however, the Storyteller

can decide that there are some situations where they are not
effective. Thus, a Child of Gaia should never depend on
this, since she could, in certain extreme situations, still
send humans into paroxysms of fear.

Fianna

Low Self-Control: +1 difficulty for Willpower rolls

The Fianna often find it hard to rule their own passions.
They ride the emotional waves of anger, giddy joy and
melancholia. Most find it hard to govern themselves enough
to shake these moods off at a whim.

Get of Fenris

Intolerance

Each Get of Fenris has something she hates, one thing she
will not tolerate. In situations where this object of contempt
is near, she will be unable to endure its presence and will do
everything in her power to rid herself of the annoyance. If this
object of intolerance is a fellow Garou, then woe be it unto
him...

The player may either define a specific Intolerance for her
character (with the Storyteller's approval) or choose from the
list below. Wyrm creatures may not be chosen — all Get are
expected to hate such monstrosities as a matter of course.

* Cowardice — You hate cowardice in all its forms,
whether it is fear of the battlefield or fear to stand up to others
in social situations. You openly scorn those you deem cow-
ardly. If you ever go into a fox frenzy, you will turn your hate
inward, and must do everything possible to make up for your
act of cowardice, becoming quite reckless in the process.

© Compromise — You hate to compromise; it is a tactic for
those who are not strong enough to get their way. You scorn
those who practice such tactics regularly (such as the Glass
Walkers and the Children of Gaia) and you must never
compromise in a situation. Your way must be enforced. If a
leader forces you to compromise, that is acceptable, but you
will begin to doubt that leader's ability to rule.

Lower Animals — You have only contempt for creatures
lower than you on the food chain. Such creatures are meant to
bekicked around by yourkind. This includes humansand even
wolves. While you believe it is your duty to defend them to a
degree (such is Gaia's will), you will not accept condescension
or insubordination from them. A grave insult froma human is
enough to drive you toward frenzy.

‘e when

* Peaceniks — You despise those who speak of pea
war is the proper response. War tempers the warrior and
prepares him to fight against the Wyrm as the Apocalypse
approaches. Yes, there are times for peace, but when attacked,
you must strike back. Never turn the other cheek.

¢ Weakness— You hate weakness in others, whether that's
a lack of physical strength or a lack of backbone. You will
openly scorn those youdeem weak and will never tolerate such
qualities in yourself. You can only be merciful when there is a
risk involved, achance that it could lead to danger; otherwise,
mercy is the hallmark of those too weak to punish criminals
(whether they are servants of the Wyrm or Garou).

© Weaver Stuff — You hate all things of the Weaver,
especially technology. You may even feel that Klaives bear too
much of her taint; only claws and fangs would then be pure
enough. You especially despise the Glass Walkers and all
Urrah. You must never willingly use technology when more
traditional means will do.

Glass Walkers

Weaver Affinity: Cannot regain Gnosis in wilderness

The Glass Walkers are tied closely with their cities, their
city spirits and the spiritual life unique to the city, with its

132 Werewolf Storytellers Handbook

[POPE Ps ET DT imines -/ -

mishmash of tyrannical Weaver and tempered Wyld. Because
of this, they lack an inherent connection with the Wyld and
may not regain Gnosis points when in the wilderness. The
exception to this is when they are at a caern; they may regain
Gnosis as they normally do at these sacred sites.

Red Talons

Wyld Affinity: Cannot regain Gnosis in cities

The Red Talons are tied closely to the wilderness, drawing
on the ebb and flow of its natural, spiritual life. Because of this,
they lack an inherent connection with the Weaver and may
not regain Gnosis within a city. The exception to this is when
they are at a caern; they may regain Gnosis as they normally
do at these sacred sites. The Storyteller may allow them to
regain a few points in the suburbs, if he deems that the ‘burbs
are rural enough.

Shadow Lords

Failure's Dagger: -1 Renown for failure

Shadow Lords prize winning above all else, and they scorn
losers. Whenever a Shadow Lord fails to carry out a task that
would normally gain him Glory, Honor or Wisdom, he will
lose one point of temporary Renown in that category. (If he
would have gained Renown in more than one category,
subtract only from the category that would have rewarded the
most.) This is in addition to any Renown normally lost (see the
Renown Awards Chart, pp. 190-193).

This does not affect the normal Renown process in any
other way; if the Shadow Lord succeeds in the action, then he
gains the normal amount of Renown.

Silent Striders

Haunted

The Silent Striders bear a connection with their Egyptian
past, which is both deeper and more mysterious than the other
tribes. Due to an ancient curse laid upon this tribe, they must
forever wander far from their ancient homeland and be
haunted by the dead.

Whenever a Silent Strider enters or exits the Umbra, a
botch means she is "caught." During this time, a wraith will be
attracted to her. This occurs any time she gets "caught", even
if the Strider was only following another's lead through the
Gauntlet. When the Strider escapes from being "caught"
between the two worlds, the wraith will follow her. Only the
Strider will see and hear the wraith. This ghost isnot necessar-
ily good or evil, but he will harass the Silent Strider, either
requesting some service ("Save my family!") or demanding
some penance ("Your kind killed me.. give mea boon or | shall
forever haunt you.").

The only way a Strider can rid herself of this ghost is to fulfill
the request of the spirit or leave the area. The spirit will not be
able to follow the Strider outside ofa certain range. (This area
is determined by the Storyteller, and may neverbe greater than
a state or county.) After one moon (one lunar month), the
Strider may return without fear of attracting the ghost again.

Silver Fangs

Derangement

The blood of the Silver Fangs is not as strong as it used to
be, largely due to years of inbreeding with limited flocks of
Kinfolk. Each Silver Fang has a Derangement, regardless of the
degree of Pure Breed she possesses. This may be chosen by the
player (with the Storyteller's approval) or taken from the list
below.

¢ Amnesia — In a highly stressful and traumatic situation,
you forget who you are.

© Intellectualization — You compulsively analyze every-
thing and block out as many emotions as possible. However,
when your fragile world of facts and figures is shattered by the
supernatural, you usually freak out.

* Manic-Depression — You suffer from wild mood swings
ranging from wild bliss to complete despair. You begin each
story in one phase or the other and can switch back and forth
for any number of reasons.

© Multiple Personalities — There are a number of different
personalities housed within your head. You may switch your
name, Nature and Demeanor during times of great stress.

© Obsession — You tend to latch on to someone or
something and make him or it the focal point of your life.

Paranoia — You see the Wyrm's influence in everything.
Don't the others see it too? Perhaps they've been corrupted as
well.

© Perfection — You work hard to keep everything in your
life going perfectly at all times. You use all of your energy to
prevent things from going wrong and have been known to
frenzy when things don't go in your favor.

© Power Madness — You are obsessed with control and
dominance over others.

© Regression — You tend to revert to childlike behavior
during times of extreme stress.

© Vengeful — When you have been wronged, you become
obsessed with getting even and bent on making those who
crossed you pay.
